Reciting a Verse of Prostration Quietly to an Unprepared Person
Ruling on reciting a verse of prostration quietly before one not prepared for it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on reciting a verse of prostration quietly before an unprepared person and explain the wisdom behind it.

Core Idea
Recite quietly to avoid compelling an unprepared listener to prostrate.

This lesson addresses a considerate practice in reciting the Quran. When reciting a verse that requires prostration, if the listener is not prepared (e.g., not in wudu or mentally ready), it is recommended to recite it quietly. This spares the listener from an immediate obligation that may be difficult. The ruling derives from the broader Hanafi principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting a verse of prostration. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (recommended) to do so quietly before an unprepared person.
2
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The wisdom is to avoid compelling the listener to prostrate, which would be a burden if they are not prepared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۱) وندب اخفاءها من غير متأهب لها )
ترجمه : (۷۷۱) اور جو سجدہ کے لئے تیار نہ ہو اس کے سامنے آیت سجدہ آہستہ پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔ تشریح : جو سجدہ کرنے کے لئے ذہنی طور پر تیار نہ ہو اس کے سامنے آیت سجدہ آہستہ پڑھنا مستحب ہے تا کہ اس کو سجدہ کے لئے مجبور نہ کیا جائے۔
(771) And it is recommended to conceal (recite quietly) it from one who is not prepared for it. Translation (771): And reciting a verse of prostration quietly before one who is not prepared for it is recommended. Explanation: Reciting a verse of prostration quietly before one who is not mentally prepared for prostration is recommended so that he is not compelled to prostrate.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This is a ruling about the etiquette of reciting a verse of prostration in the presence of others. If a person is not prepared to perform the prostration (e.g., not in a state of wudu, or busy, or not expecting it), it is mustahabb to recite the verse quietly or softly so that the listener is not forced to prostrate (since listening to the verse makes prostration wajib upon the listener as well). This shows consideration for others' circumstances.

Key Terms
اخفاء (ikḥfā'): Concealing or reciting quietly, so that the person not prepared is not compelled to prostrate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it recommended to recite a verse of prostration quietly before someone not prepared for it?
A) To avoid disturbing others
B) So that the listener is not compelled to prostrate
C) Because loud recitation is makruh
D) To show humility

Key Takeaway
Reciting a verse of prostration quietly before an unprepared person is recommended to avoid compelling them to prostrate, reflecting the Hanafi principle of removing hardship.

Recommendation of Standing Before Prostrating for Tilawa
Ruling: standing then prostrating is recommended.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on standing before sujud al-tilawa and distinguish between the recommended (mustahabb) and obligatory elements.

Core Idea
Standing before sujud al-tilawa is recommended but not obligatory; the prostration is valid whether from sitting or standing.

This lesson covers the etiquettes of sujud al-tilawa. While the prostration itself is wajib when reciting a verse of sajdah, the manner of performing it includes sunan. Many assume that standing is required, but the Hanafi school teaches that it is merely recommended. Let's examine the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is sujud al-tilawa (prostration of recitation). It is an ibadah with specific rules.
Sujud al-tilawa is distinct from the prostration in salah.
2
State the hukm level for the manner
The text uses 'nudiba' indicating recommendation. Standing before prostration is mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
The hukm applies to the standing, not the prostration itself.
3
Note the alternative and its validity
Prostrating while sitting is permissible. The prostration is valid whether one stands or sits.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf against those who consider standing obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ندب القيام ثم السجود لها (۷۷۳[الف])
ترجمه : (۷۷۲) اور مستحب ہے کہ کھڑا ہو پھر اس کے لئے سجدہ کرے۔ تشریح : یہاں سے سجدہ تلاوت کرنے کے چند آداب کا ذکر ہے۔ بیٹھے بیٹھے بھی سجدہ کر سکتا ہے لیکن مستحب یہ ہے کہ کھڑا ہو اور پھر سجدہ میں جائے۔
And it is recommended to stand then prostrate for it (773[a]). Translation (772): And it is recommended that one stand then prostrate for it. Explanation: From here begins the mention of several etiquettes of performing the prostration of recitation. One can also prostrate while sitting, but it is recommended to stand and then go into prostration.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage introduces the etiquettes (ādāb) of sujūd al-tilāwa. The ruling is that while sitting and prostrating is permissible (the prostration is valid even if performed while seated), it is mustahabb (recommended) to stand up first and then go into prostration. This is in contrast to the prostration in prayer which is done from the standing position anyway.

Key Terms
قيام (qiyām): Standing up before performing prostration of recitation, as a recommended act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing sujud al-tilawa while sitting?
A) It is invalid
B) It is makruh
C) It is permissible but standing is better
D) It is wajib to stand

Key Takeaway
Standing before sujud al-tilawa is a recommended sunnah; the prostration is valid from sitting as well.

Etiquettes of Sujūd al-Tilāwa in a Group
Rulings on listener not raising head, reciter not stepping forward, and no lining up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two etiquettes for listeners and reciter during sujūd al-tilāwa and explain why they differ from congregational prayer.

Core Idea
In sujūd al-tilāwa, listeners follow the reciter's lead but need not line up or have the reciter step forward.

This lesson covers the proper conduct for a group when a verse of prostration is recited. Unlike congregational prayer, sujūd al-tilāwa has simpler etiquettes: the listener waits for the reciter to raise his head, but no rows are required, and the reciter does not move to the front. These rules highlight that sujūd al-tilāwa is a distinct act of worship, not a mini-salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and setting
Recognize that the ruling concerns sujūd al-tilāwa performed by a group after a reciter recites a verse of prostration.
The reciter becomes like an imam only in the sequence of raising the head.
2
State the first etiquette
The listener must not raise his head before the reciter does; he waits for the reciter's lead.
This shows the reciter's precedence in the prostration.
3
State the second etiquette
The reciter is not commanded to step forward, and the listeners are not commanded to form rows; they prostrate wherever they are.
Contrast with congregational prayer where an imam stands in front and rows are formed.
4
Understand the rationale
Sujūd al-tilāwa is a separate act; the reciter is like an imam only in not being preceded in raising the head. No other prayer formalities apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يرفع السامع رأسه منها قبل تاليها ولا يؤمر التالى بالتقدم ولا السامعون بالاصطفاف فيسجدون كيف كانوا. (۷۷۳ [ب] وشرط لصحتها شرائط الصلوة الا التحريمة
ترجمه : (۷۷۳[الف]) سننے والا پڑھنے والے سے پہلے اپنا سرنہ اٹھائے ، اور نہ پڑھنے والے کو آگے بڑھنے کا حکم دیا جائے ، اور نہ سننے والےکوصف بندی کا حکم دیا جائے ، اس لئے وہ جیسا چاہیں سجدہ کریں۔ تشریح : ایک آدمی نے آیت سجدہ پڑھی اور مثلا دس آدمیوں نے اس کو سنا، اور پڑھنے والے نے اور سننے والے نے سجدہ کیا تو ایسا سمجھو کہ پڑھنے والا امام بن گیا اس لئے سننے والا پڑھنے والے سے پہلے سر نہ اٹھائے ، بلکہ پڑھنے والے کے سراٹھانے کا انتظار کرے۔ دوسرا ادب یہ ہے کہ ان دس آدمیوں کو صف بنانے کا حکم نہ دیا جائے اور نہ پڑھنے والے کو امام کی طرح آگے بڑھنے کا حکم دیا جائے ، بلکہ جو جہاں ہو وہیں سے سجدہ کر لیں ۔ یا پھر جیسا چاہیں کرلیں۔
And the listener should not raise his head from it before the reciter, and the reciter is not commanded to step forward, and the listeners are not commanded to line up; rather they prostrate as they are. Translation (773[a]): The listener should not raise his head before the reciter, and the reciter is not commanded to step forward, and the listeners are not commanded to line up, so they prostrate as they wish. Explanation: A man recited a verse of prostration and ten men heard him, and the reciter and listeners prostrated. Then one should consider that the reciter becomes like an imam, so the listener should not raise his head before the reciter, but wait for the reciter to raise his head. The second etiquette is that these ten men are not commanded to form rows, nor is the reciter ordered to step forward like an imam; rather each prostrates from where he is, or as they wish.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage outlines two etiquettes for performing sujūd al-tilāwa in a group setting when a reciter recites a verse of prostration and listeners are present. First, the listeners should not raise their heads from prostration before the reciter does, treating the reciter as an imam in that context. Second, there is no command for the listeners to form rows (like in congregational prayer) nor for the reciter to step forward to lead; they may prostrate wherever they are. These etiquettes distinguish the prostration of recitation from the congregational prayer.

Key Terms
اصطفاف (iṣṭifāf): Forming rows (like in congregational prayer). The text says listeners are not commanded to form rows for sujud al-tilawa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a group of people perform sujūd al-tilāwa together, are they required to form rows like in salah?
A) Yes, they must line up
B) No, they may prostrate as they are
C) Only if more than three people
D) The reciter must step forward to lead

Key Takeaway
Sujūd al-tilāwa in a group follows simple etiquettes: listeners follow the reciter's timing but need not arrange themselves in rows.

Conditions for Validity of Sujud al-Tilawa
Ruling on conditions for validity of prostration of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the validity of Sujud al-Tilawa and explain why the taḥrīmah (opening takbīr of prayer) is not required.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Tilawa shares prayer’s conditions but does not require the formal opening takbīr.

Sujud al-Tilawa is a wajib act when reciting or hearing a verse of prostration. But what exactly validates it? This passage clarifies that the same prerequisites that make prayer valid also apply to this prostration—except one key element: the taḥrīmah. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Sujud al-Tilawa. What is its hukm? The passage states that its validity conditions mirror those of prayer, implying it is wajib (as established elsewhere) but with modified conditions.
The ruling itself is not explicitly stated here, but it is assumed as wajib.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites two proofs: an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i regarding the necessity of wudu, and a hadith from Ibn Umar showing the Prophet (ﷺ) used takbir without the formal taḥrīmah.
Both proofs are from sunnah and athar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
From the hadith: the Prophet said takbir and prostrated without initiating a formal prayer, indicating that the taḥrīmah (which initiates prayer) is not required. From the athar: the command to perform wudu shows purity is a condition.
The hadith is the primary proof for the exception of taḥrīmah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider the opening takbir necessary for Sujud al-Tilawa. The Hanafi school differs based on this hadith.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the ummah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that taḥrīmah is not required. The conditions that remain are purity, facing qibla, covering awrah, and avoiding najasah.
This is consistent with the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط لصحتها شرائط الصلوة الا التحريمة
ترجمه : (۷۷۳ (ب) سجدہ تلاوت کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط وہی ہے جو نماز کی شرطیں ہیں سوائے تحریمہ کے۔ تشریح : جو شرطیں نماز کے صحیح ہونے کی ہیں وہی شرطیں سجدہ تلاوت کے صحیح ہونے کی ہیں، مثلا دونوں میں طہارت ہو، قبلہ رخ ہو، البتہ نماز میں تحریمہ ضروری ہے سجدہ تلاوت میں تحریمہ نہیں باندھا جائے گا۔ وجه : سجدہ کے لئے طہارت ہو اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال اذا سمعه وهو على غير وضوء فليتوضأ ثم ليقرأ فليسجد. (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۲۲۰ ، باب في الرجل يسجد السجدة وھو علی غیر وضوء ج اول ص ۷۳۵، نمبر ۴۳۲۴ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ وضو کرے اور اسکے بعد سجدہ تلاوت کرے۔ (۲) عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله يقرأ علينا القرآن فاذا مر بالسجدة كبر و سجد و سجدنا معه . (ابوداود شریف، باب في الرجل يسمع السجدة وهورا كب أو فى غیر صلوۃ ،ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف تکبیر کہہ کر سجدہ میں جائے گا اور تحریمہ نہ باندھے۔(۳) اس قول
And the condition for its validity is the conditions of prayer except for the taḥrīmah. Translation (773[b]): The condition for the validity of sujūd al-tilāwa is the same as the conditions for prayer except for the taḥrīmah. Explanation: The conditions for the validity of prayer are the same for the validity of sujūd al-tilāwa, e.g., both require purity, facing the qibla, except that in prayer the taḥrīmah is necessary while in sujūd al-tilāwa one does not tie the taḥrīmah. Reason: For purity in prostration, there is the saying of a tābi‘ī: Ibrāhīm said: If he hears it while not in wuḍū’, let him perform wuḍū’, then recite, then prostrate. (Musannaf Ibn Abī Shayba, Chapter on a man who prostrates while not in wuḍū’, vol. 1, p. 735, no. 4324) This athar indicates that one should perform wuḍū’ and then make sujūd al-tilāwa. (2) From Ibn ‘Umar: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to recite the Qur’ān to us, and when he came to a prostration, he would say takbīr and prostrate, and we prostrated with him. (Abū Dāwūd, Chapter on a man who hears a prostration while riding or not in prayer, p. 211, no. 1413) This hadith shows that one goes into prostration with just takbīr and does not tie the taḥrīmah. (3) This saying...
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This is a ruling on the validity conditions of sujūd al-tilāwa. The author states that the conditions for validity are the same as for prayer (salāt), meaning one must be in a state of purity (ṭahāra), face the qibla, etc., except that the taḥrīmah (opening takbīr of prayer) is not required. In other words, sujūd al-tilāwa is valid without the formal opening takbīr that initiates prayer; one simply says takbīr and goes into prostration. The proofs provided: a narration from Ibrāhīm al-Nakha‘ī that one should perform wuḍū’ if not in a state of purity before prostrating, and a hadith from Ibn ‘Umar that the Prophet (ﷺ) would say takbīr and prostrate at the verse of prostration, without any additional prayer opening. The third proof is cut off in the text.

Key Terms
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbīr that initiates the formal prayer (salāt), which is a pillar (rukn) of prayer but not required for sujūd al-tilāwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between the conditions for sujūd al-tilāwa and salāt?
A) Sujūd al-tilāwa does not require purity
B) Sujūd al-tilāwa does not require facing qibla
C) Sujūd al-tilāwa does not require the opening takbīr (taḥrīmah)
D) Sujūd al-tilāwa does not require covering the awra

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Tilawa shares all validity conditions with prayer except the formal opening takbīr (taḥrīmah).

Etiquette of Sujud al-Tilawah: The Mustahab Actions
Rulings on the adab of sujud al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended etiquettes of sujud al-tilawah and apply them in practice.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah has recommended adab: recite softly, stand before prostrating, and follow reciter's lead.

Sujud al-tilawah is an act of worship triggered by reciting or hearing verses of prostration. Beyond the obligation (wajib for reciter), there are etiquettes that enhance the practice. In this lesson, we examine three rulings from the Hanafi school on how to perform sujud al-tilawah with proper adab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
From the passage, extract three distinct etiquettes: (1) reciting softly for unprepared, (2) standing before prostrating, (3) listener not raising head before reciter, and no rows required.
2
Understand the hukm level
Each is mustahab (recommended). Note that omitting them does not invalidate the sujud but loses reward.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a scenario: A group hears a sajdah verse. According to the third rule, the listener should wait for the reciter to raise his head, and no one needs to rearrange for rows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود التلاوة (۷۱) وندب اخفاءها من غير متأهب لها ) و ندب القيام ثم السجود لها (۷۷۳[الف]) ولا يرفع السامع رأسه منها قبل تاليها ولا يؤمر التالى بالتقدم ولا السامعون بالاصطفاف فيسجدون كيف كانوا.
ترجمه : (۷۷۱) اور جو سجدہ کے لئے تیار نہ ہو اس کے سامنے آیت سجدہ آہستہ پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔ تشریح : جو سجدہ کرنے کے لئے ذہنی طور پر تیار نہ ہو اس کے سامنے آیت سجدہ آہستہ پڑھنا مستحب ہے تا کہ اس کو سجدہ کے لئے مجبور نہ کیا جائے۔ ترجمه : (۷۷۲) اور مستحب ہے کہ کھڑا ہو پھر اس کے لئے سجدہ کرے۔ تشریح : یہاں سے سجدہ تلاوت کرنے کے چند آداب کا ذکر ہے۔ بیٹھے بیٹھے بھی سجدہ کر سکتا ہے لیکن مستحب یہ ہے کہ کھڑا ہو اور پھر سجدہ میں جائے۔ ترجمه : (۷۷۳[الف]) سننے والا پڑھنے والے سے پہلے اپنا سرنہ اٹھائے ، اور نہ پڑھنے والے کو آگے بڑھنے کا حکم دیا جائے ، اور نہ سننے والےکوصف بندی کا حکم دیا جائے ، اس لئے وہ جیسا چاہیں سجدہ کریں۔

Chapter of Prostration of Recitation: (771) It is mustahab to recite it softly from one who is not prepared for it. (772) And mustahab is to stand then prostrate for it. (773[a]) The listener should not raise his head before the reciter, nor is the reciter commanded to step forward, nor are the listeners commanded to form rows; they prostrate as they are.

Translation: (771) It is mustahab to recite the verse of prostration softly before one who is not prepared for prostration. Explanation: It is mustahab to recite the verse of prostration softly before one who is not mentally prepared to prostrate, so that he is not compelled to prostrate. Translation: (772) It is mustahab to stand then prostrate for it. Explanation: Here several etiquettes of sujud al-tilawah are mentioned. One may prostrate while sitting, but it is mustahab to stand and then go into prostration. Translation: (773[a]) The listener should not raise his head before the reciter, nor is the reciter commanded to step forward, nor are the listeners commanded to form rows; they may prostrate however they wish. Explanation: A person recited a verse of prostration and ten people listened. The reciter and listeners prostrated; think of the reciter as an imam, so the listener should not raise his head before the reciter, but wait for the reciter to raise his head. Another etiquette: those ten people are not commanded to form rows, nor is the reciter commanded to step forward like an imam; rather each prostrates where he is, or as they wish.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the etiquette of sujud al-tilawah. The author, following the Hanafi school, presents three points: (1) It is recommended to recite the verse of prostration quietly if the listener is not prepared for it, to avoid putting him in an awkward position. (2) It is recommended to stand before prostrating, though sitting is permissible. (3) The listener should not raise his head before the reciter, as the reciter takes the position of an imam. Additionally, there is no requirement for the reciter to step forward or for the listeners to form rows; they may prostrate where they are. These etiquettes are based on the practice of the early community.

Key Terms
سجد التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran called 'ayaat al-sajdah'.
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended; an action whose performance is rewarded and whose omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what should the listener do regarding raising the head during sujud al-tilawah?
A) The listener should raise his head before the reciter.
B) The listener should not raise his head before the reciter.
C) The listener must raise his head simultaneously with the reciter.
D) The listener may raise his head whenever he wishes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes consideration for others in sujud al-tilawah: recite softly, stand before prostrating, and follow the reciter's lead without strict rows.

Conditions for Sujud al-Tilawah
Ruling on conditions for sujud al-tilawah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for sujud al-tilawah, identify the exception of the opening takbir, and explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah needs all prayer conditions except the opening takbir.

In this lesson, we examine the conditions for the validity of sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The Hanafi school rules that it shares all the conditions of the prescribed prayer (salah) except for the opening takbir (tahrimah), which is not required. This distinction is based on clear evidence from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions. Understanding this ruling helps you correctly perform this act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: the conditions for sujud al-tilawah are identical to those for salah, with one exception.
Focus on the exception.
2
Note the exception
Recognize that the opening takbir (tahrimah) is not a condition for sujud al-tilawah, unlike for salah.
This is the key difference.
3
Examine the proofs
Look at the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and the athar of Ibrahim and 'Abdullah bin Muslim. They show the Prophet and Companions said takbir and prostrated without an opening takbir.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud.
4
Contrast with other schools
Note the Shafi'i position that sujud al-tilawah requires takbirat al-ihram. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The ikhtilaf affects practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۷۳ [ب] وشرط لصحتها شرائط الصلوة الا التحريمة
ترجمه : (۷۷۳ (ب) سجدہ تلاوت کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط وہی ہے جو نماز کی شرطیں ہیں سوائے تحریمہ کے۔ تشریح : جو شرطیں نماز کے صحیح ہونے کی ہیں وہی شرطیں سجدہ تلاوت کے صحیح ہونے کی ہیں، مثلا دونوں میں طہارت ہو، قبلہ رخ ہو، البتہ نماز میں تحریمہ ضروری ہے سجدہ تلاوت میں تحریمہ نہیں باندھا جائے گا۔ وجه : سجدہ کے لئے طہارت ہو اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال اذا سمعه وهو على غير وضوء فليتوضأ ثم ليقرأ فليسجد. (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۲۲۰ ، باب في الرجل يسجد السجدة وھو علی غیر وضوء ج اول ص ۷۳۵، نمبر ۴۳۲۴ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ وضو کرے اور اسکے بعد سجدہ تلاوت کرے۔ (۲) عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله يقرأ علينا القرآن فاذا مر بالسجدة كبر و سجد و سجدنا معه . (ابوداود شریف، باب في الرجل يسمع السجدة وهورا كب أو فى غیر صلوۃ ،ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف تکبیر کہہ کر سجدہ میں جائے گا اور تحریمہ ن باندھے۔(۳) اس قول
تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسلم قال كان ابي اذا قرأ السجدة قال الله اكبر ثم سجد . (مصنف ابن ابی شیة ۲۰۲ ، باب من قال اذا قرأت السجدة فكبر واسجد، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۴، نمبر ۴۱۸۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحریمہ نہ باندھے۔ (۴) قبلہ رخ ہو اس کے لئے یہ عمل تابعی ہے۔ عن ابي عبد الرحمن انه كان يقرأ بها و هو جالس فيستقبل القبلة و يسجد ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۲۱ ، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة وهوعلى غير القبلة ، ج اول ص ۳۷۶، نمبر ۴۳۳۰ ) اس میں ہے کہ قبلہ رخ سجدہ کرے۔
(773[b]) And its conditions for validity are the conditions of prayer except the takbirat al-tahrimah.

Translation: (773[b]) The conditions for the validity of sujud al-tilawah are the same as the conditions for prayer except the opening takbir. Explanation: The conditions for the validity of prayer are the same conditions for the validity of sujud al-tilawah, e.g., both require purity, facing the qiblah. However, in prayer the opening takbir is obligatory; in sujud al-tilawah, the opening takbir is not performed. Proof: For purity, there is this saying of a tabi'i: From Ibrahim, he said: 'If he hears it while not in wudu, let him perform wudu, then recite, then prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 220, Bab fi al-rajul yasjud al-sajdah wa huwa 'ala ghayr wudu', vol. 1, p. 735, no. 4324) This athar indicates to perform wudu and then perform sujud al-tilawah. (2) From Ibn 'Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah would recite Quran to us; when he passed a verse of prostration, he would say 'Allahu Akbar', prostrate, and we prostrated with him.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-rajul yasma' al-sajdah wa huwa rakib aw fi ghayr salat, p. 211, no. 1413) This hadith shows that one simply says takbir and prostrates, and does not perform the opening takbir. (3) This is also in the saying of a tabi'i: From 'Abdullah bin Muslim: 'When my father recited a verse of prostration, he would say 'Allahu Akbar', then prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 202, Bab man qala idha qara't al-sajdah fakabbir wa asjud, vol. 1, p. 1364, no. 4187) This athar shows he did not perform the opening takbir. (4) For facing the qiblah: there is this action of a tabi'i: From Abu 'Abd al-Rahman: 'He would recite it while sitting, and would face the qiblah and prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 221, Bab al-rajul yaqra' al-sajdah wa huwa 'ala ghayr al-qiblah, vol. 1, p. 376, no. 4330) It shows to prostrate facing the qiblah.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The author states that the conditions for the validity of sujud al-tilawah are identical to those for salah, with the sole exception of the opening takbir (tahrimah). Thus, one must be in a state of ritual purity (wudu or ghusl), face the qiblah, cover the awrah, and avoid najasah. However, the opening takbir is not required. The proofs provided are from the actions of the Companions and Successors: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar shows that the Prophet (s) simply said takbir and prostrated without an opening takbir. The athar of Ibrahim and 'Abdullah bin Muslim confirm this. For facing the qiblah, the athar of Abu 'Abd al-Rahman is cited. These sources establish the Hanafi position that sujud al-tilawah does not require the tahrimah.

Key Terms
تحریمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates prayer.
شرط (sharṭ): A condition that must be present for the act to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which condition of salah is NOT required for sujud al-tilawah?
A) Purity (taharah)
B) Facing the qiblah
C) Opening takbir (tahrimah)
D) Covering the awrah

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah requires the same conditions as salah, except the opening takbir (tahrimah), as proven by the practice of the Prophet.

The Manner of Sujud al-Tilawah
Description of the manner of sujud al-tilawah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi manner of sujud al-tilawah and identify which elements are sunnah and which are not required.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is one sajdah between two takbirs, without hands, tashahhud, or taslim.

This lesson explains the specific manner of performing the prostration of recitation (sujud al-tilawah) as established in the Hanafi school. Unlike the prostrations within the obligatory prayer, sujud al-tilawah has a simpler form, with no tashahhud or taslim. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components
The passage lists: one prostration between two takbirs, no raising hands, no tashahhud, no taslim.
2
Note the ruling of each component
The takbirs are sunnah, not wajib; the absence of tashahhud and taslim is confirmed by athar.
3
Review the proofs
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar shows the takbirs; the athar of Sa'id bin Jubayr and al-Hasan show no taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۷۴) اور سجدے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ دو تکبیروں کے درمیان ایک سجدہ کرے، یہ دونوں تکبیر میں سنت ہیں، بغیر ہاتھ اٹھائے ہوئے ، اور بغیر تشہد پڑھے ہوئے ، اور بغیر سلام کے۔ تشریح : سجدہ تلاوت کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ تکبیر کہ کر جدہ میں جائے اور تکبیر کہ کرسجدہ سے سراٹھائے ہتکبیر کے لئے ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے ، تشہد نہ پڑھے ، سلام نہ پھیرے۔ اس سجدہ تلاوت کرے۔
وجه : (۱) تکبیر کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله يقرأ علينا القرآن فاذا مر بالسجدة كبر وسجد و سجدنا معه . (ابوداود شریف، باب فی الرجل يسمع السجدة وھورا كب او فی غیر صلوۃ ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۱۳) (۲) سلام نہ کرے اور تشہد نہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن سعید بن جبير انه كان يقرأ السجدة فيرفع رأسه ولا يسلم، قال كان الحسن يقرأ بنا سجود القرآن ولا يسلم . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۰۱ ، باب من کان لا يسلم من السجدة ، ج اول ، ص ۱۳۶۴، نمبر ۴۱۸۳/۴۱۸۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ تلاوت میں تشہد اور سلام نہیں ہیں۔ صرف تکبیر کہہ کر سجدہ کرے پھر تکبیر کہہ کر سر اٹھائے بس اتنا ہی کافی ہے۔
Translation: (774) And its manner is that he performs one prostration between two takbirs; both takbirs are sunnah, without raising hands, without reciting tashahhud, and without taslim. Explanation: The manner of sujud al-tilawah is that he says takbir and goes into prostration, then says takbir and raises his head from prostration. He does not raise his hands for the takbirs, does not recite tashahhud, does not give taslim. He performs sujud al-tilawah in this way.
Proof: (1) For saying takbir, there is this hadith: From Ibn 'Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah would recite Quran to us; when he passed a verse of prostration, he would say 'Allahu Akbar', prostrate, and we prostrated with him.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-rajul yasma' al-sajdah wa huwa rakib aw fi ghayr salat, p. 211, no. 1413) (2) For not giving taslim and not reciting tashahhud, there is this saying of a tabi'i: From Sa'id bin Jubayr: 'He would recite a verse of prostration, then raise his head and not give taslim.' And he said: 'Al-Hasan would lead us in the prostrations of the Quran and would not give taslim.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 201, Bab man kana la yusallim min al-sajdah, vol. 1, p. 1364, nos. 4183/4184) This athar shows that in sujud al-tilawah, there is no tashahhud and no taslim. Simply say takbir, prostrate, then say takbir and raise the head; that is sufficient.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This is a ruling statement describing the manner of sujud al-tilawah. The Hanafi school holds that the prostration consists of one sajdah between two takbirs: the first takbir when going down, the second when rising. Both takbirs are sunnah. There is no raising of hands, no tashahhud, and no taslim. The proofs are from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and the athar of Sa'id bin Jubayr and al-Hasan. This distinguishes sujud al-tilawah from the prostrations within salah, which include tashahhud and taslim.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah consists of one sajdah between two sunnah takbirs, with no tashahhud or taslim.

Ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr
Ruling on sajdat al-shukr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-shukr and explain why it is considered makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-shukr is makruh and unrewarded in the Hanafi school; leave it.

When a Muslim receives a sudden blessing or good news, the spontaneous urge to prostrate in gratitude is natural. However, the Hanafi school, following Imam Abu Hanifah, holds that performing a separate prostration for gratitude (sajdat al-shukr) is a disliked and sinful act. This lesson clarifies the ruling and its basis so you can act with knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the act in question is sujud performed spontaneously upon receiving a blessing, outside the context of prayer.
2
State the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifah
The text explicitly says 'sajdat al-shukr is makruh according to the Imam.' Memorize this: makruh tahrimi, meaning it is sinful and should be avoided.
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram.
3
Understand the consequence
The text adds 'there is no reward for it.' This means that even if one performs it, no spiritual reward is earned. It is a waste of effort.
4
Note the recommended action
The author instructs: 'leaving it is better.' Therefore, the mufta bihi (operative) position is to avoid sajdat al-shukr entirely.
5
Recognize the authority level
This ruling is from Imam Abu Hanifah himself, and the text presents it as the relied-upon view. Be aware that some Sahibayn may have considered it permissible, but the fatwa is on makruh.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is consider it mustahab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : (۷۷۵)سجدة الشكر مكروهة عند الامام لا يثاب عليها وتركها
ترجمه : (۷۷۵) امام صاحب کے نزدیک تنہا سجدہ شکر مکروہ ہے، اس کا کچھ ثواب نہیں ، اس لئے نہ کرے۔ تشریح : سجدہ شکر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کوئی بات آئی تو فورا سجدہ میں گر جائے ، مصنف لکھتے ہیں کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ مکروہ
Section: (775) Sajdat al-shukr is makruh according to the Imam (Abu Hanifah); there is no reward for it, and leaving it is (better).

Translation: (775) According to Imam Abu Hanifah, sajdat al-shukr alone is makruh; there is no reward for it, so do not perform it. Explanation: Sajdat al-shukr means that when something (good) happens, one immediately goes into prostration. The author writes that according to Imam Abu Hanifah, it is makruh.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on sajdat al-shukr, the prostration of gratitude. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, performing a separate prostration for gratitude (outside of prayer) is makruh and not rewarded. Therefore, it should be avoided. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position. The text indicates that this ruling is specific to Imam Abu Hanifah, implying that Abu Yusuf or Muhammad may have had a different view, but the author presents this as the correct view.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed upon receiving a blessing or good news as an expression of gratitude to Allah.
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; an action that is sinful to perform but less severe than haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is mustahab and rewarded.
B) It is wajib upon receiving a blessing.
C) It is makruh and not rewarded.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-shukr is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school; perform it not, for it earns no reward.

Manner of Sujood al-Tilawah and Its Proofs
Ruling with proof on the manner of sujood al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the manner of sujood al-tilawah and identify the two proofs that establish it according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sujood al-tilawah: one prostration between two sunnah takbirs — no tashahhud, no taslim.

Sujood al-tilawah is a simple act of worship performed when reciting or hearing a Quranic verse of prostration. This lesson clarifies its exact manner as taught by the Hanafi school, distinguishing it from the prostrations in regular prayer. We will also examine the textual evidence — a hadith from Ibn Umar and an athar from the Salaf — that establish the two sunnah takbirs and the omission of tashahhud and taslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being described: the manner of sujood al-tilawah (and al-shukr). Note that the text labels the two takbirs as 'sunnah', so the overall hukm is sunnah muakkadah.
The ruling is not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the components of the manner
Break down the description: one prostration, two takbirs (one to enter, one to rise), and the omitted elements: no raising of hands, no tashahhud, no taslim.
Memorise these components distinctly.
3
Find the first proof (hadith)
The text cites Ibn Umar's hadith: the Prophet would say takbir when passing a sajdah verse and prostrate. This establishes the takbir before prostration.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1413.
4
Find the second proof (athar)
The text cites Sa'id ibn Jubayr and Hasan al-Basri: they recited the sujood verse and raised their heads without taslim. This shows that taslim and tashahhud are not part of sujood al-tilawah.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, nos. 4183/4184.
5
Connect the proofs to the ruling
Understand how each proof supports a specific element: the hadith supports the takbir, the athar supports the absence of taslim. Together they define the complete manner.
Both proofs are zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل سجدة الشكر (۷۷۴) وكيفيتها ان يسجد سجدة واحدة بين تكبيرتين هما سنتان بلا رفع يد ولا تشهد ولا تسليم.

ترجمه : (۷۷۴) اور سجدے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ دو تکبیروں کے درمیان ایک سجدہ کرے، یہ دونوں تکبیر میں سنت ہیں، بغیر ہاتھ اٹھائے ہوئے ، اور بغیر تشہد پڑھے ہوئے ، اور بغیر سلام کے۔ تشریح : سجدہ تلاوت کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ تکبیر کہ کر جدہ میں جائے اور تکبیر کہ کرسجدہ سے سراٹھائے ہتکبیر کے لئے ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے ، تشہد نہ پڑھے ، سلام نہ پھیرے۔ اس سجدہ تلاوت کرے۔
وجه : (۱) تکبیر کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله يقرأ علينا القرآن فاذا مر بالسجدة كبر وسجد و سجدنا معه . (ابوداود شریف، باب فی الرجل يسمع السجدة وھورا کب او فی غیر صلوۃ ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۱۳) (۲) سلام نہ کرے اور تشہد نہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن سعید بن جبير انه كان يقرأ السجدة فيرفع رأسه ولا يسلم، قال كان الحسن يقرأ بنا سجود القرآن ولا يسلم . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۰۱ ، باب من کان لا يسلم من السجدة ، ج اول ، ص ۱۳۶۴، نمبر ۴۱۸۳/۴۱۸۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ تلاوت میں تشہد اور سلام نہیں ہیں۔ صرف تکبیر کہہ کر سجدہ کرے پھر تکبیر کہہ کر سر اٹھائے بس اتنا ہی کافی ہے۔
Chapter of Sujood al-Shukr. (774) Its manner is that he performs one prostration between two takbirs; both are sunnah, without raising hands, without tashahhud, and without taslim. Translation: (774) And the manner of prostration is that he performs one prostration between two takbirs; these both takbirs are sunnah, without raising hands, and without reciting tashahhud, and without taslim. Explanation: The manner of sujood al-tilawah is that he says takbir and goes into prostration, and says takbir and raises his head from prostration; he does not raise hands for the takbir, does not recite tashahhud, does not give taslim. He performs this sujood al-tilawah. Evidence: (1) For saying takbir, there is this hadith: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to recite the Quran to us, and when he passed by a prostration verse, he would say takbir and prostrate, and we prostrated with him. (Abu Dawud, chapter on a man who hears the prostration while riding or not in prayer, p. 211, no. 1413) (2) For not doing taslim and tashahhud, there is this saying of a tabi'i: From Sa'id ibn Jubayr that he used to recite the prostration and raise his head without saying taslim. He said: Al-Hasan used to lead us in the prostrations of the Quran and did not say taslim. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 201, chapter on those who did not say taslim from the prostration, vol. 1, p. 1364, nos. 4183/4184) From this athar it is known that there is no tashahhud or taslim in sujood al-tilawah. Simply say takbir and prostrate, then say takbir and raise the head; this is sufficient.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with its proofs on the manner of performing sujood al-shukr, which is the same as sujood al-tilawah. The Arabic matn states: one prostration between two takbirs; the takbirs are sunnah, and there is no raising of hands, no tashahhud, and no taslim. The Urdu commentary expands on this by explaining that the manner of sujood al-tilawah is: say takbir and go into sujood, then say takbir and rise; no hands raised, no tashahhud, no taslim. Two proofs are given: 1) The hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet would say takbir when passing a sajdah verse and prostrate. 2) The athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr and Hasan al-Basri that they did not say taslim after sujood al-tilawah. Thus the prostration consists only of two takbirs and one sajdah.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed to thank Allah for a blessing or deliverance from harm.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' to mark the beginning and end of the prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many takbirs are performed in sujood al-tilawah according to this text?
A) One takbir
B) Two takbirs
C) Three takbirs
D) None

Key Takeaway
Sujood al-tilawah and sujood al-shukr are performed as a single prostration between two takbirs, with no tashahhud or taslim.

Ruling on Sujood al-Shukr: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of sujood al-shukr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on sujood al-shukr and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Sujood al-shukr is makruh according to Abu Hanifa but a rewardable act according to Sahibayn; the latter is the preponderant view.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that sujood al-shukr (prostration of thanks) is makruh and yields no reward, while his two senior disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), consider it a meritorious act (qurbah) deserving reward. Understanding the reasoning and evidence for each position is essential for grasping the school's methodology in handling differing proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position of Imam Abu Hanifa
Identify the ruling attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa: sujood al-shukr is makruh (disliked) and no reward is earned. Note that the text does not provide his explicit evidence, but the rationale is that sujood is a worship act limited to prayer or specific causes.
The text uses 'عند الامام' to indicate Imam Abu Hanifa's view.
2
Identify the opposing view of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that sujood al-shukr is a qurbah (act of worship) worthy of reward. They equate its performance to sujood al-tilawah in form and conditions.
The phrase 'وقالا هي قربة' marks their position.
3
Examine the evidence for the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn cite the hadith of Abu Bakrah: the Prophet would prostrate in gratitude upon receiving joyful news. This dalil is ahad but considered reliable in meaning.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi; the text quotes it partially.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, one should avoid sujood al-shukr (leaving it is better). According to the Sahibayn, performing it is recommended and brings reward.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) in later Hanafi works favors the Sahibayn.
5
Determine the tarjih and the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya) give preponderance to the Sahibayn's view, deeming sujood al-shukr permissible and recommended.
This tarjih is based on the strength of the hadith and the principle that acts of worship are permissible unless prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۷۵)سجدة الشكر مكروهة عند الامام لا يثاب عليها وتركها
تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسلم قال كان ابي اذا قرأ السجدة قال الله اكبر ثم سجد . (مصنف ابن ابی شیة ۲۰۲ ، باب من قال اذا قرأت السجدة فكبر واسجد، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۴، نمبر ۴۱۸۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحریمہ نہ باندھے۔ (۴) قبلہ رخ ہو اس کے لئے یہ عمل تابعی ہے۔ عن ابي عبد الرحمن انه كان يقرأ بها و هو جالس فيستقبل القبلة و يسجد ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۲۱ ، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة وهوعلى غير القبلة ، ج اول ص ۳۷۶، نمبر ۴۳۳۰ ) اس میں ہے کہ قبلہ رخ سجدہ کرے۔
(۷۷۶) وقالا هي قربة يثاب عليها وهيئتها مثل سجدة التلاوة.
ترجمه : (۷۷۶) صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ یہ قربت ہے اس پر ثواب دیا جائے گا، اور اس کی ہیئت سجدہ تلاوت کی طرح ہے۔ تشریح : صاحبین کے نزدیک آگے والے حدیث کی وجہ سے سجدہ شکر جائز بھی ہے، قربت کی چیز بھی ہے، اور اس پر ثواب بھی دیا جائے گا۔ اور جس طرح سجدہ تلاوت کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح سجدہ شکر بھی ادا کرے ، اور انہیں شرطوں کے ساتھ کرے ، یعنی طہارت ہو قبلہ رخ ہو وغیرہ۔ وجه : عن ابى بكرة عن النبى الله انه كان اذا جائه امر سرور او بشر به خرا ساجدا شاكرا لله_(ابوداود شریف ، باب فی سجود الشکر، ص ۴۰۴، نمبر ۲۷۷۴ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی سجدة الشكر ، ص ۱۳۸۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور میلہ سجدہ شکر ادا کرتے تھے ۔
(775) Sujood al-shukr is makruh according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]; no reward is earned for it, and leaving it [is better]. It is also [mentioned] in the tabi'i [generation]. From Abdullah ibn Muslim: My father, when he recited the prostration verse, said Allahu Akbar and then prostrated. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 202, chapter on one who said when reciting the prostration 'Allahu Akbar' and prostrated, vol. 1, p. 1364, no. 4187) From this athar it is known that he does not bind the takbirat al-tahrimah. (4) Face the qiblah: for this there is the practice of a tabi'i. From Abi Abd al-Rahman that he recited it [the prostration] while sitting, so he faced the qiblah and prostrated. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 221, chapter on a man who recites the prostration while not facing the qiblah, vol. 1, p. 376, no. 4330) In it is that he prostrates facing the qiblah. (776) And they (the two) said: It is an act of worship; reward is earned for it, and its manner is like sujood al-tilawah. Translation: (776) The Sahibayn said that it is a good deed; reward will be given for it, and its manner is like that of sujood al-tilawah. Explanation: According to the Sahibayn, due to the upcoming hadith, sujood al-shukr is permissible, it is a good deed, and reward will be given for it. And just as sujood al-tilawah is performed, similarly sujood al-shukr should be performed, with the same conditions, i.e., purity, facing qiblah, etc. Evidence: From Abu Bakrah, from the Prophet, that when a matter of joy came to him or he was given glad tidings, he would fall down prostrating, thanking Allah. (Abu Dawud, chapter on sujood al-shukr, p. 404, no. 2774; Tirmidhi, chapter on sujood al-shukr, p. 1383, no. 1578) In this hadith is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed sujood al-shukr.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of sujood al-shukr. Imam Abu Hanifa holds it to be makruh, meaning it is disliked and no reward is earned. The reason is that sujood is a form of worship specific to prayer, and performing it outside prayer without a clear command is disliked. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, holding it to be a good deed (qurbah) with reward, citing the hadith of Abu Bakrah that the Prophet performed sujood al-shukr upon receiving joyful news. The manner, according to them, is identical to sujood al-tilawah: two takbirs, one sajdah, conditions of purity and facing qiblah. The commentary also includes conditions for sujood al-tilawah (facing qiblah, no takbirat al-tahrimah) which are relevant to both.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed to thank Allah for a blessing, without being linked to recitation.
الامام (al-imam): Refers to Imam Abu Hanifa in this context.
صاحبین (sahibayn): The two disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Makruh and no reward
B) Qurbah and rewardable
C) Haram
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Sujood al-shukr is a rewardable act according to the preponderant Hanafi view (Sahibayn), provided conditions like purity and facing qiblah are met.

Benefit of Reciting All Sajdah Verses
Narrates a benefit from Imam al-Nasafi about reciting all sajdah verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the practice and promised benefit of reciting all sajdah verses in one sitting according to Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Reciting all 14 sajdah verses in one sitting with separate prostrations brings divine sufficiency.

This lesson presents a spiritual practice narrated by Imam al-Nasafi, a renowned Hanafi scholar. It is not a legal obligation but a recommended act with a promised benefit. Understanding its basis helps us appreciate the devotional dimensions of sujood al-tilawah and its potential rewards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Practice
The practice consists of reciting all verses of sajdah (prostration) from the Quran in a single sitting (majlis wahid) and performing a separate prostration (sajdah) for each verse. Note that according to the Hanafi school, there are 14 such verses.
2
Understand the Promised Outcome
The passage states that whoever does this, Allah will suffice them in what concerns them (كفاه الله ما اهمه). This includes all important matters, worldly and religious.
3
Recognize the Source and Authority
This benefit is narrated from Imam al-Nasafi (a major Hanafi scholar) in his work al-Kafi. It is not a hadith from the Prophet but a transmitted spiritual practice.

This is not a ruling (hukm) but a recommended act of devotion with a promised benefit. The Urdu commentary reinforces that this practice removes difficulties. The source of this benefit is from the book al-Kafi, which is a well-known Hanafi fiqh work.

Sajdat al-Shukr: Permissibility and Form according to the Sahibayn
Ruling from Sahibayn on permissibility and form of sajdat al-shukr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-shukr according to the Sahibayn, identify its essential conditions, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A prostration of gratitude is a rewarded act of devotion, but its permissibility differs between the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa.

Sajdat al-shukr is a practice of the Prophet ﷺ upon receiving joyful news. While the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) affirm it as a legitimate and rewarding act, Imam Abu Hanifa reportedly held a different view. This lesson examines the ruling, the evidence, and the conditions for this prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling per Sahibayn
Read the Arabic text: 'Wa qala hiya qurbah yuthabu alayha'. Determine the legal classification: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or something else? Note that it is called a qurbah (act of devotion).
In Hanafi terminology, 'qurbah' refers to a mustahabb (recommended) act.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith of Abu Bakra which shows the Prophet ﷺ prostrated upon receiving joyful news. Identify the source and its chain.
The hadith is in Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. Since it describes the Prophet's action without an explicit command, what does that indicate in Hanafi usul? The action demonstrates permissibility and recommendation.
In Hanafi usul, an action of the Prophet ﷺ without a command indicates sunnah (recommendation), not obligation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Compare the Sahibayn's position with that of Imam Abu Hanifa. The source mentions an ikhtilaf. Understand the basis for each view and which is mufta bihi.
Later Hanafi scholars prefer the Sahibayn's view due to the strength of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة مهمة (۷۷۶) وقالا هى قربة يثاب عليها وهيئتها مثل سجدة التلاوة. ترجمه : (۷۷۶) صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ یہ قربت ہے اس پر ثواب دیا جائے گا، اور اس کی ہیئت سجدہ تلاوت کی طرح ہے۔ تشریح : صاحبین کے نزدیک آگے والے حدیث کی وجہ سے سجدہ شکر جائز بھی ہے، قربت کی چیز بھی ہے، اور اس پر ثواب بھی دیا جائے گا۔ اور جس طرح سجدہ تلاوت کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح سجدہ شکر بھی ادا کرے ، اور انہیں شرطوں کے ساتھ کرے ، یعنی طہارت ہو قبلہ رخ ہو وغیرہ۔ وجه : عن ابى بكرة عن النبى الله انه كان اذا جائه امر سرور او بشر به خرا ساجدا شاكرا لله_(ابوداود شریف ، باب فی سجود الشکر، ص ۴۰۴، نمبر ۲۷۷۴ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی سجدة الشكر ، ص ۱۳۸۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور میلہ سجدہ شکر ادا کرتے تھے ۔
Important benefit (776): And they (the two, i.e., Sahibayn) said: It is an act of devotion for which reward is given, and its form is like the prostration of recitation. Translation: (776) The Sahibayn said: This is an act of devotion, reward will be given for it, and its form is like the prostration of recitation. Explanation: According to the Sahibayn, due to the hadith mentioned below, the prostration of gratitude is permissible, it is an act of devotion, and reward will be given for it. And just as the prostration of recitation is performed, similarly the prostration of gratitude should be performed, and with the same conditions, i.e., purity, facing the qibla, etc. Evidence: From Abu Bakra from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that when a matter of joy came to him or he was given glad tidings, he would fall prostrate in gratitude to Allah. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on the Prostration of Gratitude, p. 404, no. 2774; Tirmidhi, Chapter on the Prostration of Gratitude, p. 1383, no. 1578) This hadith indicates that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform the prostration of gratitude.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that sajdat al-shukr (prostration of gratitude) is a legitimate act of devotion (qurbah) that is rewarded. Its form is identical to sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation), requiring the same conditions such as ritual purity and facing the qibla. The evidence is the hadith of Abu Bakra, which shows the Prophet ﷺ performed it upon receiving joyful news. This establishes permissibility and recommendation.

Key Terms
سجدہ الشکر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed to express gratitude to Allah upon receiving a blessing or glad tidings.
قربة (qurbah): An act that brings nearness to Allah and is rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-shukr is a recommended act of gratitude, performed like sajdat al-tilawah, with conditions of purity and facing qiblah; the mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn.

Virtue of Reciting All Sajdah Verses in One Sitting
A virtue statement from al-Nasafi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recount the virtue of reciting all sajdah verses in one sitting and prostrating for each, as reported by Imam al-Nasafi, and identify the Hanafi ruling that sajdah tilawah is wajib.

Core Idea
Reciting all ayat al-sajdah in one sitting with prostrations brings Allah's sufficiency for all important matters.

Imam al-Nasafi records a profound virtue in his al-Kafi: gathering all the verses of prostration in one sitting and performing the prostrations for each. This practice is a powerful means of seeking Allah's help in one's concerns. In the Hanafi school, reciting these verses obligates a prostration (sajdah tilawah), and performing this combined recitation with prostrations is especially recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The virtue is for one who recites all the verses of prostration (ayat al-sajdah) in one sitting (majlis) and performs a prostration for each verse.
These verses are the 14 Quranic verses where prostration is wajib upon recitation according to the Hanafi school.
2
State the promised reward
The reward is that Allah will suffice (kafāhu) that person for all that is important to him (mā ahamma). This includes worldly and religious needs.
3
Note the source
This virtue is attributed to Imam al-Nasafi in his famous work al-Kafi. Recognize the authority: al-Nasafi is an early Hanafi jurist.
4
Understand the additional note
The passage also states that it is permissible for such a person to pray a two-rak'at nafl (supererogatory prayer). This may be an optional extension of the practice.
The nafl prayer is not part of the virtue itself but an additional permissible act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة مهمة لدفع كل مهمة (۷۷۷) قال الامام النسفى فى الكافى من قرأ آى السجدة كلّها في مجلس واحد وسجد لكل منها كفاه الله ما اهمه. ہے، اور اس کے لئے پورا دورکعت نفل پڑھے یہ جائز ہے۔ ترجمه : (۷۷۷) کافی کتاب میں امام نسفی نے کہا ہے کہ : جو ایک مجلس میں تمام سجدہ کی آیتیں پڑھ کر ہر ایک کے لئے علیحدہ علیحدہ سجدہ کرے، تو اللہ تعالی اس کے تمام مقاصد کے لئے کافی ہیں۔

Commentary
This passage relates a benefit from Imam al-Nasafi's work al-Kafi: a person who recites all the Quranic verses of prostration (ayat al-sajdah) in one gathering and performs the respective prostrations will have Allah's sufficiency for all his important matters. The line about reciting a two-rak'at nafl prayer (supererogatory) seems to be an additional note that this is also permissible.

Key Terms
آی السجدة (ayat al-sajdah): Verses of the Quran that require prostration upon recitation.

Key Takeaway

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Conditions for Jumu'ah: Obligation and Validity
Listing of conditions for Jumu'ah being obligatory and valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions for Jumu'ah being obligatory (fard 'ayn) and the six conditions for its validity according to the Hanafi school, and apply them to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn upon every qualified individual; its validity depends on city, sultan, time, khutbah, audience, and congregation.

The Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) holds a special status as a weekly obligation. The Hanafi school enumerates specific conditions that make Jumu'ah binding on an individual, and separate conditions that must be fulfilled for the prayer to be valid. This lesson unpacks both sets of conditions as presented in the classical matn.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate between obligation and validity conditions
Recognize that the passage first lists conditions for Jumu'ah to become obligatory (fard 'ayn) on an individual, then lists conditions for the prayer itself to be valid. These two sets are distinct.
Obligation conditions relate to the person; validity conditions relate to the prayer's performance.
2
Identify the seven conditions for obligation
List each of the seven conditions: male, free, resident (in city or environs per al-asbah riwayah), healthy, safe from oppressor, both eyes sound, both feet sound.
The condition of residence includes environs (fana'). Absence of sight or limbs does not affect validity if Jumu'ah is performed.
3
Identify the six conditions for validity
List each of the six validity conditions: city or outskirts, sultan or his deputy, time of Zuhr, khutbah before prayer, at least one obligatee present to listen, general permission.
There is also an additional condition: congregation of three persons besides the imam, even if slaves, travelers, or sick.
4
Analyze the additional congregation requirement
Note that the congregation of three (aside from imam) is mentioned after the six, implying it is a seventh validity condition or a further specification. The text treats it as supplementary.
This congregation confirms the public nature of Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجمعة باب : جمعہ کے بیان میں کی جس میں سات شرطیں پائی جاویں اس پر نماز جمعہ فرض عین ہے:۔ ....... مرد ہو۔ .......آزاد ہو۔ شہر میں یا اس کی حد میں اصبح روایت میں مقیم ہو۔ ..... تندرست ہو۔ ظالم سے امن ہو۔ ... دونوں آنکھیں سلامت ہوں ۔ ... دونوں پاؤں سلامت ہوں۔ اور جمعہ صحیح ہونے کے لئے چھ چیزیں شرط ہیں: شہر یا فناء شہر ۔ ...... سلطان یا اس کا نائب۔ ..... ظہر کا وقت ، پس ظہر سے پہلے جمعہ صحیح نہیں، ظہر کے وقت میں جمعہ کی نیت سے اس سے پہلے خطبہ ہو۔ جن لوگوں سے جمعہ ادا ہوتا ہو ان میں سے ایک شخص بھی خطبہ سننے کے لئے حاضر ہو۔ ...... عام اجازت ہو۔ ☆☆☆ امام کے سوا تین آدمی کی جماعت ہو، خواہ غلام ہوں، یا مسافر ہوں، یا بیمار ہوں ۔ باب الجمعة ضروری نوٹ: جمعہ اہل شہر پر واجب ہے اور پہلی مرتبہ اس کو مدینہ میں قائم کیا تھا۔ اس کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہے۔ یا ایھا الذين آمنوا اذا نودي للصلوة من يوم الجمعة فاسعوا الى ذكر الله وذروا البیع ۔ ( آیت ۹ ، سورۃ الجمعۃ ۶۲) اس آیت سے جمعہ کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔ جمعہ کا ثبوت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن عمر و أبا هريرة حدثاه أنهما سمعا
Chapter of Jumu'ah: Chapter explaining Jumu'ah. The one in whom seven conditions are found, Jumu'ah prayer is fard 'ayn upon him: ... male, ... free, resident in a city or its boundary according to the morning narration (asbah riwayah), ... healthy, safe from the oppressor, ... both eyes sound, ... both feet sound. And for Jumu'ah to be valid, six things are conditions: city or its outskirts, ... sultan or his deputy, ... time of Zuhr, so Jumu'ah is not valid before Zuhr; in the time of Zuhr, with intention of Jumu'ah, a khutbah before it. At least one person from those upon whom Jumu'ah is performed is present to listen to the khutbah. ... general permission. ☆☆☆ Congregation of three persons besides the imam, whether they be slaves, travellers, or sick. Chapter of Jumu'ah: Necessary note: Jumu'ah is obligatory on the people of the city, and it was first established in Madinah. Its proof is this verse: 'O you who believe, when the call to prayer is made on Friday, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade.' (Surah al-Jumu'ah, verse 9). From this verse the proof of Jumu'ah is established. The proof of Jumu'ah is also in this hadith: 'Indeed Abdullah ibn Umar and Abu Hurayrah narrated to him that they both heard...'
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on Jumu'ah (Friday prayer) by listing conditions. First, seven conditions for Jumu'ah to become obligatory (fard 'ayn) on an individual: being male, free, resident in a city (or its environs according to one narration, al-asbah riwayah), healthy, safe from an oppressive ruler, having both eyes sighted, and having both feet sound. Second, six conditions for Jumu'ah to be valid: the prayer must be held in a city or its outskirts; the sultan or his deputy must be present (or authorize the imam); it must be performed in the time of Zuhr (i.e., after the sun passes the meridian); a khutbah (sermon) must be delivered before the prayer with the intention of Jumu'ah; at least one person from those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory must be present to listen to the khutbah; and there must be general permission (i.e., the doors are open for people to attend). The passage then adds that the congregation must consist of at least three persons besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travellers, or ill. Finally, a note confirms that Jumu'ah is wajib on the people of the city and was first established in Madinah, citing Quran 62:9 and an incomplete hadith.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition; something that must be present for an act to be obligatory or valid.
فناء شہر (fana' al-madinah): The outskirts or environs of a city, including adjacent dwellings and fields.
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before the Jumu'ah prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Seven
B) Six
C) Five
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only on those who meet seven specific conditions; its validity rests on six distinct conditions.

Seven Conditions for Jumu'ah Being Obligatory
Lists conditions for obligation and provides proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn and identify which individuals are exempted from the obligation.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only when seven conditions combine; absence of any one removes the obligation but does not invalidate the prayer.

This lesson focuses on the first set of conditions presented in the passage: those that make Jumu'ah an individual obligation. Understanding these conditions is crucial because they determine who must attend Jumu'ah and who is excused. The passage lists seven conditions and provides hadith proofs. Note that the conditions for obligation are separate from the conditions for validity, which we will cover in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
List the seven conditions
From the passage, extract the seven conditions required for Jumu'ah to be fard 'ayn: being male, free, residing in a city, healthy, safe from an oppressor, having both eyes, and having both feet.
The conditions are listed in the Arabic text after 'جس میں سات شرطیں پائی جاویں اس پر نماز جمعہ فرض عین ہے'.
2
Identify who is exempted for each condition
For each condition, state the corresponding exempted group: women (non-male), slaves (non-free), travelers/villagers (non-resident), sick (non-healthy), those in unsafe areas, blind (missing eyes), and crippled (missing feet).
The exemptions are explicitly mentioned in the commentary.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Dawood lists four exemptions: slave, woman, child, and sick. The Darqutni addition adds 'traveler'. Explain how these cover most of the seven conditions.
Children are not in the seven conditions; they are exempted by default.
4
Understand the ruling when obligation is absent
If a person lacks one of the seven conditions, Jumu'ah is not fard 'ayn on them. However, if they choose to pray it, it is valid and suffices for Zuhr. This is supported by an athar from Hasan al-Basri.
This distinguishes between obligation (shurut al-wujub) and validity (shurut al-sihhah).

وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن طارق بن شهاب عن النبى الله الله قال الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة الا اربعة عبد مملوک او امرأة او صبى او مريض (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة للملوك والمرأة ،ص۱۶۲، نمبر ۱۰۶۷) دارقطنی میں اومسافر، کا لفظ بھی ہے ( دار قطنی ، باب من تجب علیہ الجمعہ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳ نمبر۱۵۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام، عورت، بچہ اور بیمار پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔
ترجمه : (۷۷۹) [۵] ظالم سے امن ہو ۔ [۶] دونوں آنکھیں سلامت ہوں ۔ [2] دونوں پاؤں سلامت ہوں۔ تشریح : پانچویں شرط یہ ہے کہ ظالم سے امن ہو چنانچہ اگر شہر میں ہنگامہ، جس سے جان کا خطرہ ہو تو جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ دونوں آنکھیں سلامت ہو، چنانچہ نابینا پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ ساتویں شرط یہ ہے کہ دونوں پاؤں سالم ہوں ، چنانچہ اپاہج پر جمعہ
واجب نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) امن اور ا پانچ کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے . عن الحسن قال ليس على الخائف و لا على العبد يخدم أهـلـه و لا عـلـى ولى الجنازة و لا على الاعمى اذا لم يجد قائدا الجمعة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من رخص في ترک الجمعۃ ، ج اول ،ص ۴۷۹، نمبر ۵۵۲۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جہاں امن نہ ہو، اور غلام اور نا بینا کو مسجد تک لیجانے والا نہ ہو تو اس پر جمعہ نہیں ہے۔ (۲) یہ لوگ جمعہ پڑھے تو ہو جائے گا اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن الحسن قال ان جمعن مع الامام اجز أهن من صلوة الامام. مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ،۳۴۰ المرأة تشهد الجمعة اتجزيها صلوۃ الامام ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۵۵۶
Chapter of Friday. Conditions for Jumu'ah: On whom seven conditions are found, Jumu'ah prayer is fard 'ayn: male, free, residing in a city or its boundary according to the more sound narration, healthy, safe from an oppressor, both eyes sound, both feet sound. For Jumu'ah to be valid, six things are conditions: city or its outskirts, sultan or his deputy, time of Zuhr (so before Zuhr Jumu'ah is not valid), a sermon before it with intention of Jumu'ah, presence of one person from those for whom Jumu'ah is valid to hear the sermon, general permission. And congregation of three besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. Note: Jumu'ah is wajib on city dwellers, first established in Madinah. Proof: Quran 62:9. Also hadith from Muslim. Translation: (778) Jumu'ah prayer is fard 'ayn for one in whom seven conditions combine: [1] male, [2] free, [3] residing in city or its boundary, [4] healthy, [5] safe from oppressor, [6] both eyes sound, [7] both feet sound. Commentary: If these seven are found, Jumu'ah is fard; if one is missing, it is not fard but if performed it is valid. First condition: male, so not wajib on women. Second: free, not on slaves. Third: residing, not on traveler or villager. Fourth: healthy, not on sick. Proof: Hadith from Abu Dawood: Jumu'ah is a right wajib on every Muslim except four: slave, woman, child, sick. In Darqutni: or traveler. Fifth: safe from oppressor, so if turmoil dangerous, not wajib. Both eyes sound, so blind not wajib. Both feet sound, so crippled not wajib. Proof: Athar from Hasan: Jumu'ah is not on the fearful, the slave serving his family, the one accompanying a funeral, the blind without guide. (2) If they pray Jumu'ah, it is valid: Athar from Hasan: If they pray with imam, it suffices them from Zuhr.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by listing seven conditions for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn: male, free, settled in a city (muqeem), healthy, safe from an oppressor, having both eyes, and both feet. Then it lists six conditions for Jumu'ah to be valid: city or outskirts, presence of ruler or deputy, time of Zuhr, a sermon before the prayer, presence of at least one person from those obligated to hear the sermon, and general permission. It further states that a congregation of three besides the imam is required for validity. The text provides proofs from the Quran (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) and multiple hadith, including from Muslim, Abu Dawood, and Darqutni, establishing the obligation and specifying exemptions. The commentary explains each condition and notes that if a person lacking a condition performs Jumu'ah, it is valid (i.e., fulfills the obligation of Zuhr). The authority weight of this ruling is from later Hanafi works (fatawa mutakhkhirin), as the text is a commentary based on classical sources.

Key Terms
جمعہ (Jumu'ah): Friday congregational prayer performed in place of Zuhr.
فرض عین (fard 'ayn): Individual obligation incumbent on every qualified Muslim.
شرط (shart): Condition that must exist for obligation or validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn according to this passage?
A) Being male
B) Being free
C) Being a resident of a city
D) Being able to walk without a limp

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only when all seven conditions are met; a missing condition removes the obligation but not the validity if performed.

beginner
7 min
Six Conditions for Jumu'ah Being Valid
Lists conditions for validity and congregation requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for Jumu'ah being valid (sahih) and recognise the requirement of a congregation of three besides the imam.

Core Idea
For Jumu'ah to be valid, six conditions must be present; without them, the prayer is not accepted as Jumu'ah and must be prayed as Zuhr.

The previous lesson covered conditions for obligation; this lesson addresses conditions for validity. Even if a person is obligated, the Jumu'ah prayer itself has its own prerequisites. The passage lists six conditions that must be fulfilled for the prayer to be valid. Additionally, a congregation of at least three persons besides the imam is required. Understanding these conditions ensures that the Jumu'ah performed is legally sound.

Guided Path
1
List the six conditions for validity
From the passage, extract the six conditions: being in a city or its outskirts, presence of the sultan or his deputy, time of Zuhr, a sermon before the prayer with intention of Jumu'ah, presence of at least one person from the obligated group to hear the sermon, and general permission.
These are listed after 'اور جمعہ صحیح ہونے کے لئے چھ چیزیں شرط ہیں'.
2
Identify the congregation requirement
The passage adds a separate condition: a congregation of three besides the imam, regardless of their status (slaves, travelers, etc.).
This is given after the six conditions, marked with stars.
3
Explain the significance of each condition
Briefly explain why each condition matters: city/jurisdiction ensures community, ruler ensures authority, time ensures proper sequence, sermon is distinctive, presence ensures audience, permission avoids anarchy.
Some conditions are practical, some symbolic.
4
Distinguish between obligation and validity conditions
Compare the two sets: obligation conditions relate to the individual, validity conditions relate to the prayer itself. A person may be obligated but the prayer may be invalid if validity conditions are not met (e.g., no sermon).
The passage emphasizes this distinction implicitly.

رسول الله لا يقول : على أعواد منبره (( لينتهين أقوام عن دعهم الجمعات ، أو ليختمن الله على قلوبهم ، ثم ليكونن من الغافلين - (مسلم شريف، باب التغلیظ فی ترک الجمعة ، ص ۱۳۴۷، نمبر ۲۰۰۲۸۶۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جمعہ پڑھنا بہت ضروری ہے۔ ترجمه : ۷۷۸) جمعہ کی نماز اس پر فرض عین ہے جس میں سات شرطیں جمع ہوں ۔ [۱] مذکر ہو۔ [۲]۲ آزاد ہو۔ [۳] شہر میں یا اس کی حد میں اصبح روایت میں مقیم ہو ۔ [۴] تندرست ہو۔
تشریح : یہ سات شرطیں پائی جائیں تو اس پر جمعہ کی نماز فرض ہے، اور اگر ان میں سے ایک بھی کم ہو جائے تو اس فرض نہیں البتہ پڑھ لے تو ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ [1] پہلی شرط ہے کہ مرد ہو چنانچہ عورت پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔[۲] دوسری شرط ہے کہ آزاد ہو، غلام پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ [۳] تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ شہر یا اس کی حدود میں مقیم ہو، چنانچہ مسافر پر ، اور دیہاتی پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ (۴) اور چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ تندرست ہو چنانچہ بیمار پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے، البتہ یہ لوگ پڑھ لیں تو ادا ہو جائے گا۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن طارق بن شهاب عن النبى الله الله قال الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة الا اربعة عبد مملوک او امرأة او صبى او مريض (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة للملوك والمرأة ،ص۱۶۲، نمبر ۱۰۶۷) دارقطنی میں اومسافر، کا لفظ بھی ہے ( دار قطنی ، باب من تجب علیہ الجمعہ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳ نمبر۱۵۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام، عورت، بچہ اور بیمار پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔
ترجمه : (۷۷۹) [۵] ظالم سے امن ہو ۔ [۶] دونوں آنکھیں سلامت ہوں ۔ [2] دونوں پاؤں سلامت ہوں۔ تشریح : پانچویں شرط یہ ہے کہ ظالم سے امن ہو چنانچہ اگر شہر میں ہنگامہ، جس سے جان کا خطرہ ہو تو جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ دونوں آنکھیں سلامت ہو، چنانچہ نابینا پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ ساتویں شرط یہ ہے کہ دونوں پاؤں سالم ہوں ، چنانچہ اپاہج پر جمعہ
واجب نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) امن اور ا پانچ کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے . عن الحسن قال ليس على الخائف و لا على العبد يخدم أهـلـه و لا عـلـى ولى الجنازة و لا على الاعمى اذا لم يجد قائدا الجمعة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من رخص في ترک الجمعۃ ، ج اول ،ص ۴۷۹، نمبر ۵۵۲۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جہاں امن نہ ہو، اور غلام اور نا بینا کو مسجد تک لیجانے والا نہ ہو تو اس پر جمعہ نہیں ہے۔ (۲) یہ لوگ جمعہ پڑھے تو ہو جائے گا اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن الحسن قال ان جمعن مع الامام اجز أهن من صلوة الامام. مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ،۳۴۰ المرأة تشهد الجمعة اتجزيها صلوۃ الامام ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۵۵۶
Chapter of Friday. Conditions for Jumu'ah: On whom seven conditions are found, Jumu'ah prayer is fard 'ayn: male, free, residing in a city or its boundary according to the more sound narration, healthy, safe from an oppressor, both eyes sound, both feet sound. For Jumu'ah to be valid, six things are conditions: city or its outskirts, sultan or his deputy, time of Zuhr (so before Zuhr Jumu'ah is not valid), a sermon before it with intention of Jumu'ah, presence of one person from those for whom Jumu'ah is valid to hear the sermon, general permission. And congregation of three besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. Note: Jumu'ah is wajib on city dwellers, first established in Madinah. Proof: Quran 62:9. Also hadith from Muslim. Translation: (778) Jumu'ah prayer is fard 'ayn for one in whom seven conditions combine: [1] male, [2] free, [3] residing in city or its boundary, [4] healthy, [5] safe from oppressor, [6] both eyes sound, [7] both feet sound. Commentary: If these seven are found, Jumu'ah is fard; if one is missing, it is not fard but if performed it is valid. First condition: male, so not wajib on women. Second: free, not on slaves. Third: residing, not on traveler or villager. Fourth: healthy, not on sick. Proof: Hadith from Abu Dawood: Jumu'ah is a right wajib on every Muslim except four: slave, woman, child, sick. In Darqutni: or traveler. Fifth: safe from oppressor, so if turmoil dangerous, not wajib. Both eyes sound, so blind not wajib. Both feet sound, so crippled not wajib. Proof: Athar from Hasan: Jumu'ah is not on the fearful, the slave serving his family, the one accompanying a funeral, the blind without guide. (2) If they pray Jumu'ah, it is valid: Athar from Hasan: If they pray with imam, it suffices them from Zuhr.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by listing seven conditions for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn: male, free, settled in a city (muqeem), healthy, safe from an oppressor, having both eyes, and both feet. Then it lists six conditions for Jumu'ah to be valid: city or outskirts, presence of ruler or deputy, time of Zuhr, a sermon before the prayer, presence of at least one person from those obligated to hear the sermon, and general permission. It further states that a congregation of three besides the imam is required for validity. The text provides proofs from the Quran (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) and multiple hadith, including from Muslim, Abu Dawood, and Darqutni, establishing the obligation and specifying exemptions. The commentary explains each condition and notes that if a person lacking a condition performs Jumu'ah, it is valid (i.e., fulfills the obligation of Zuhr). The authority weight of this ruling is from later Hanafi works (fatawa mutakhkhirin), as the text is a commentary based on classical sources.

Key Terms
جمعہ (Jumu'ah): Friday congregational prayer performed in place of Zuhr.
شرط (shart): Condition that must exist for obligation or validity.
خطبہ (khutbah): Sermon delivered before Jumu'ah prayer, a condition for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for Jumu'ah to be valid according to this passage?
A) The prayer must be in a city or its outskirts.
B) The imam must be a scholar of high rank.
C) A sermon must be delivered before the prayer.
D) At least one person must hear the sermon.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is valid only when all six conditions and a congregation of three besides the imam are present; missing any invalidates the Jumu'ah.

Salah — Prayer
