Seven Conditions for Jumu'ah Obligation
Listing seven conditions for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn and state the ruling when any condition is missing.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only when seven conditions are present; absence of any condition lifts the obligation.

Jumu'ah prayer is a weekly obligation, but it is not incumbent upon every Muslim unconditionally. The Hanafi school specifies seven conditions that must be met for Jumu'ah to be fard 'ayn. This lesson will walk through those conditions and the evidence supporting them, clarifying who is exempt and what happens if an exempt person prays anyway.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage rules Jumu'ah as fard 'ayn (individual obligation) for those meeting the conditions.
Fard 'ayn means each qualified individual must perform it; it is not a communal obligation.
2
List the seven conditions
Extract the seven conditions from the text: masculinity, freedom, residence in a city or its suburbs, health, safety from oppressor, sound eyesight, sound feet.
The Urdu commentary clarifies the corrupted Arabic list.
3
Understand the legal effect of missing a condition
If any condition is absent, the obligation of Jumu'ah drops; however, if the person prays it, the prayer is valid and counts.
This is an important nuance: obligation vs. validity.
4
Examine the primary proof (hadith)
The hadith from Tariq ibn Shihab explicitly exempts four categories: slave, woman, child, and sick person. This indicates that others are obligated.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
5
Consider additional evidence (athar)
The athar from Hasan al-Basri adds the fearful and the blind (without a guide) to the exempted categories, reinforcing the conditions of safety and eyesight.
This athar is a saying of a tabi'i, used as supporting evidence.

Source Text

باب الجمعة
(۷۷۸) صــلــوـة الـجمعة فرض عين على من اجتمع فيه سبعة شرائط. الذكورة والحرية والاقامة في مصر او فيما هو داخل في حد الاقامة فيها فى الاصح والصحة (۷۹) والامن من ظالم وسلامة رسول الله لا يقول : على أعواد منبره (( لينتهين أقوام عن دعهم الجمعات ، أو ليختمن الله على قلوبهم ، ثم ليكونن من الغافلين - (مسلم شريف، باب التغلیظ فی ترک الجمعة ، ص ۱۳۴۷، نمبر ۲۰۰۲۸۶۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جمعہ پڑھنا بہت ضروری ہے۔ ترجمه : ۷۷۸) جمعہ کی نماز اس پر فرض عین ہے جس میں سات شرطیں جمع ہوں ۔ [۱] مذکر ہو۔ [۲]۲ آزاد ہو۔ [۳] شہر میں یا اس کی حد میں اصبح روایت میں مقیم ہو ۔ [۴] تندرست ہو۔
تشریح : یہ سات شرطیں پائی جائیں تو اس پر جمعہ کی نماز فرض ہے، اور اگر ان میں سے ایک بھی کم ہو جائے تو اس فرض نہیں البتہ پڑھ لے تو ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ [1] پہلی شرط ہے کہ مرد ہو چنانچہ عورت پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔[۲] دوسری شرط ہے کہ آزاد ہو، غلام پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ [۳] تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ شہر یا اس کی حدود میں مقیم ہو، چنانچہ مسافر پر ، اور دیہاتی پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ (۴) اور چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ تندرست ہو چنانچہ بیمار پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے، البتہ یہ لوگ پڑھ لیں تو ادا ہو جائے گا۔

وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن طارق بن شهاب عن النبى الله الله قال الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة الا اربعة عبد مملوک او امرأة او صبى او مريض (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة للملوك والمرأة ،ص۱۶۲، نمبر ۱۰۶۷) دارقطنی میں اومسافر، کا لفظ بھی ہے ( دار قطنی ، باب من تجب علیہ الجمعہ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳ نمبر۱۵۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام، عورت، بچہ اور بیمار پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔
ترجمه : (۷۷۹) [۵] ظالم سے امن ہو ۔ [۶] دونوں آنکھیں سلامت ہوں ۔ [2] دونوں پاؤں سلامت ہوں۔ تشریح : پانچویں شرط یہ ہے کہ ظالم سے امن ہو چنانچہ اگر شہر میں ہنگامہ، جس سے جان کا خطرہ ہو تو جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ دونوں آنکھیں سلامت ہو، چنانچہ نابینا پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ ساتویں شرط یہ ہے کہ دونوں پاؤں سالم ہوں ، چنانچہ اپاہج پر جمعہ
واجب نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) امن اور ا پانچ کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے . عن الحسن قال ليس على الخائف و لا على العبد يخدم أهـلـه و لا عـلـى ولى الجنازة و لا على الاعمى اذا لم يجد قائدا الجمعة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من رخص في ترک الجمعۃ ، ج اول ،ص ۴۷۹، نمبر ۵۵۲۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جہاں امن نہ ہو، اور غلام اور نا بینا کو مسجد تک لیجانے والا نہ ہو تو اس پر جمعہ نہیں ہے۔ (۲) یہ لوگ جمعہ پڑھے تو ہو جائے گا اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن الحسن قال ان جمعن مع الامام اجز أهن من صلوة الامام. مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ،۳۴۰ المرأة تشهد الجمعة اتجزيها صلوۃ الامام ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۵۵۶)
(778) Prayer of Friday is individual obligation on whom seven conditions are present: masculinity, freedom, residence in a city or within its boundary in the soundest view, health, safety from an oppressor, soundness of both eyes, soundness of both feet. The Prophet said: 'People must cease neglecting Friday prayers, or Allah will seal their hearts, then they will be among the heedless.' Translation: Friday prayer is individual obligation on one who has seven conditions: male, free, resident in a city or its boundary, healthy, safe from oppressor, both eyes intact, both feet intact. Explanation: If these seven conditions exist, Friday prayer is obligatory; if even one is missing, it is not obligatory, but if they pray, it is valid. Evidence: Hadith from Tariq ibn Shihab: 'Friday is a due obligation on every Muslim in congregation, except four: an owned slave, a woman, a child, and a sick person.' (779) Safety from oppressor, soundness of both eyes, soundness of both feet. Explanation: Fifth condition: safety from oppressor; if there is turmoil endangering life, Friday is not obligatory. Sixth: both eyes intact; blind person not obliged. Seventh: both feet sound; cripple not obliged. Evidence: Athar from Hasan al-Basri: 'Friday is not required of the fearful, the slave serving his family, the one accompanying a funeral, nor the blind who cannot find a guide.'
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage details the seven conditions that make Jumu'ah prayer obligatory (wajib or fard 'ayn) upon a Muslim. The ruling is that Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only when these conditions are met; if any condition is absent, the prayer is not obligatory, but if performed, it is valid and suffices. The seven conditions are: being male (thus women are not obligated), being free (slaves are exempt), residing in a city or its suburbs (travelers and villagers are exempt), being healthy (the sick are exempt), being safe from oppressors (those in fear are exempt), having sound eyesight (the blind are exempt), and having sound feet (the crippled are exempt). The passage then provides proofs: a hadith from the Prophet listing exempted categories, and an athar from Hasan al-Basri adding the fearful and blind. Note that the Arabic text in the OCR is severely garbled, but the Urdu commentary clarifies the correct list.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation that each competent Muslim must perform; if some perform it, others are not absolved.
المصر (al-misr): A city or large town, as opposed to a small village.
الحرية (al-hurriyyah): Freedom, as opposed to being a slave.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): Residence, as opposed to travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following persons is NOT exempt from Jumu'ah obligation?
A) A woman
B) A healthy free adult male residing in a city
C) A slave
D) A sick person

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only when seven conditions are met; otherwise, it is not obligatory but valid if performed.

Validity Condition for Jumu'ah: City Requirement
Stating the first condition for Jumu'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that Jumu'ah must be performed in a city or its outskirts and identify the three pieces of evidence that support this ruling.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in a proper city or its attached outskirts, not in small villages or scattered dwellings.

The Hanafi school holds that Jumu'ah is not valid in every small settlement. This lesson explores the first of six conditions: the requirement that Jumu'ah be held in a city (misr) or its immediate outer area (fina'). The ruling is based on the statement of 'Ali, the practice of the people of Madinah, and the location of the first Jumu'ah after the Prophet's mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The first condition for Jumu'ah validity is that it must be performed in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). This is a shart (condition) – if absent, the prayer is invalid.
The Hanafi definition of misr includes permanent settlement, paved roads, a market, and a qadi.
2
Recognize the first evidence
The author cites the statement of 'Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah and no Takbir al-Tashriq except in a comprehensive city (misr jami').' The explicit negation (لا) indicates prohibition of Jumu'ah in non-cities.
This is reported in Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Analyze the second evidence
The practice of the people of Madinah: they would come from the Awali (villages on the outskirts) to the city for Jumu'ah, as reported in a hadith from 'A'ishah. If Jumu'ah were valid in villages, it would have been held there.
The hadith shows that people came covered in dust and sweat, implying they traveled to the city.
4
Examine the third evidence
The first Jumu'ah after the one in the Prophet's mosque was held in Jawathi (a fortress with a city) in Bahrain. If Jumu'ah were permissible in villages, it would have been held earlier in other conquered villages.
This is reported by Ibn Abbas in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.

Source Text

(۷۸۰) ويشترط لصحتها ستة اشياء. المصر او فناؤه
تشریح : جمعہ صحیح ہونے کے لئے پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ شہر ہو ، یا ہر کا فناء ہو۔ وجه : (۱) حضرت علی کا قول کا ہے۔ عن علی قال لا جمعة ولا تشريق الا في مصر جامع ، وكان يعد الامصار البصرة والكوفة والمدينة والبحرين (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب القرى الصغارج ثالث ص ۰ ۷ نمبر ۵۱۹ / مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۳۳۱ من قال لا جمعة ولا تشریق الا فی مصر جامع ، ج اول ص ۴۳۹، نمبر ۵۰۵۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بڑے شہر میں جمعہ جائز ہے (۲) اس کی تائید اس بات سے ہوتی ہے کہ مدینہ کے عوالی میں جمعہ نہیں ہوتا تھا، اگر گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ہوتا تو عوالی میں ضرور ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة زوج النبي الله قالت كان الناس ينتابون الجمعة من منازلهم والعوالي فيأتون في الغبار فيصبهم الغبار والعرق ( بخاری شریف، باب من این توتی الجمعة وعلى من تجب ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۱۹۰۲ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب من تحجب علیہ الجمعة ، ص ۱۵۸ نمبر ۱۰۵۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عوالی کے گاؤں میں جمعہ نہیں ہوتا تھا۔صرف مدینہ جیسے شہر میں جمعہ ہوتا تھا (۳) مدینہ طیبہ کے بعد پہلی مرتبہ جوائی جیسے قلعہ میں نماز جمعہ ہوئی ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال ان اول جمعة جمعت بعد جمعة في مسجد رسول الله عله في مسجد عبد القيس بجوالي من البحرين. (بخاری شریف ، باب الجمعة في القرى والمدن ص ۱۲۲ نمبر ۸۹۲/ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الجمعۃ فی القری ص ۱۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسجد عبد القیس میں مدینہ کے بعد پہلی مرتبہ جمعہ ہوا ہے جو بحرین میں تھی ۔ اگر گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ہوتا تو بحرین کے فتح سے پہلے کتنے گاؤں فتح ہو گئے تھے ان میں جمعہ کیوں نہیں ہوا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ شہر میں جمعہ جائز ہے گاؤں میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ نوٹ : جوانی کے بارے میں لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ وہ ایک قلعہ کا نام ہے اور وہاں شہر تھا۔ فائدہ: پانچ قسم کی بستیاں ہوتیں ہیں [1] خیمے والے، جو پانی کی تلاش میں صحراوں میں ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ منتقل ہوتے رہتے ہیں ۔ ان خیموں میں کسی امام کے یہاں جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اینٹ پتھر کے مکانات تو ہوں لیکن مجتمع نہ ہوں بکھرے ہوئے ہوں ، ایک مکان یہاں ہے تو دوسرا مکان کافی دوری پر ہے ۔ ان میں بھی کسی کے یہاں جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے ۔ (۳) تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اینٹ پتھر کے مکانات ہوں جسکی وجہ سے انکے رہنے والے ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ منتقل نہ ہو
(780) Six things are conditions for its validity: the city or its outskirts. Explanation: The first condition for validity is that it be a city or its surroundings. Evidence: (1) Statement of Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah and no Takbir al-Tashriq except in a comprehensive city.' He counted Basra, Kufa, Madinah, and Bahrain as cities. This indicates Jumu'ah is valid in large cities. (2) It is supported by the fact that Jumu'ah was not held in the villages (Awali) of Madinah; if it were valid in villages, it would have been held there. Hadith from A'ishah: 'People would come for Jumu'ah from their houses and the Awali, covered in dust and sweat.' This indicates that Jumu'ah was not held in the Awali villages. (3) The first Jumu'ah after Madinah was held in the fortress of Jawathi. Hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah held after the one in the Prophet's Mosque was in the mosque of Abd al-Qays in Jawathi, Bahrain.' If Jumu'ah were valid in villages, it would have been held in many villages before that. Note: Jawathi is said to be a fortress with a city. Benefit: There are five types of settlements: (1) Tent-dwellers who move seeking water – Jumu'ah is not valid among them. (2) Brick houses but scattered far apart – Jumu'ah is not valid. (3) Brick houses such that the inhabitants do not move from one place to another – ...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage discusses the first condition for the validity of Jumu'ah: that it be performed in a city (misr) or its immediate outskirts (fina'). The author provides three pieces of evidence: first, the statement of Ali that Jumu'ah is only in a 'comprehensive city' (misr jami'), listing Basra, Kufa, Madinah, and Bahrain as examples. Second, the practice of the people of Madinah: they would come from the Awali (villages) to the city for Jumu'ah, proving Jumu'ah was not held in the villages. Third, the first Jumu'ah after the establishment of the Prophet's mosque was in Jawathi, a fortress with a city, indicating that Jumu'ah is restricted to intentionally built settlements like cities. The passage then begins a beneficial note classifying five types of settlements; the text is cut off, but the first two types are clearly defined: nomadic tent-dwellers and scattered brick houses are not valid places for Jumu'ah. The third type, dense brick houses where residents have fixed abodes, is where Jumu'ah becomes valid, but the full explanation is incomplete in our text.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A large city that is permanently settled and has a judge and markets; the first condition for Jumu'ah validity.
الفناء (al-fina'): The immediate outskirts of a city that are functionally part of it, within the same urban area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which evidence does the author use to prove that Jumu'ah is not valid in villages?
A) A hadith from Ibn Abbas about the first Jumu'ah in Jawathi
B) The statement of Ali that Jumu'ah is only in a comprehensive city
C) The practice that people came from the Awali to Madinah for Jumu'ah
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina') according to the Hanafi school, based on the statement of 'Ali and early practice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Original Hanafi Position: Jumu'ah Requires a City or Its Outskirts
Stating the city condition for Jumu'ah with textual evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for Jumu'ah validity according to the Hanafi school and cite the primary textual evidences.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in a city or its outskirts — villages do not qualify.

The Hanafi school holds that for Jumu'ah to be valid, it must be performed in a city (misr) or its immediate precincts (fina'). This lesson examines the three key evidences from the sayings and practice of the Companions that establish this condition. Understanding these proofs is essential for grasping the school's rigor in preserving the urban character of the Friday congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The text states that the first of six conditions for Jumu'ah validity is that it be held in a misr (city) or its fina' (outskirts). Identify this from the Arabic: "المصر او فناؤه".
This is a shart (condition), not a rukn.
2
Examine the saying of Ali
The passage quotes Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah nor tashriq except in a comprehensive city.' He listed Basra, Kufa, Medina, and Bahrain as examples. Understand that this is a qawl sahabi (Companion's statement) serving as dalil.
The Hanafis consider qawl sahabi as a valid source when not contradicted.
3
Analyze the practice of the Awali
The hadith of Aisha shows people from the outskirts (Awali) came into Medina for Jumu'ah, implying no Jumu'ah was held in their villages. This is istidlal bi al-fi'l (inference from practice).
If Jumu'ah were allowed in villages, they would have held it there.
4
Consider the first Jumu'ah after Medina
The hadith of Ibn Abbas states that the first Jumu'ah after Medina was at Juatha. The Hanafis interpret Juatha as a fort/city, not a village. This supports the city condition.
Opponents say Juatha was a village; this is the point of dispute.
5
Conclude the original Hanafi ruling
Based on these evidences, the original Hanafi ruling is that Jumu'ah is not valid in a village; it must be in a city (misr) or its fina'.
This is the position found in Zahir al-Riwayah.

، باب الجمعۃ فی القری ص ۶۰ نمبر ۰۶۸ ار بخاری شریف ، باب وفد عبد القيس ، ص ۷۴۱ ، نمبر ۴۳۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جوانی بحرین کے گاؤں کا نام ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ..... ہے۔(۳) حدثني عبد الرحمن بن کعب بن مالک . فلما سمع الاذان بالجمعة استغفر له فقلت : يا أبتاه أرأيت استغفارك لأسعد بن زرارة كلما سمعت الأذان بالجمعة فقال : أى بنى كان اسعد أول من صل الله علہ جمع بنـا في المدينة قبل مقدم رسول الله عله في هزم من حرة بنى بياضة في نقيع يقال له الخضمات ، قلت و كم أنتم يومئذ قال : أربعون رجلا . (سنن بیہقی، باب العدد الذین اذا کا نوافی قریة وجبت ميهم الجمعة، ج ثالث، ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۵۶۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مدینے میں پہلا جمعہ ہوا تو کل چالیس آدمی تھے ۔ (۴) ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث بھی ہے۔ عن ام عبد الله الدوسية قالت سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول الجمعة واجبة على اهل كل قرية وان لم يكونوا الا ثلاثة ورابعهم امامهم (دارقطنی ، باب الجمعہ علی اہل القرية ج ثانی ص نے نمبر ۱۵۷۸ رسن بیہقی ، باب العد والذین اذا کانوا فی قریة وجبت عليهم الجمعة ، ج ثالث ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۵۶۱۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گاؤں میں جمعہ واجب ہے چاہے اس گاؤں میں چار ہی آدمی کیوں نہ ہو (۵) عن ابی اما مة ان النبى الله قال على الخمسين جمعة ليس فيما دون ذلک (دار قطنی ، ذکر العدد فی الجمعة ج ثانی ص نمبر ۱۵۶۴ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الجمعۃ فی القری ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۹) اس حدیث
Chapter of Jumu'ah. The two eyes and safety of the feet. (780) Six things are required for its validity: the city or its outskirts. (3) From al-Zuhri: I asked him about a traveler who passes through a village and stays there on Friday. He said: If he hears the adhan, he should attend Jumu'ah. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this effect it is understood that if these people attend Jumu'ah, then the Zuhr prayer is performed. Translation: (780) And for Jumu'ah to be valid, six things are conditions: [1] A city or its outskirts. Explanation: The first condition for the validity of Jumu'ah is that it be a city or its precincts. Evidence: (1) The saying of Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah nor tashriq except in a comprehensive city, and he considered the cities of Basra, Kufa, Medina, and Bahrain.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this effect it is understood that Jumu'ah is permissible in a big city. (2) This is supported by the fact that Jumu'ah was not held in the 'Awali of Medina. If Jumu'ah were permissible in a village, it should have been held in the 'Awali. The hadith is: From Aisha, wife of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, she said: 'People used to come for Jumu'ah from their homes and the 'Awali, and they would come in dust and be covered with dust and sweat.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that Jumu'ah was not held in the villages of 'Awali, only in a city like Medina. (3) After Medina, the first Jumu'ah was held in a fort like Juatha. The hadith is: From Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah held after the Jumu'ah in the mosque of the Messenger of God was in the mosque of Abd al-Qays at Juatha in Bahrain.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This effect mentions that Jumu'ah was held in the mosque of Abd al-Qays, which was in Bahrain, after Medina. If Jumu'ah were permissible in a village, then before the conquest of Bahrain many villages had been conquered; why was Jumu'ah not held in them? From this it is understood that Jumu'ah is permissible in a city, not in a village. Note: Regarding Juatha, people say it is the name of a fort and there was a city there. Benefit: There are five types of settlements: [1] Tent-dwellers, who move from place to place in deserts seeking water. Jumu'ah is not permissible in their tents according to any imam. [2] Second type: There are brick and stone houses, but they are not congregated; they are scattered, one house here, another far away. In these also Jumu'ah is not permissible according to anyone. (3) Third type: There are brick and stone houses such that their residents cannot move from one place to another, and the population is congregated, not scattered. Then if there are forty people, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, Jumu'ah is permissible. [4] Fourth type: It is not a city but a large habitation called a qasbah. According to the Hanafis, Jumu'ah is not permissible in it. However, nowadays they give a fatwa to establish Jumu'ah in it, one based on the previous hadith, and another reason is that villagers do not pray anything except Jumu'ah and the two Eids; if concession is not given to pray Jumu'ah, then no symbol of Islam would remain among them. Another reason is that these people insist on praying Jumu'ah, so Hanafi scholars also give a fatwa for Jumu'ah in a qasbah. In our villages of Jharkhand, practice is upon this. [5] Fifth type: It is a city, then by consensus Jumu'ah is permissible. Evidence: (1) A small village whose houses are congregated, Jumu'ah is permissible in it. For this there is a saying of a Tabi'i: From Amr ibn Dinar: 'We heard that there is no Jumu'ah except in a congregated village.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Here 'congregated village' means that the houses of the village are not scattered like desert people but are congregated like village houses. Then Jumu'ah is permissible in it. (2) In this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah held in Islam after the Jumu'ah held in the mosque of the Messenger of God in Medina was the Jumu'ah held at Juatha, a village of Bahrain.' (Abu Dawud, Bukhari) In this hadith, Juatha is a village of Bahrain. From this it is understood that Jumu'ah is permissible in a village. (3) Abd al-Rahman ibn Kab ibn Malik narrated: 'When he heard the adhan for Jumu'ah, he asked forgiveness for him. I said: O father, do you ask forgiveness for As'ad ibn Zurara every time you hear the adhan for Jumu'ah? He said: O my son, As'ad was the first to gather us for Jumu'ah in Medina before the arrival of the Messenger of God in a hollow of the Harra of Bani Bayadah in a place called al-Khadamat. I said: How many were you that day? He said: Forty men.' (Sunan Bayhaqi) This hadith states that the first Jumu'ah in Medina had forty men. (4) Their evidence is also this hadith: From Umm Abdullah al-Dawsiyyah: 'I heard the Messenger of God say: Jumu'ah is obligatory on the people of every village, even if they are only three and their imam is the fourth.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi) This hadith says that Jumu'ah is obligatory in a village even if there are only four people in that village. (5) From Abu Umamah that the Prophet said: 'Upon fifty is Jumu'ah, not for what is less than that.' (Darqutni, Abu Dawud) This hadith...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Jumu'ah (Friday prayer) by stating a key condition for its validity: the prayer must be held in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). The author begins by listing six conditions for validity, the first being the city condition. He then provides multiple evidences from the practices of the Companions and hadith. The evidence includes the saying of Ali that Jumu'ah and tashriq (Eid prayer) are only in a comprehensive city, the fact that the people of the outskirts (Awali) of Medina would come into the city for Jumu'ah rather than holding it in their villages, and the first Jumu'ah after Medina being at Juatha, which is described as a fort or city. The author then categorizes settlements into five types: 1) tent-dwellers (no Jumu'ah), 2) scattered stone houses (no Jumu'ah), 3) congregated stone houses with forty residents (Shafi'i allows, Hanafi still requires a city), 4) a large town (qasbah) which is not a city (Hanafi originally disallows but later fatwa allows due to necessity), and 5) a city (consensus allows). The author then presents the opposing view that Jumu'ah can be held in a small congregated village, citing the saying of Amr ibn Dinar, the hadith of Juatha being a village, the hadith of the first Jumu'ah in Medina with forty men, the hadith making Jumu'ah obligatory on a village even with only four people, and the hadith 'upon fifty is Jumu'ah' indicating a minimum number. The passage thus presents both the strict Hanafi position and the later practical fatwa, acknowledging the dispute with Shafi'i and the adjustment for necessity.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or large urban settlement with a permanent population and administrative functions; a place where congregational prayers like Jumu'ah are valid.
فناء (finaa): The outskirts or precincts of a city that are considered part of the city for the purpose of Jumu'ah validity.
قرى (qura): Villages or small rural settlements; the text discusses whether Jumu'ah is valid in them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a piece of evidence cited in the passage for the condition of city for Jumu'ah?
A) The saying of Ali that Jumu'ah is only in a comprehensive city
B) The practice of the Awali coming to Medina for Jumu'ah
C) The hadith that the first Jumu'ah after Medina was at Juatha
D) The hadith that Jumu'ah is obligatory on the people of every village

Key Takeaway
The original Hanafi school requires Jumu'ah to be held in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'); villages do not qualify.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Later Fatwa and the Shafi'i Dispute on Jumu'ah in Villages
Discussing the dispute and later practical concession for Jumu'ah in qasbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why later Hanafi scholars allowed Jumu'ah in a qasbah and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on Jumu'ah in villages.

Core Idea
Necessity overrides the strict city condition: later Hanafi fatwa permits Jumu'ah in large towns to preserve the symbol of Islam.

While the original Hanafi position restricts Jumu'ah to cities, later scholars relaxed this for large villages (qasbah) due to practical necessity. This lesson examines the Shafi'i view that allows Jumu'ah in any congregated village with forty men, the Hanafi response, and the rationales behind the later fatwa. Understanding this evolution is key to appreciating how fiqh adapts to changing circumstances without abandoning principles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the five settlement types
The text categorizes settlements into five types: tents (no Jumu'ah), scattered houses (no Jumu'ah), congregated village (Shafi'i allows with 40), qasbah (large village, Hanafi originally no), and city (consensus). Identify the defining features of each.
Qasbah is the focus of the later fatwa.
2
Examine the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i allows Jumu'ah in any village with forty resident men. His evidence includes: the hadith of Ibn Abbas that Juatha was a village, the hadith of the first Jumu'ah in Medina with forty men, the hadith making Jumu'ah obligatory even on a village of four, and the hadith 'upon fifty is Jumu'ah'.
These hadith are from the passage.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that Juatha was a fort/city, not a village; the forty-man hadith refers to Medina, which is a city; the hadith of obligation on a village is considered weak or overridden by the practice of the Companions; and the 'fifty' hadith specifies a number, not a settlement type.
The Hanafis prioritize the practice of the Companions over isolated hadith.
4
Understand the later Hanafi fatwa
Despite the original position, later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) gave a fatwa allowing Jumu'ah in a qasbah due to two reasons: (1) the hadith of the first Jumu'ah at Juatha can be interpreted as a village; (2) necessity: villagers only pray Jumu'ah and Eid; if Jumu'ah is not allowed, no Islamic symbol remains. The practice in Jharkhand follows this fatwa.
This is a clear example of fatwa changing due to maqasid (higher objectives) and necessity.

باب الجمعة العينين وسلامة الرّجلين. (۷۸۰) ويشترط لصحتها ستة اشياء. المصر او فناؤه (۳) عن الزهري قال سألته عن المسافر يمر بقرية فينزل فيها يوم الجمعة قال اذا سمع الاذان فليشهد الجمعة (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من تجب علیہ الجمعة ص ۷۴ نمبر ۵۲۱۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ لوگ جمعہ میں حاضر ہو جائے تو ظہر کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ ترجمه : (۷۸۰) اور جمعہ صحیح ہونے کے لئے چھ چیزیں شرط ہیں: [1] شہر یا فتاء شہر ۔ تشریح : جمعہ صحیح ہونے کے لئے پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ شہر ہو ، یا ہر کا فناء ہو۔ وجه : (۱) حضرت علی کا قول کا ہے۔ عن علی قال لا جمعة ولا تشريق الا في مصر جامع ، وكان يعد الامصار البصرة والكوفة والمدينة والبحرين (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب القرى الصغارج ثالث ص ۰ ۷ نمبر ۵۱۹ / مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۳۳۱ من قال لا جمعة ولا تشریق الا فی مصر جامع ، ج اول ص ۴۳۹، نمبر ۵۰۵۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بڑے شہر میں جمعہ جائز ہے (۲) اس کی تائید اس بات سے ہوتی ہے کہ مدینہ کے عوالی میں جمعہ نہیں ہوتا تھا، اگر گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ہوتا تو عوالی میں ضرور ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة زوج النبي الله قالت كان الناس ينتابون الجمعة من منازلهم والعوالي فيأتون في الغبار فيصبهم الغبار والعرق ( بخاری شریف، باب من این توتی الجمعة وعلى من تجب ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۱۹۰۲ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب من تحجب علیہ الجمعة ، ص ۱۵۸ نمبر ۱۰۵۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عوالی کے گاؤں میں جمعہ نہیں ہوتا تھا۔صرف مدینہ جیسے شہر میں جمعہ ہوتا تھا (۳) مدینہ طیبہ کے بعد پہلی مرتبہ جوائی جیسے قلعہ میں نماز جمعہ ہوئی ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال ان اول جمعة جمعت بعد جمعة في مسجد رسول الله عله في مسجد عبد القيس بجوالي من البحرين. (بخاری شریف ، باب الجمعة في القرى والمدن ص ۱۲۲ نمبر ۸۹۲/ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الجمعۃ فی القری ص ۱۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسجد عبد القیس میں مدینہ کے بعد پہلی مرتبہ جمعہ ہوا ہے جو بحرین میں تھی ۔ اگر گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ہوتا تو بحرین کے فتح سے پہلے کتنے گاؤں فتح ہو گئے تھے ان میں جمعہ کیوں نہیں ہوا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ شہر میں جمعہ جائز ہے گاؤں میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ نوٹ : جوانی کے بارے میں لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ وہ ایک قلعہ کا نام ہے اور وہاں شہر تھا۔ فائدہ: پانچ قسم کی بستیاں ہوتیں ہیں [1] خیمے والے، جو پانی کی تلاش میں صحراوں میں ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ منتقل ہوتے رہتے ہیں ۔ ان خیموں میں کسی امام الرحمن بن کعب بن مالک . فلما سمع الاذان بالجمعة استغفر له فقلت : يا أبتاه أرأيت استغفارك لأسعد بن زرارة كلما سمعت الأذان بالجمعة فقال : أى بنى كان اسعد أول من صل الله علہ جمع بنـا في المدينة قبل مقدم رسول الله عله في هزم من حرة بنى بياضة في نقيع يقال له الخضمات ، قلت و كم أنتم يومئذ قال : أربعون رجلا . (سنن بیہقی، باب العدد الذین اذا کا نوافی قریة وجبت ميهم الجمعة، ج ثالث، ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۵۶۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مدینے میں پہلا جمعہ ہوا تو کل چالیس آدمی تھے ۔ (۴) ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث بھی ہے۔ عن ام عبد الله الدوسية قالت سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول الجمعة واجبة على اهل كل قرية وان لم يكونوا الا ثلاثة ورابعهم امامهم (دارقطنی ، باب الجمعہ علی اہل القرية ج ثانی ص نے نمبر ۱۵۷۸ رسن بیہقی ، باب العد والذین اذا کانوا فی قریة وجبت عليهم الجمعة ، ج ثالث ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۵۶۱۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گاؤں میں جمعہ واجب ہے چاہے اس گاؤں میں چار ہی آدمی کیوں نہ ہو (۵) عن ابی اما مة ان النبى الله قال على الخمسين جمعة ليس فيما دون ذلک (دار قطنی ، ذکر العدد فی الجمعة ج ثانی ص نمبر ۱۵۶۴ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الجمعۃ فی القری ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۹) اس حدیث
Chapter of Jumu'ah. The two eyes and safety of the feet. (780) Six things are required for its validity: the city or its outskirts. (3) From al-Zuhri: I asked him about a traveler who passes through a village and stays there on Friday. He said: If he hears the adhan, he should attend Jumu'ah. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this effect it is understood that if these people attend Jumu'ah, then the Zuhr prayer is performed. Translation: (780) And for Jumu'ah to be valid, six things are conditions: [1] A city or its outskirts. Explanation: The first condition for the validity of Jumu'ah is that it be a city or its precincts. Evidence: (1) The saying of Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah nor tashriq except in a comprehensive city, and he considered the cities of Basra, Kufa, Medina, and Bahrain.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this effect it is understood that Jumu'ah is permissible in a big city. (2) This is supported by the fact that Jumu'ah was not held in the 'Awali of Medina. If Jumu'ah were permissible in a village, it should have been held in the 'Awali. The hadith is: From Aisha, wife of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, she said: 'People used to come for Jumu'ah from their homes and the 'Awali, and they would come in dust and be covered with dust and sweat.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that Jumu'ah was not held in the villages of 'Awali, only in a city like Medina. (3) After Medina, the first Jumu'ah was held in a fort like Juatha. The hadith is: From Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah held after the Jumu'ah in the mosque of the Messenger of God was in the mosque of Abd al-Qays at Juatha in Bahrain.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This effect mentions that Jumu'ah was held in the mosque of Abd al-Qays, which was in Bahrain, after Medina. If Jumu'ah were permissible in a village, then before the conquest of Bahrain many villages had been conquered; why was Jumu'ah not held in them? From this it is understood that Jumu'ah is permissible in a city, not in a village. Note: Regarding Juatha, people say it is the name of a fort and there was a city there. Benefit: There are five types of settlements: [1] Tent-dwellers, who move from place to place in deserts seeking water. Jumu'ah is not permissible in their tents according to any imam. [2] Second type: There are brick and stone houses, but they are not congregated; they are scattered, one house here, another far away. In these also Jumu'ah is not permissible according to anyone. (3) Third type: There are brick and stone houses such that their residents cannot move from one place to another, and the population is congregated, not scattered. Then if there are forty people, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, Jumu'ah is permissible. [4] Fourth type: It is not a city but a large habitation called a qasbah. According to the Hanafis, Jumu'ah is not permissible in it. However, nowadays they give a fatwa to establish Jumu'ah in it, one based on the previous hadith, and another reason is that villagers do not pray anything except Jumu'ah and the two Eids; if concession is not given to pray Jumu'ah, then no symbol of Islam would remain among them. Another reason is that these people insist on praying Jumu'ah, so Hanafi scholars also give a fatwa for Jumu'ah in a qasbah. In our villages of Jharkhand, practice is upon this. [5] Fifth type: It is a city, then by consensus Jumu'ah is permissible. Evidence: (1) A small village whose houses are congregated, Jumu'ah is permissible in it. For this there is a saying of a Tabi'i: From Amr ibn Dinar: 'We heard that there is no Jumu'ah except in a congregated village.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Here 'congregated village' means that the houses of the village are not scattered like desert people but are congregated like village houses. Then Jumu'ah is permissible in it. (2) In this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah held in Islam after the Jumu'ah held in the mosque of the Messenger of God in Medina was the Jumu'ah held at Juatha, a village of Bahrain.' (Abu Dawud, Bukhari) In this hadith, Juatha is a village of Bahrain. From this it is understood that Jumu'ah is permissible in a village. (3) Abd al-Rahman ibn Kab ibn Malik narrated: 'When he heard the adhan for Jumu'ah, he asked forgiveness for him. I said: O father, do you ask forgiveness for As'ad ibn Zurara every time you hear the adhan for Jumu'ah? He said: O my son, As'ad was the first to gather us for Jumu'ah in Medina before the arrival of the Messenger of God in a hollow of the Harra of Bani Bayadah in a place called al-Khadamat. I said: How many were you that day? He said: Forty men.' (Sunan Bayhaqi) This hadith states that the first Jumu'ah in Medina had forty men. (4) Their evidence is also this hadith: From Umm Abdullah al-Dawsiyyah: 'I heard the Messenger of God say: Jumu'ah is obligatory on the people of every village, even if they are only three and their imam is the fourth.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi) This hadith says that Jumu'ah is obligatory in a village even if there are only four people in that village. (5) From Abu Umamah that the Prophet said: 'Upon fifty is Jumu'ah, not for what is less than that.' (Darqutni, Abu Dawud) This hadith...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Jumu'ah (Friday prayer) by stating a key condition for its validity: the prayer must be held in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). The author begins by listing six conditions for validity, the first being the city condition. He then provides multiple evidences from the practices of the Companions and hadith. The evidence includes the saying of Ali that Jumu'ah and tashriq (Eid prayer) are only in a comprehensive city, the fact that the people of the outskirts (Awali) of Medina would come into the city for Jumu'ah rather than holding it in their villages, and the first Jumu'ah after Medina being at Juatha, which is described as a fort or city. The author then categorizes settlements into five types: 1) tent-dwellers (no Jumu'ah), 2) scattered stone houses (no Jumu'ah), 3) congregated stone houses with forty residents (Shafi'i allows, Hanafi still requires a city), 4) a large town (qasbah) which is not a city (Hanafi originally disallows but later fatwa allows due to necessity), and 5) a city (consensus allows). The author then presents the opposing view that Jumu'ah can be held in a small congregated village, citing the saying of Amr ibn Dinar, the hadith of Juatha being a village, the hadith of the first Jumu'ah in Medina with forty men, the hadith making Jumu'ah obligatory on a village even with only four people, and the hadith 'upon fifty is Jumu'ah' indicating a minimum number. The passage thus presents both the strict Hanafi position and the later practical fatwa, acknowledging the dispute with Shafi'i and the adjustment for necessity.

Key Terms
قصبہ (qasbah): A large town or fortified settlement that is larger than a village but not a full city.
جوامع (jawami'): Plural of jamii', meaning comprehensive; used in the phrase 'masjid jamii' (central mosque).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a reason given in the passage for the later Hanafi fatwa allowing Jumu'ah in a qasbah?
A) Based on the hadith that the first Jumu'ah was at Juatha, which some consider a village
B) The villagers insist on praying Jumu'ah
C) There is a Quranic verse specifically permitting Jumu'ah in villages
D) To preserve the symbol of Islam in rural areas

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi fatwa permits Jumu'ah in large villages (qasbah) due to necessity, preserving the Islamic symbol while maintaining the original ruling in principle.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
15 min
The Settlement Condition for Friday Prayer: Original Ruling and Later Fatwa
Discusses the requirement of a city or village for Jumu'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the original Hanafi requirement for the settlement in Jumu'ah and analyze the later fatwa permitting it in qasbahs based on necessity and hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah originally required a city or ruler, but later Hanafi fatwa allows it in large villages to preserve Islamic symbols.

In this passage, we examine a key condition for the validity of Friday prayer: the type of settlement. The Hanafi school historically required a large city (misr) or a town with a ruler, but later scholars issued a fatwa allowing Jumu'ah in qasbahs (large villages) due to practical necessity. This lesson unpacks the classical ruling, the evidence from hadith, and the rationale behind the contemporary fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn on eligible men. The settlement condition is a condition of validity; identify the original Hanafi position and the later fatwa.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites multiple hadith and athar supporting Jumu'ah in villages. Identify each source (e.g., Jawatha hadith, Umm Abdullah hadith, practice of Mus'ab).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For each hadith, determine how it proves the permissibility of Jumu'ah in villages. For example, the Jawatha hadith shows the Prophet's Companions praying Jumu'ah in a village.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i allows Jumu'ah in any village with 40 men. The original Hanafi position is stricter. Understand the basis of each school's argument.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The later Hanafi fatwa adopts a permissive view due to necessity (preserving Islamic symbols) and the hadith evidence. Recognize that this is a mufta bihi position today.

Chapter of Friday Prayer. ... if there is a clustered population, not scattered, and if there are forty men, then according to Imam Shafi'i Jumu'ah is valid. [4] The fourth scenario is that it is not a city but a large settlement called a qasbah; according to the Hanafis, Jumu'ah is not valid there. However, nowadays they give a fatwa allowing Jumu'ah there, firstly based on the previous hadith, and secondly because rural people do not pray anything except Jumu'ah and the two Eids; if Jumu'ah is also not permitted, then no symbol of Islam would remain among them. Thirdly, these people insist on praying Jumu'ah, so Hanafi scholars also give a fatwa for praying Jumu'ah in a qasbah. In our villages of Jharkhand, this is practiced. [5] The fifth scenario is that it is a city, in which Jumu'ah is unanimously valid. Evidence: (1) For a small village with clustered houses, Jumu'ah is valid. This is the statement of a Tabi'i: 'Amr ibn Dinar said: We heard that there is no Jumu'ah except in a clustered village. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on small villages, vol. 3, p. ?, no. 5197). Here 'clustered village' means that the houses of the village are not scattered like desert dwellers but are clustered like the houses of a village. So Jumu'ah is valid there. (2) In this hadith: Ibn 'Abbas said: The first Jumu'ah gathered in Islam after the Jumu'ah gathered in the mosque of the Messenger of Allah in Medina was the Jumu'ah gathered at Jawatha, a village of Bahrain. 'Uthman said: a village of 'Abd al-Qays. (Abu Dawud, chapter on Jumu'ah in a village, p. 60, no. 068; Bukhari, chapter on the delegation of 'Abd al-Qays, p. 741, no. 437). This hadith indicates that Jumu'ah is permissible in a village. (3) 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ka'b ibn Malik narrated: ... He said: As'ad was the first to gather us for Jumu'ah in Medina before the arrival of the Messenger of Allah in a harrah of the Banu Bayadah in a well-known place called al-Khadamat. I said: How many were you that day? He said: Forty men. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the number who, if present in a village, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory on them, vol. 3, p. 252, no. 5605). This hadith indicates that the first Jumu'ah in Medina was with forty men. (4) Another proof is this hadith: Umm 'Abdullah al-Dawsiyya said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Jumu'ah is obligatory on the people of every village, even if there are only three and the fourth is their imam. (Darqutni, chapter on Jumu'ah for the people of a village, vol. 2, p. ?, no. 1578; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, ibid., vol. 3, p. 255, no. 5616). This hadith indicates that Jumu'ah is obligatory in a village even if there are only four men. (5) Abu Umama narrated that the Prophet said: Jumu'ah is upon fifty; there is no Jumu'ah for those less than that. (Darqutni, mention of the number for Jumu'ah, vol. 2, p. ?, no. 1564; Abu Dawud, chapter on Jumu'ah in a village, p. 60, no. 1069). This hadith indicates that when there are fifty men, Jumu'ah should be established. (6) When the Prophet sent Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr to Medina, there were twelve men praying, and he led them in Jumu'ah. The text: It is narrated from al-Zuhri that when the Prophet sent Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr to Medina, he gathered them for Jumu'ah while they were twelve men. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, ibid., vol. 3, p. 255, no. 5617). This effect shows that in Medina itself, Jumu'ah was established with only twelve men, indicating that Jumu'ah is permissible in a village.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion on the first condition for Friday prayer: the type of settlement. The author presents five scenarios (though the first three are implied from context) focusing on the fourth (qasbah/town) and fifth (city). He notes the classical Hanafi position that Jumu'ah is not valid in a qasbah, but gives a contemporary fatwa allowing it due to necessity: rural people otherwise have no congregational symbol of Islam, and they insist on praying. The fifth scenario, a city, is unanimously valid. Then he brings six proofs: (1) The statement of 'Amr ibn Dinar that Jumu'ah is only in a clustered village, which he interprets as houses not scattered. (2) The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas about the first Jumu'ah in Jawatha, a village in Bahrain. (3) The hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ka'b that the first Jumu'ah in Medina had forty men. (4) The hadith of Umm 'Abdullah that Jumu'ah is wajib on every village, even with only four men. (5) The hadith of Abu Umama that Jumu'ah is upon fifty. (6) The practice of Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr leading Jumu'ah with twelve men in Medina. The author uses these to argue that Jumu'ah is permissible in villages, countering the strict Hanafi requirement of a city. The Hanafi school's original ruling required a large city (misr) with a ruler, but this passage shows a later relaxation for smaller settlements to preserve Islamic practice.

Key Terms
قریہ جامعہ (qaryah jāmi‘ah): A village with clustered houses, not scattered like desert dwellings.
قصبہ (qasbah): A large village or town that is not a full city.
جمعہ (jumu‘ah): The Friday congregational prayer, obligatory on men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the original Hanafi ruling regarding Jumu'ah in a qasbah (large town)?
A) Jumu'ah is valid in a qasbah without any conditions.
B) Jumu'ah is not valid in a qasbah, but a later fatwa allows it due to necessity.
C) Jumu'ah is only valid in a qasbah if there are exactly 40 men.
D) Jumu'ah is valid in a qasbah only according to Imam Shafi'i.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi condition of settlement for Jumu'ah has evolved from a strict requirement of a city with a ruler to a more permissive fatwa allowing Jumu'ah in large, clustered villages to preserve Islamic practice.

Condition of the Ruler for Friday Prayer
States the necessity of a ruler or deputy for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition requiring a ruler or deputy for Jumu'ah and explain the evidence from the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires a legitimate authority to prevent chaos; if none exists, the community appoints someone.

This passage examines the second condition for Friday prayer: the presence of a ruler or his deputy. The Hanafi school imposes this condition to maintain order due to the large gathering. The author provides evidence from the Companions and then clarifies that the community can appoint a leader if no formal ruler exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The condition is that Jumu'ah must be led by the ruler (sultan) or his appointed deputy (na'ib).
2
Understand the rationale
The author explains that because Jumu'ah gathers many people, there is a risk of conflict, so a designated authority is needed to prevent chaos.
3
Examine the evidence
The author cites statements from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar and the practice of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, showing that an amir should lead.
4
Note the practical allowance
In the absence of a ruler, the Muslims gather and choose someone as amir to lead Jumu'ah.
5
Apply to modern situations
In non-Islamic states, the mosque's khatib or a chosen imam can lead, fulfilling the condition.

ترجمه : (۸۱)[۲] سلطان یا اس کا نائب ہو۔
تشریح : جمعہ میں لوگ بہت جمع ہوتے ہیں اس لئے جھگڑا ہونے کا خطرہ ہے، اس لئے بادشاہ یا اس کا نائب اس کو قائم کرے۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابی میں ہے۔ سأل عبد الله بن عمر بن خطاب عن القرى التي بين مكة والمدينة ماترى في الجمعة قال نعم اذا كان عليهم امير فليجمع ۔ (سنن بیھٹی ، باب العدد الذین اذکا نوافی قریة وجبت عليهم الجمعة ، ج ثالث ، ص ۲۵۴، نمبر ۵۶۱۳) (۲) کتب عمر بن عبد العزيز الى عدى بن عدى : أيما أهل قرية ليسوا بأهل عمود ينتقلون فأمر عليهم أميرا يجمع بهم - مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۳۳۲، من کان میری الجمعة في القرى وغيرها ، ج اول، ص ۴۴۰، نمبر (۵۰۶۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ امیر ہو یا امیر بنایا گیا ہو تو وہ جمعہ قائم کر سکتا ہے (۳) عن عمر بن العزيز ... قال لهم حين فرغ من صلوته ان الامام يجمع حيث كان (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الامام مجمع حیث کان ، ج ثالث ، ص ۶۶ ، نمبر ۵۱۶۱/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۳۹۰ باب الامام يكون مسافر افیمر بالموضع ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۷۶، نمبر ۵۴۹۹) بخاری میں یہ جملہ ہے حدثنا ابو خلدة صلى بنا امير الجمعة (بخاری شریف، باب اذا اشتد الحر یوم الجمعة ، ص ۱۲۴، نمبر ۹۰۶) ان آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ امیر اور بادشاہ جمعہ قائم کرے۔ نوٹ: جہاں امیر اور بادشاہ نہیں ہیں وہاں مسلمان جمع ہو کر جس کو امیر چن لے وہ جمعہ قائم کرائے گا۔ آج کل بہت سے ملکوں میں اسلامی حکومت نہیں ہے اور نہ وہاں امیر اور قاضی ہیں وہاں یہی کرتے ہیں کہ لوگ مسجد کے خطیب سے جمعہ قائم کروا لیتے ہیں۔
Translation: (781)[2] The ruler or his deputy. Explanation: Jumu'ah gathers many people, so there is a risk of conflict; therefore, the king or his deputy should lead it. Evidence: (1) From the statement of a Companion: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar was asked about the villages between Mecca and Medina, 'What do you think about Jumu'ah?' He said: 'Yes, if they have an amir, then let him lead Jumu'ah.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the number... vol. 3, p. 254, no. 5613) (2) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz wrote to 'Adi ibn 'Adi: 'Any people of a village who are not of nomadic origin and do not move, appoint an amir over them to lead Jumu'ah with them.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter 332, vol. 1, p. 440, no. 5069) This effect shows that if there is an amir or an appointed amir, he can lead Jumu'ah. (3) From 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz... he said to them after finishing his prayer: 'The imam leads Jumu'ah wherever he is.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on the imam leading Jumu'ah wherever he is, vol. 3, p. 66, no. 5161 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter 390, vol. 2, p. 476, no. 5499) In Bukhari there is the phrase: Abu Khalda narrated: The amir led us in Jumu'ah. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on when it is hot on Friday, p. 124, no. 906) From these effects it is known that the amir and the king lead Jumu'ah. Note: Where there is no amir or king, the Muslims gather and choose someone as amir, and he leads Jumu'ah. Nowadays in many countries there is no Islamic government and no amir or qadi; they do that people have the khatib of the mosque lead Jumu'ah.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion on the second condition for Friday prayer: the presence of a ruler or his deputy. The author explains that Jumu'ah requires a leader with authority to avoid conflict due to the large gathering. The evidence includes: the statement of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar that Jumu'ah is held when there is an amir; the letter of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ordering the appointment of an amir for villages; the practice of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz himself declaring that the imam leads Jumu'ah wherever he is; and the narration from Bukhari that the amir led the people in Jumu'ah. The author then adds a practical note: if no ruler exists, the Muslims choose someone themselves; in modern non-Islamic states, the mosque's khatib typically leads. This shows that the condition is not a strict requirement of a formal government but rather that someone be in charge to maintain order.

Key Terms
سلطان (sulṭān): The ruler or governing authority who establishes order.
نائب (nā’ib): A deputy appointed by the ruler to act in his place.

B) The Muslims gather and choose someone as amir to lead Jumu'ah.
C) They must travel to a place where there is a ruler.
D) Only the khatib of the mosque can lead Jumu'ah.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah requires a ruler or deputy for order, but the community can appoint a leader if none exists.

Time Condition for Friday Prayer
Establishes the time condition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time condition for Jumu'ah and explain the consequence if the time expires.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid within Zuhr time; missing the time requires praying Zuhr instead.

This passage clarifies a crucial condition for the Friday prayer: it must be performed within the time of Zuhr. Many Muslims assume Jumu'ah can be prayed at any time on Friday, but the Hanafi school restricts it to the Zuhr window. Understanding this condition prevents invalid prayers and ensures proper qada when missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that Jumu'ah is a fard prayer, but its validity depends on conditions. The passage specifies the third condition: time.
2
State the time condition
The text says Jumu'ah must be performed within the time of Zuhr. It cannot be before Zuhr begins or after it ends.
Zuhr time begins at zawal (sun crossing the meridian).
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah when the sun began to decline (zawal).
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
4
Apply wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'hina tamīlu al-shams' (when the sun declines) indicates that Jumu'ah is performed at the start of Zuhr time, thus it must be within that time window.
This is the evidence (dalil) for the condition.
5
Note the consequence of missing the time
If Zuhr time expires before Jumu'ah is performed, Jumu'ah becomes invalid. One must then pray Zuhr as qada (make-up).
Jumu'ah cannot be made up; it is replaced by Zuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۲)(۳) ظہر کا وقت ہو، چنانچہ ظہر سے پہلے جمعہ صحیح نہیں ، اور ظہر کا وقت نکلنے سے جمعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح : تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے لئے ظہر کا وقت ہو، چنانچہ ظہر سے پہلے جمعہ جائز نہیں، اور ظہر کا وقت نکل گیا تو جمعہ نہیں پڑھ سکے گا، اب ظہر کی قضا پڑھے۔ وجه (۱) حدیث میں ہے . عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الله كان يصلى الجمعة حين تميل الشمس ( بخاری شریف ، باب وقت الجمعۃ اذا زالت الشمس ، ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۹۰۴ رمسلم شریف ، باب فی وقت صلوۃ الجمعۃ ، ص ۲۸۳، نمبر) اللہ
Translation: (782)(3) It must be the time of Zuhr; thus, before Zuhr, Jumu'ah is not valid, and if the time of Zuhr expires, Jumu'ah becomes invalid. Explanation: The third condition is that Jumu'ah must be in the time of Zuhr. Thus, before Zuhr, Jumu'ah is not permissible, and if Zuhr time passes, one cannot pray Jumu'ah; instead, one prays Zuhr as qada. Evidence: (1) In the hadith: Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah used to pray Jumu'ah when the sun began to decline. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on the time of Jumu'ah when the sun passes the meridian, p. 123, no. 904; Sahih Muslim, chapter on the time of Jumu'ah prayer, p. 283, no. ...) Allah
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion of the third condition for Jumu'ah: the time. The author states clearly that Jumu'ah is only valid within the time of Zuhr prayer. If one prays it before Zuhr begins, it is invalid; if the Zuhr time exits, Jumu'ah becomes invalid and one must make up Zuhr. The proof is the hadith of Anas that the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah when the sun began to decline (zawal), which is the start of Zuhr time. This aligns with the Hanafi position that the time for Jumu'ah is the same as Zuhr, not before. The incomplete reference at the end suggests a cut-off in the OCR.

Key Terms
ظہر (ẓuhr): The noon prayer time, starting from zawal (sun crossing meridian).
قضا (qaḍā’): Make-up prayer performed after the prescribed time has passed.

Key Takeaway

The Ruler as a Condition for Jumu'ah
Stating the first condition for Jumu'ah and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that Jumu'ah must be led by the sultan or his deputy, identify the supporting proofs, and apply the ruling to scenarios without an Islamic ruler.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah must be led by the ruler or his deputy; if none, Muslims appoint one.

In the Hanafi school, the first condition for the validity of Jumu'ah is that it be led by the sultan (ruler) or his appointed deputy. This requirement, based on the practice of the early Muslim community, aims to prevent disputes that can arise from the large congregation. The passage presents several proofs from the statements of Companions and early caliphs, and then addresses how the ruling applies when there is no Islamic ruler.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the first line of the matn: it states that Jumu'ah requires the sultan or his deputy. Recognize this as a condition (shart) for the prayer's validity.
The condition is not the prayer itself but an external requirement.
2
Examine the proofs
The text quotes three proofs: the statement of Abdullah ibn Umar, the letter of Umar ibn Abdulaziz, and the hadith of Abu Khulda. Identify the common element: all link Jumu'ah to the presence of an amir.
These are transmitted through athar (reports from early generations).
3
Understand the rationale
The commentary mentions that the ruler's involvement prevents disputes due to the large gathering. This is the underlying reason ('illa) for the condition.
This rationale helps apply the ruling in new contexts.
4
Apply when no ruler exists
The passage explicitly states that where there is no ruler, the Muslims should gather and appoint someone as amir. In modern times, this often means the mosque's khatib.
The ruling remains intact; the appointed person takes the place of the sultan.
5
Note the related issue of quorum
The additional proof about Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr leading Jumu'ah with only 12 men shows that the condition is about leadership, not a large congregation.
This clarifies that Jumu'ah is valid in small towns as long as a leader is present.

(۷۸۱) والسلطان او نائبه (۷۸۲) ووقت الظهر فلا تصح قبله وتبطل بخروجه (۷۸۳) والخطبة قبلها بقصدها في وقتها (۷۸۴) وحضور احد لسماعها ممّن تنعقدبهم الجمعة ولو واحدا

ترجمه : (۸۱)[۲] سلطان یا اس کا نائب ہو۔
تشریح : جمعہ میں لوگ بہت جمع ہوتے ہیں اس لئے جھگڑا ہونے کا خطرہ ہے، اس لئے بادشاہ یا اس کا نائب اس کو قائم کرے۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابی میں ہے۔ سأل عبد الله بن عمر بن خطاب عن القرى التي بين مكة والمدينة ماترى في الجمعة قال نعم اذا كان عليهم امير فليجمع ۔ (سنن بیھقی ، باب العدد الذین اذکا نوافی قریة وجبت عليهم الجمعة ، ج ثالث ، ص ۲۵۴، نمبر ۵۶۱۳) (۲) کتب عمر بن عبد العزيز الى عدى بن عدى : أيما أهل قرية ليسوا بأهل عمود ينتقلون فأمر عليهم أميرا يجمع بهم - مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۳۳۲، من کان میری الجمعة في القرى وغيرها ، ج اول، ص ۴۴۰، نمبر (۵۰۶۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ امیر ہو یا امیر بنایا گیا ہو تو وہ جمعہ قائم کر سکتا ہے (۳) عن عمر بن العزيز ... قال لهم حين فرغ من صلوته ان الامام يجمع حيث كان (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الامام مجمع حیث کان ، ج ثالث ، ص ۶۶ ، نمبر ۵۱۶۱/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۳۹۰ باب الامام يكون مسافر افیمر بالموضع ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۷۶، نمبر ۵۴۹۹) بخاری میں یہ جملہ ہے حدثنا ابو خلدة صلى بنا امير الجمعة (بخاری شریف، باب اذا اشتد الحر یوم الجمعة ، ص ۱۲۴، نمبر ۹۰۶) ان آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ امیر اور بادشاہ جمعہ قائم کرے۔

نوٹ: جہاں امیر اور بادشاہ نہیں ہیں وہاں مسلمان جمع ہو کر جس کو امیر چن لے وہ جمعہ قائم کرائے گا۔ آج کل بہت سے ملکوں میں اسلامی حکومت نہیں ہے اور نہ وہاں امیر اور قاضی ہیں وہاں یہی کرتے ہیں کہ لوگ مسجد کے خطیب سے جمعہ قائم کروا لیتے ہیں۔

(۶) حضور نے جب مصعب ابن عمیر کومدینہ بھیجا تو اس وقت وہاں نماز پڑھنے والے کل بارہ آدمی تھے اور انہیں کو جمعہ کی نماز پڑھائی ، عبارت یہ ہے۔ و يذكر عن الزهري أن مصعب ابن عمير حين بعثه النبي عله الى المدينة جمع بهم و هم اثنا عشرة رجلا . ) سنن بيہقي ، باب العد دالذين اذا کا نوافی قریة وجبت عليهم الجمعة ، ج ثالث ،ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۵۶۱۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ خود مدینہ طیبہ میں صرف ۱۲ آدمیوں سے جمعہ قائم کیا گیا ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گاؤں میں جمعہ پڑھنا جائز ہے۔
Chapter of Friday Prayer. (781) And the sultan or his deputy. (782) And the time of Zuhr, so it is not valid before it and becomes invalid by its exit. (783) And the khutbah before it with intention in its time. (784) And the presence of one to hear it from those by whom Jumu'ah is valid, even if one. Translation: (781)[2] The sultan or his deputy. Explanation: In Jumu'ah many people gather, so there is risk of dispute, therefore the king or his deputy should establish it. Evidence: (1) In the saying of the Companion: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar ibn al-Khattab was asked about the villages between Makkah and Madinah, what do you see regarding Jumu'ah? He said: Yes, if they have an amir, let him perform Jumu'ah. (2) 'Umar ibn 'Abdulaziz wrote to 'Adi ibn 'Adi: Any village people who are not tent-dwellers moving about, appoint over them an amir to perform Jumu'ah with them. In this effect, whether there is an amir or one appointed, he can establish Jumu'ah. (3) From 'Umar ibn 'Abdulaziz... he said to them when he finished his prayer: The imam performs Jumu'ah wherever he is. In Bukhari: Abu Khulda narrated: The amir of Jumu'ah led us in prayer. From these effects it is known that the amir and king should establish Jumu'ah. Note: Where there is no amir or king, the Muslims should gather and choose someone as amir, and he will establish Jumu'ah. Nowadays, in many countries there is no Islamic government and there is no amir or qadi, so people do as follows: they have the khatib of the mosque establish Jumu'ah for them. (6) When the Prophet sent Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr to Madinah, at that time there were a total of twelve people praying there, and he led them in Jumu'ah. The text is: 'And it is mentioned from al-Zuhri that Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr, when the Prophet sent him to Madinah, he gathered them in Jumu'ah and they were twelve men.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) From this effect it is known that even in Madinah itself, Jumu'ah was established with only 12 people, from which it is known that it is permissible to pray Jumu'ah in a village.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the first condition for the validity of Jumu'ah: that it must be led by the sultan (ruler) or his deputy. The author provides evidence from the actions of the Companions and early Muslims. The key idea is that the ruler's involvement prevents disputes due to the large gathering. The passage then addresses the practical scenario where there is no Islamic ruler: Muslims may choose someone as amir, or in modern times the mosque's khatib may lead. The additional discussion about the quorum of twelve people from the story of Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr supports the permissibility of Jumu'ah in small towns, which is a related but separate issue.

Key Terms
سلطان (sulṭān): The ruler or authority figure who leads the Jumu'ah prayer.
نائب (nā’ib): Deputy or representative of the sultan appointed to lead Jumu'ah.
أمير (amīr): Commander or leader; in the context of Jumu'ah, the one authorized to lead the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Time of Zuhr as a Condition for Jumu'ah
Stating the time condition for Jumu'ah and its proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time condition for Jumu'ah and determine when Jumu'ah is valid or invalid based on Zuhr time.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah must be performed within the time of Zuhr; if performed before or after, it is invalid and Zuhr must be prayed.

This lesson explains the second condition for Jumu'ah: it must be performed in the time of Zuhr. We will examine the textual evidence from hadith and the practice of the Salaf, and understand the practical implication if the time expires.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Recognize that the passage explicitly states that being in the time of Zuhr is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah. If Jumu'ah is performed before or after Zuhr time, it is invalid.
The condition is based on the hadith indicating the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah at zawal.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites hadith from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet used to pray Jumu'ah 'when the sun declined' (hina tamīlu al-shams). This indicates the time of zawal, which is the start of Zuhr time.
The second hadith about napping after Jumu'ah also supports quick performance after zawal.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase 'hina tamīlu al-shams' directly points to zawal. In Hanafi usul, the imperative or indicative action of the Prophet establishes the ruling as binding. Thus, Jumu'ah must be performed in Zuhr time.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) with zanni thubut but accepted across madhhabs.
4
Apply the implication
If the time of Zuhr expires, Jumu'ah becomes invalid. The passage provides the example of the Tabi'i who prayed Zuhr when al-Hajjaj delayed Jumu'ah. One must then pray Zuhr as qada.
This shows the practical consequence: one cannot join a late Jumu'ah; the obligation shifts to Zuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۲)(۳) ظہر کا وقت ہو، چنانچہ ظہر سے پہلے جمعہ صحیح نہیں ، اور ظہر کا وقت نکلنے سے جمعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح : تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے لئے ظہر کا وقت ہو، چنانچہ ظہر سے پہلے جمعہ جائز نہیں، اور ظہر کا وقت نکل گیا تو جمعہ نہیں پڑھ سکے گا، اب ظہر کی قضا پڑھے۔ وجه (۱) حدیث میں ہے . عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الله كان يصلى الجمعة حين تميل الشمس ( بخاری شریف ، باب وقت الجمعۃ اذا زالت الشمس ، ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۹۰۴ رمسلم شریف ، باب فی وقت صلوۃ الجمعۃ ، ص ۲۸۳، نمبر ۱۹۹۴/۸۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زوال کے بعد جمعہ کی نماز پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ اور یہ وقت ظہر کا ہے اس لئے ظہر کے وقت میں پڑھا جائے گا (۲) عن انس بن مالک قال : كنا نبكر بالجمعة و نقيل بعد الجمعة ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب وقت الجمعة اذازالت الشمس، ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۱۹۰۵ مسلم شریف ، باب صلاة الجمعة حين تزول الشمس ،ص ۱۳۴۵، نمبر ۱۹۹۱/۸۵۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ زوال کے فورا بعد جمعہ پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ (۳)۔ ظہر کا وقت نکل جائے تو پھر جمعہ نہیں پڑھے گا بلکہ ظہر کی قضا پڑھے گا۔ اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ كان الحجاج يؤخر الجمعة فكنت انا اصلى وابراهيم و سعيد بن جبير فصليا الظهر ثم نتحدث وهو يخطب ثم نصلى معهم ثم نجعلها نافلة (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة،۱۳۸۷الجمعة يؤخرها الامام حتى يذهب وقتها ، ج اول ص ۴۷۴ نمبر ۵۴۸۶ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر کا وقت ختم ہو جائے تو اب جمعہ نہیں پڑھے بلکہ ظہر کی نماز قضا پڑھے۔
Translation: (782)(3) It should be the time of Zuhr, so before Zuhr Jumu'ah is not correct, and if the time of Zuhr exits, Jumu'ah becomes invalid. Explanation: The third condition is that it should be the time of Zuhr for Jumu'ah. So before Zuhr Jumu'ah is not permissible, and if the time of Zuhr has left, then he cannot pray Jumu'ah; rather he should pray Zuhr as missed. Evidence: (1) In the hadith: From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah used to pray Jumu'ah when the sun declined. This hadith shows that they used to pray Jumu'ah after zawal, and this is the time of Zuhr. (2) From Anas ibn Malik: We used to hasten to Jumu'ah and take a nap after Jumu'ah. This also indicates that they prayed immediately after zawal. (3) If the time of Zuhr leaves, then he will not pray Jumu'ah but will pray Zuhr as missed. In the statement of the Tabi'i: Al-Hajjaj used to delay Jumu'ah, so I, Ibrahim, and Sa'id ibn Jubayr prayed Zuhr, then talked while he was delivering the khutbah, then prayed with them and considered it nafl. This shows that if time exits, one should pray Zuhr.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes the second condition for Jumu'ah: it must be performed in the time of Zuhr. The author cites hadith from Anas ibn Malik showing that the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah at zawal (sun's decline). If the time of Zuhr ends, Jumu'ah becomes invalid and one must pray Zuhr as a missed prayer. The proof from a Tabi'i demonstrates the practice of praying Zuhr independently when the imam delays Jumu'ah beyond its time.

Key Terms
ظہر کا وقت (ẓuhr kā waqt): The time of the Zuhr prayer, starting from zawal (sun's decline) until the shadow of an object equals its length.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pray Jumu'ah as soon as possible
B) Pray Zuhr as a missed prayer
C) Combine Jumu'ah with Asr
D) Skip the prayer

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah must be prayed in the time of Zuhr; otherwise, it is invalid and one must pray Zuhr as missed.

Condition of the Khutbah Before Jumu'ah
Stating that the khutbah must precede Jumu'ah with intention in its time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions of a valid Jumu'ah khutbah and explain why omitting the khutbah requires praying Zuhr.

Core Idea
A khutbah before Jumu'ah is a condition; without it, Jumu'ah is invalid and must be replaced by Zuhr.

The Jumu'ah prayer is a weekly obligation but has unique conditions. One essential condition is that a khutbah (sermon) must precede the prayer. This lesson clarifies the requirements of that khutbah and the consequence of its omission, supported by hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states that the khutbah must be before Jumu'ah, with intention (niyyah) and in the time of Zuhr. These are three sub-conditions for a valid khutbah.
2
Understand the rationale
The khutbah replaces two rak'ats of Zuhr, explaining why Jumu'ah is two rak'ats. This is derived from the statement of 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah.
3
Apply the consequence
If the khutbah is omitted, Jumu'ah is invalid; one must pray Zuhr (four rak'ats) because the condition was never met.
This consequence is supported by the athar from Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح : جمعہ سے پہلے جمعہ کی نیت سے ظہر کے وقت میں خطبہ ہو یہ چوتھی شرط ہے۔ وجه : (۱) ظہر کی نماز چار رکعتیں ہیں اور جمعہ کی نماز دورکعتیں ہیں اس لئے دورکعت کے بدلے میں دو خطبے ہیں۔ اس لئے خطبہ جمعہ کی شرط ہے اسکے لئے پیار ہے۔ عن عطاء بن ابی رباح و غیره و عن سعيد بن جبير قال : كانت الجمعة أربعا فـجـعـلـت الـخـطـبـة مكـان الركعتين - . (سن للبیھقی ، باب وجوب الخطبة وانه اذالم يخب صلی ظہرا اربا ، ج ثالث ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۵۷۰۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ظہر کی دورکعت کے بدلے میں جمعہ کے دو خطبے ہیں۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر صلى الله قال كان النبي لا يخطب قائماثم يقعد ثم يقوم كما يفعلون الآن . Translation: (783)[2] There should be a khutbah before Jumu'ah, with the intention of Jumu'ah in the time of Zuhr. Explanation: That there is a khutbah before the prayer with the intention of Jumu'ah in the time of Zuhr is the fourth condition. Evidence: (1) Zuhr prayer is four rak'ats and Jumu'ah is two rak'ats, so in place of two rak'ats there are two khutbahs. Therefore, the khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah. From 'Ata ibn Abi Rabah and others: 'Jumu'ah used to be four rak'ats, then the khutbah was placed in place of two rak'ats.' (2) In the hadith from Ibn 'Umar: 'The Prophet used to deliver the khutbah standing, then sit, then stand, as they do now.' This indicates two khutbahs with a sitting between them. If the khutbah is not delivered, then one should pray Zuhr (four rak'ats). Proof: 'There is no Jumu'ah without a khutbah; whoever does not deliver a khutbah should pray four rak'ats.'
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that a khutbah (sermon) must precede Jumu'ah, delivered with the intention of Jumu'ah in the time of Zuhr. The khutbah substitutes for two rak'ats of Zuhr, hence Jumu'ah is two rak'ats. The hadith shows the Prophet delivered two khutbahs standing with a sitting between. If the khutbah is omitted, Jumu'ah is invalid and one must pray Zuhr.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khuṭbah): The sermon delivered before the Jumu'ah prayer, consisting of two parts.

Key Takeaway
The khutbah before Jumu'ah is a condition; without it, the prayer is invalid and must be replaced by Zuhr.

The Hanafi Condition of a Listener for Jumu'ah Khutbah
Stating the fifth condition for Jumu'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah validity regarding listeners and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires at least one listener; the khutbah cannot be delivered to an empty congregation.

This lesson examines the fifth condition for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school: the presence of at least one person to hear the khutbah. We will explore the textual evidence and understand why this condition is essential for the validity of Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the passage and state the condition exactly as given: at least one person from those obligated to perform Jumu'ah must be present to hear the khutbah.
2
Understand the scope of the listener
The listener must be someone upon whom Jumu'ah is fard (obligatory). This excludes minors, women, and travelers who are not obligated.
Hanafi position: The condition is that the person is subject to the obligation of Jumu'ah.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub commands attending the dhikr (khutbah). The imperative indicates obligation in Hanafi usul, supporting the condition that someone must be present.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a condition.
4
Note the cross-madhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require a minimum of 40 people for Jumu'ah. The Hanafi school holds that one qualified listener suffices for the khutbah.
This difference affects the minimum congregation size.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۴)[۵] جن لوگوں سے جمعہ ادا ہوتا ہو ان میں سے ایک شخص بھی خطبہ سننے کے لئے حاضر ہو۔
تشریح : جن لوگوں سے جمعہ قائم ہوتا ہو ان میں سے کم سے کم ایک آدمی خطبہ سننے کے لئے موجود ہو، پانچویں شرط یہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے، عن سمرة بن جندب ان النبى الله الله قال احضروا الذكر و ادنوا من الامام فان الرجل لا يزال يتباعد حتى يؤخر في الجنة و ان دخلها - (ابوداود شریف ، باب الدنو من الامام عند الموعظة
Translation: (784)[5] One of those by whom Jumu'ah is performed should be present to hear it. Explanation: The fifth condition is that at least one person among those by whom Jumu'ah is established should be present to hear the khutbah. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: From Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet said: 'Attend the remembrance and draw near to the imam, for a man continues to distance himself until he is delayed in Paradise even if he enters it.' (Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, though the proof is cut short. It states the fifth condition for Jumu'ah: at least one person who is required to attend Jumu'ah must be present to hear the khutbah. The hadith encourages attendance and closeness to the imam. The condition ensures that the khutbah is not delivered to an empty congregation.

Key Terms
حضور (ḥuḍūr): The presence of a person who is subject to the obligation of Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Jumu'ah khutbah is valid only if at least one person obligated to attend is present to hear it.
