Jumu'ah is Prayed During Zuhr Time
Ruling with proof about time of Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that Jumu'ah must be prayed within zuhr time and explain the consequence if the time expires.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is valid only within zuhr time; if missed, zuhr must be made up.

This passage clarifies the critical link between Jumu'ah and zuhr time. Using hadith and the practice of the Companions and Tabi'in, it establishes that Jumu'ah is a substitute for zuhr and must be offered within the same time window. If the imam delays beyond zuhr time, the obligation to pray Jumu'ah lapses and one must pray zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that Jumu'ah is to be performed at the time of zuhr (after zawal).
This is the core ruling of the passage.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith from Anas ibn Malik (r.a.) which indicates they used to hasten to Jumu'ah after zawal and then take a nap. This shows the time is immediately after zawal – i.e., the beginning of zuhr time.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the consequence of time expiry
If zuhr time passes, Jumu'ah is no longer valid. One must pray the qada of zuhr instead.
This is supported by the athar from the Tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Sa'id ibn Jubayr.
4
Note the practical application
If you arrive or the imam delays Jumu'ah until after zuhr time ends, you should pray zuhr (4 rak'at) individually, not Jumu'ah.
The passage states: 'If the time of zuhr passes, then Jumu'ah will not be prayed, rather he will pray the qada of zuhr.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجمعة قبلها بقصدها في وقتها (۷۸۴) وحضور احد لسماعها ممّن تنعقدبهم الجمعة ولو واحدا في ۱۹۹۴/۸۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زوال کے بعد جمعہ کی نماز پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ اور یہ وقت ظہر کا ہے اس لئے ظہر کے وقت میں پڑھا جائے گا (۲) عن أنس بن مالك قال : كنا نبكر بالجمعة و نقيل بعد الجمعة ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب وقت الجمعة اذازالت الشمس، ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۱۹۰۵ مسلم شریف ، باب صلاة الجمعة حين تزول الشمس ،ص ۱۳۴۵، نمبر ۱۹۹۱/۸۵۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ زوال کے فورا بعد جمعہ پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ (۳)۔ ظہر کا وقت نکل جائے تو پھر جمعہ نہیں پڑھے گا بلکہ ظہر کی قضا پڑھے گا۔ اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ كان الحجاج يؤخر الجمعة فكنت انا اصلى وابراهيم و سعيد بن جبير فصليا الظهر ثم نتحدث وهو يخطب ثم نصلى معهم ثم نجعلها نافلة (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة،۱۳۸۷الجمعة يؤخرها الامام حتى يذهب وقتها ، ج اول ص ۴۷۴ نمبر ۵۴۸۶ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر کا وقت ختم ہو جائے تو اب جمعہ نہیں پڑھے بلکہ ظہر کی نماز قضا پڑھے۔
Chapter of Jumu'ah. Before it with intention in its time (784) and presence of one to hear it from those upon whom Jumu'ah is binding even if one... From this hadith it is known that after zawal they used to pray Jumu'ah. And this is the time of zuhr, therefore it will be prayed in zuhr time. (2) From Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) said: We used to hasten to Jumu'ah and take a nap after Jumu'ah. (Bukhari, chapter on time of Jumu'ah when the sun passes meridian, p.123, no.1905; Muslim, chapter on Jumu'ah prayer when the sun passes meridian, p.1345, no.1991/859) In this hadith it is that immediately after zawal they used to pray Jumu'ah. (3) If the time of zuhr passes, then Jumu'ah will not be prayed, rather he will pray the qada of zuhr. In this saying of a tabi'i: Al-Hajjaj used to delay Jumu'ah, so I and Ibrahim and Sa'id ibn Jubayr would pray zuhr, then we would talk while he was delivering the khutbah, then we would pray with them and then make it nafl. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 1387, chapter on Jumu'ah delayed by imam until its time passes, vol.1 p.474 no.5486) From this athar it is known that if zuhr time ends, then Jumu'ah is not prayed, rather he prays the qada of zuhr.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the time of Jumu'ah. The author begins the chapter on Jumu'ah and immediately addresses its time. He states that Jumu'ah is to be performed at the time of zuhr, i.e., after the sun passes its zenith (zawal). This is established by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Anas ibn Malik. The hadith indicates that after zawal, the Prophet used to delay the Jumu'ah prayer? Actually, the hadith says 'we used to hasten to Jumu'ah and take a nap after Jumu'ah,' implying it was early after zawal. Another hadith from Anas confirms they prayed immediately after zawal. The author then deduces that if the zuhr time expires, one cannot pray Jumu'ah; rather, one must pray the qada of zuhr. This is supported by the practice of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Sa'id ibn Jubayr, who, when the governor al-Hajjaj delayed Jumu'ah beyond its time, prayed zuhr instead and then prayed with the congregation as nafl. This establishes that Jumu'ah is valid only within zuhr time.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith, marking the beginning of zuhr time.
جمعہ (jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces zuhr for those obliged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if the imam delays Jumu'ah until after zuhr time expires, what should a person do?
A) Wait for the imam to finish Jumu'ah
B) Pray Jumu'ah alone
C) Pray zuhr instead
D) Skip both prayers

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid during zuhr time; if the time passes, one must pray zuhr instead of Jumu'ah.

The Khutbah: A Condition for Jumu'ah Prayer
Establishing that two khutbahs before Jumu'ah are a condition replacing two rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the khutbah for Jumu'ah and explain the consequence of its omission.

Core Idea
Two khutbahs replace two rak'ahs — omitting the khutbah invalidates Jumu'ah.

This passage establishes that the khutbah before Jumu'ah is not just recommended but a legal condition. The author uses both rational reasoning (talil) and prophetic practice to prove that the khutbah substitutes for two rak'ahs of zuhr. Missing the khutbah means the Jumu'ah is void and one must pray zuhr instead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delivering the khutbah before Jumu'ah. The ruling is wajib (obligatory).
This is the fourth condition mentioned in the text.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: (a) an athar from 'Ata' and Sa'id ibn Jubayr showing the khutbah replaces two rak'ahs; (b) the hadith of Ibn 'Umar showing the Prophet's practice of two khutbahs.
The athar has a chain of transmission; the hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The logical link: zuhr has four rak'ahs, Jumu'ah has two, so the two missing rak'ahs are replaced by two khutbahs. The hadith establishes the manner and necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is also require the khutbah but classify it as a condition (shart) rather than wajib; the practical consequence is similar (Jumu'ah invalid without it).
The cross-madhhab difference is in usul classification, not in practice.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit athar and prophetic practice. The ruling is mufta bihi and part of zahir al-riwayah.
The text indicates this is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۳) [۲] جمعہ سے پہلے خطبہ ہو جمعہ کی نیت سے ظہر کے وقت میں۔
تشریح : جمعہ سے پہلے جمعہ کی نیت سے ظہر کے وقت میں خطبہ ہو یہ چوتھی شرط ہے۔ وجه : (۱) ظہر کی نماز چار رکعتیں ہیں اور جمعہ کی نماز دورکعتیں ہیں اس لئے دورکعت کے بدلے میں دو خطبے ہیں۔ اس لئے خطبہ
جمعہ کی شرط ہے اسکے لئے پیار ہے۔ عن عطاء بن ابی رباح و غیره و عن سعيد بن جبير قال : كانت الجمعة أربعا فـجـعـلـت الـخـطـبـة مكـان الركعتين - . (سن للبیھقی ، باب وجوب الخطبة وانه اذالم يخب صلی ظہرا اربا ، ج ثالث ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۵۷۰۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ظہر کی دورکعت کے بدلے میں جمعہ کے دو خطبے ہیں۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر صلى الله عليه وسلم قال كان النبي لا يخطب قائماثم يقعد ثم يقوم كما يفعلون الآن . (بخارى شريف، باب الخطبة قائماص ۱۲۵ نمبر ۹۲۰ رمسلم شریف فصل يخطب الخطبتين قائما ص ۲۸۳ کتاب الجمعہ نمبر ۱۹۹۴/۸۶۱ رابوداؤد شریف، باب الخطبة قائماص ۱۶۳ نمبر ۱۰۹۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو خطبے دیں گے اور دونوں کے درمیان امام بیٹھیں گے ۔ اگر خطبہ نہیں پڑھا تو ظہر کی نماز پرھے گا اس کا ثبوت اس اثر میں ہے عن مصعب بن عمير قال و بلغنا انه لا جمعة الا بخطبة فمن لم يخطب صلى اربعا .
سن للبیھقی ، باب وجوب الخطبة واند از الم مخطب صلی ظہرا اربعا، ج ثالث ص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۵۷۰۲/مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الامام لا يخطب یوم الجمعۃ کم صلی ، ج ثالث ، ص ۷۳ نمبر ۵۲۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر خطبہ نہیں پڑھا تو ظہر کی چار رکعت پڑھے گا۔
Translation: (783) [2] Before Jumu'ah there should be a khutbah with the intention of Jumu'ah at zuhr time. Explanation: Before Jumu'ah there should be a khutbah with the intention of Jumu'ah at zuhr time; this is the fourth condition. Proof: (1) Zuhr prayer has four rak'ahs and Jumu'ah prayer has two rak'ahs, so in place of two rak'ahs there are two khutbahs. Therefore, the khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah. There is proof for this: from 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah and others and from Sa'id ibn Jubayr who said: 'Jumu'ah was four (rak'ahs), then the khutbah was placed in place of the two rak'ahs.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on obligation of khutbah and that if he does not deliver khutbah he prays zuhr four, vol.3 p.278 no.5703) In this athar, the two khutbahs of Jumu'ah are in place of the two rak'ahs of zuhr. (2) In the hadith from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to deliver the khutbah standing, then sit, then stand as they do now. (Bukhari, chapter on khutbah standing, p.125 no.920; Muslim, section on delivering two khutbahs standing, p.283; Abu Dawud, chapter on khutbah standing, p.163 no.1094) From this hadith it is known that two khutbahs are given and between them the imam sits. If the khutbah is not recited, then he will pray zuhr. Proof of this is in the athar from Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr: 'We have heard that there is no Jumu'ah except with a khutbah; whoever does not deliver a khutbah prays four (rak'ahs).' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on obligation of khutbah and that if he does not deliver khutbah he prays zuhr four, vol.3 p.278 no.5702; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on imam does not deliver khutbah on Friday how many he prays, vol.3 p.73 no.5208) From this athar it is known that if he does not deliver a khutbah, he prays four rak'ahs of zuhr.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the condition of khutbah for Jumu'ah. The author states that before Jumu'ah prayer, there must be a khutbah performed with the intention of Jumu'ah and within zuhr time. This is the fourth condition (from the sequence). The reasoning (talil) is that since Jumu'ah substitutes for zuhr, and zuhr has four rak'ahs while Jumu'ah has two, the two missing rak'ahs are replaced by two khutbahs. This is supported by an athar from 'Ata' and Sa'id ibn Jubayr. Additionally, the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) shows that he delivered two khutbahs standing, with a sitting in between. The critical consequence: if the imam omits the khutbah, the Jumu'ah is invalid and one must pray zuhr instead.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered before Jumu'ah prayer, consisting of two parts with a sitting in between.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The congregation prays Jumu'ah without khutbah
B) They must pray zuhr instead
C) The khutbah can be made up after prayer
D) The imam must repeat the Jumu'ah later

Key Takeaway
The khutbah is a wajib condition for Jumu'ah; omitting it requires praying zuhr instead.

Condition: Presence of a Listener for the Khutbah
Stating and proving the condition of listener presence for Jumu'ah khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that at least one person obligated for Jumu'ah must be present to hear the khutbah, and identify the textual proofs from hadith and Quran that establish this condition.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires at least one listener for the khutbah; without it, the prayer is invalid.

The khutbah is a central element of Jumu'ah, but is it enough for the imam to deliver it alone? The Hanafi school teaches that a congregation is essential. This lesson examines the fifth condition for Jumu'ah: the presence of at least one listener from those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory. We will trace how this ruling is derived from the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub and the Quranic verse in Surat al-Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Locate the explicit statement of the condition in the text: that at least one person from those obliged for Jumu'ah must be present to hear the khutbah.
The text says 'one person' is sufficient.
2
Examine the first proof (hadith)
Read the hadith cited from Abu Dawud. The Prophet (peace be upon him) commands attending the 'remembrance' (khutbah) and drawing near the imam. This implies that listeners must be present to obey the command.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but accepted in Hanafi usul for furu' rulings.
3
Examine the second proof (Quran)
Consider the verse from Surat al-Jumu'ah (62:11) that criticizes those who leave the standing Prophet during the khutbah. This indicates that there were listeners present, establishing the norm that an audience is required.
The verse is used as isharah (indication) for the condition, not a direct command.
4
Apply the condition
Understand that if no listener from the obliged category is present, the Jumu'ah is not valid. The khutbah must be heard by at least one person who is required to attend.
This condition is specific to the khutbah; the prayer itself may have different conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۴)[۵] جن لوگوں سے جمعہ ادا ہوتا ہو ان میں سے ایک شخص بھی خطبہ سننے کے لئے حاضر ہو۔ تشریح : جن لوگوں سے جمعہ قائم ہوتا ہو ان میں سے کم سے کم ایک آدمی خطبہ سننے کے لئے موجود ہو، پانچویں شرط یہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے، عن سمرة بن جندب ان النبى الله الله قال احضروا الذكر و ادنوا من الامام فان الرجل لا يزال يتباعد حتى يؤخر في الجنة و ان دخلها - (ابوداود شریف ، باب الدنو من الامام عند الموعظة ص ۱۶۷، نمبر (۱۱۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ خطبہ کے وقت امام کے قریب ہو۔ (۲) اس آیت میں اس کا اشارہ ہے ۔ و اذا رأوا تجارة أو لهوا أنفضوا اليها وتركوك قائما . (آیت اا، سورۃ الجمعۃ (۶۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ حضور کو جمعہ کے وقت کھڑے ہوئے چھوڑ دیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کچھ آدمی سننے والے بھی ہوں۔
Translation: (784)[5] One person from those upon whom Jumu'ah is performed should be present to hear the khutbah. Explanation: From those upon whom Jumu'ah is established, at least one person should be present to hear the khutbah; this is the fifth condition. Proof: (1) In this hadith, from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Attend the remembrance and draw near to the imam, for a man continues to distance himself until he is delayed in Paradise even if he enters it.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on drawing near to the imam during the sermon, p.167, no.1108) In this hadith, it is to be near the imam during the khutbah. (2) There is an indication from this ayah: 'And when they see trade or amusement, they disperse to it and leave you standing.' (Surah al-Jumu'ah, 62:11) This ayah indicates that when the Prophet was standing (delivering the khutbah), some people left, implying that some were listening.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth condition for Jumu'ah: that at least one person from those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory must be present to hear the khutbah. The condition is derived from two proofs. First, the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub encourages attending the reminder (the khutbah) and sitting close to the imam. This implies that there must be an audience. Second, the Quranic verse from Surat al-Jumu'ah criticizes those who left the Prophet while he was delivering the khutbah. This indicates that there were listeners present. If no one is present to listen, the khutbah would be meaningless and the Jumu'ah would not be valid.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Jumu'ah prayer; the condition here requires that it be heard by at least one listener.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of listeners required for the khutbah of Jumu'ah to be valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Three men
B) One person from those obligated
C) At least two people
D) No minimum

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah requires at least one obligated listener for the khutbah; without it, the prayer is invalid and must be prayed as Zuhr.

General Permission: The Sixth Condition of Jumu'ah
Stating that general permission to attend Jumu'ah is a condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of general permission for Jumu'ah and explain why it is necessary.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires public access — no permission, no congregation.

Jumu'ah is a weekly obligation that must be a public gathering. The Hanafi school specifies six conditions for its validity. This lesson focuses on the sixth condition: general permission (al-idhn al-amm) for people to attend. Without this, the prayer is not valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
Recognize that Jumu'ah prayer is ruled upon and that one of its conditions is general permission for attendance.
The condition is about public access, not a specific permission from an individual.
2
Understand why this condition is required
Jumu'ah is meant to be a communal gathering; general permission ensures that all Muslims have the opportunity to attend and fulfill the obligation.
It distinguishes Jumu'ah from private or exclusive prayers.
3
Distinguish from other prayers
Other prayers (e.g., Duhr) do not require general permission; Jumu'ah is unique in needing a public invitation.
If general permission is not present, the prayer is not considered Jumu'ah; Duhr must be prayed instead.
4
Determine the consequence of missing the condition
If this condition is absent, Jumu'ah is invalid and the obligation defaults to Duhr. This highlights the importance of open congregation.
The condition is external; it must be fulfilled by the community or ruler.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۵) [۶] عام اجازت ہو۔
تشریح : جمعہ میں آنے کے لئے عام لوگوں کو اجازت ہوتب جمعہ ہوگا، یہ چھٹی شرط ہے۔
Translation: (785)[6] General permission. Explanation: For coming to Jumu'ah, there should be general permission for people; then Jumu'ah will be valid. This is the sixth condition.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage states the sixth condition for Jumu'ah: that there be general permission for people to attend. This means that the ruler or imam should have granted an open invitation to the community, and there should be no restrictions preventing attendance. If people are not allowed to come freely, Jumu'ah cannot be established. This condition ensures that the obligation of Jumu'ah is publicly accessible.

Key Terms
اذن عام (idhn 'amm): General permission for the public to attend Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permission from one's employer
B) The imam giving permission to a specific group
C) Open invitation for all Muslims to attend
D) Permission to leave the mosque

Key Takeaway
General permission for public attendance is a necessary condition for Jumu'ah; without it, the prayer is invalid and Duhr must be prayed instead.

The Congregation Condition for Jumu'ah
Specifying the minimum congregation of three men and the need to remain until sajdah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum congregation required for Jumu'ah in the Hanafi school and identify the timing condition (remaining until sajdah).

Core Idea
Three men besides the imam suffice for Jumu'ah, but they must stay until prostration.

Jumu'ah is a weekly obligation with specific conditions. One key condition is the presence of a congregation. This passage from a Hanafi primer explains the minimum number of men required and how long they must remain for the prayer to be valid. Understanding this condition helps distinguish when Jumu'ah may be performed in small communities and when it must be substituted with Zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the first sentence: the condition is a congregation of three men besides the imam. Note that slaves, travelers, and sick are included; women and children are not.
2
Understand the timing requirement
The congregation must remain with the imam until the prostration (sajdah) of the first rak'ah. If they leave after that, the imam completes Jumu'ah alone; if before, Jumu'ah is invalid and Zuhr must be prayed.
This is based on the rule that catching one rak'ah suffices for Jumu'ah.
3
Examine the primary proof
The hadith from Umm 'Abdullah al-Dawsiyyah states Jumu'ah is obligatory on the people of a village even if only three, with the imam as the fourth. This shows three men are sufficient.
This hadith is adduced as the main evidence for the three-man minimum.
4
Examine the supporting proofs
The hadith from Abu Hurairah and the athar from Ibn 'Umar show that catching one rak'ah of Jumu'ah is enough, implying the congregation must be present until the sajdah (completing the first rak'ah).
These reinforce the timing condition.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) require larger congregations (e.g., forty men). This lesson focuses on the Hanafi view; the difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi view is considered a concession for small communities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۶)[۷] اور جماعت ہو اور وہ تین مرد ہوں امام کے علاوہ ، اگر چہ غلام ہوں ، یا مسافر ہو، یا بیمار ہوں، اور شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ امام کے ساتھ سجدے تک باقی رہیں۔ پس اگر وہ سجدہ کرنے کے بعد جائیں تو امام اکیلا جمعہ پورا کرے، اور اگر امام کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے بھاگ جائیں تو جمعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح : جمعیت سے مشتق ہے اس لئے کم از کم تین مرد ہوں تو جمعہ قائم ہوگا، چاہے ایسے مرد ہوں جن پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے، مثلا غلام ہوں یا مسافر ہوں یا بیمار ہوں تب بھی جمعہ قائم ہو جائے گا لیکن اگر عورت ہو، یا بچہ ہو تو اس سے جمعہ قائم نہیں ہوگا ، اور یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ جمعہ قائم ہونے تک باقی رہیں، اور جمعہ پہلی رکعت کے سجدہ کرنے سے قائم ہوگا، اس لئے پہلی رکعت کے سجدے تک باقی رہیں تو جمعہ پڑھا جائے گا ، اور اگر اس سے پہلے بھاگ جائیں ، یا تین میں سے ایک کم ہو جائے تو جمعہ کے بجائے ظہر پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن ام عبد الله الدوسية قالت سمعت رسول الله لا يقول الجمعة واجبة صلى الله عليه وسلم على اهل كل قرية وان لم يكونوا الا ثلثة ورابعهم امامهم . (دار قطنی ، باب الجمعۃ علی اہل قریہ ج ثانی ص ۷ نمبر ۱۵۷۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہو کہ امام کے علاوہ تین آدمی ہوں تب جمعہ ہو گا۔ (۲) پہلی رکعت کے سجدہ تک باقی رہیں اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال : أن النبى الله الله قال : اذا ادرك أحدكم الركعتين من يوم الجمعة فقد أدرك الجمعة و اذا ادرك ركعة فليركع اليها أخرى ، و ان لم يدرك ركعة فليصل أربع ركعات (دار قطنی ، باب فیمن یدرک من الجمعة رکعة أولم یدرکھا، ج ثانی، ص ۹ نمبر ۱۵۸۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک رکعت پائے تو جمعہ پڑھے اور اس سے کم پائے تو چار رکعت ظہر پڑھے ۔ (۳) اثر میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ قال عبد الله بن عمر : من ادرك ركعة من الجمعة فليصل اليها أخرى و من لم يدرك الركوع فليصل أربعا - مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من قال اذا ادرک رکعتة من الجمعة صلی الیها آخری، ج اول ص ۴۶۱، نمبر ۵۳۳۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک رکعت یعنی رکوع تک ملے تو جمعہ کی نماز پڑھے، اور اس سے کم ملے تو ظہر کی نماز پڑھے۔ (۴) سجدہ سے پہلے ایک رکعت پوری نہیں ہوتی اور جب تک ایک رکعت نہ ہو تو جمعہ
Translation: (786)[7] And there should be a congregation, and they are three men besides the imam, even if they are slaves, or travelers, or sick. And the condition is that they remain with the imam until the prostration. So if they leave after his prostration, the imam completes it alone. And if they flee before the imam's prostration, then Jumu'ah is invalid. Explanation: It is derived from 'jama'ah' (congregation), so the minimum is three men for Jumu'ah to be established, even if they are men upon whom Jumu'ah is not obligatory, such as slaves, travelers, or sick; even then Jumu'ah is established. But if there is a woman or a child, Jumu'ah is not established by them. And this is also a condition: that they remain until Jumu'ah is established. And Jumu'ah is established by the prostration of the first rak'ah. Therefore, if they remain until the prostration of the first rak'ah, then Jumu'ah is prayed. And if they leave before that, or one of the three becomes less, then he prays zuhr instead of Jumu'ah. Proof: (1) In this hadith, from Umm 'Abdullah al-Dawsiyyah, she said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of every village, even if there are only three, and their imam is the fourth.' (Darqutni, chapter on Jumu'ah upon the people of a village, vol.2 p.7 no.1578) From this hadith, three men besides the imam are required for Jumu'ah. (2) For remaining until the prostration of the first rak'ah, this hadith is: from Abu Hurairah said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If one of you catches two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah, he has caught Jumu'ah; and if he catches one rak'ah, he should add another to it; and if he does not catch a rak'ah, he should pray four rak'ahs.' (Darqutni, chapter on the one who catches one rak'ah of Jumu'ah or does not catch it, vol.2 p.9 no.1586) This hadith indicates that if one catches one rak'ah, he prays Jumu'ah, and if less, he prays four rak'ahs (zuhr). (3) There is an athar as proof. 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar said: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Jumu'ah, let him add another to it; and whoever does not catch the ruku', let him pray four (rak'ahs).' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on whoever says if one catches two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah he prays another, vol.1 p.461 no.5332) This athar shows that if one catches a rak'ah, i.e., the ruku', he prays Jumu'ah, and if less, he prays zuhr. (4) Before the prostration, one rak'ah is not complete, and as long as one rak'ah is not...
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh condition for Jumu'ah: the congregation must consist of at least three men besides the imam. These men need not be those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory (e.g., slaves, travelers, the sick are included). Women and children cannot fulfill this condition. Additionally, these three men must remain with the imam until the prostration of the first rak'ah (sajdah of the first rak'ah). If they leave after the imam's sajdah, the imam can complete Jumu'ah alone; but if they leave before the sajdah, Jumu'ah is invalid and zuhr must be prayed. The proofs include a hadith from Umm 'Abdullah al-Dawsiyyah requiring three men, and a hadith from Abu Hurairah indicating that catching one rak'ah is sufficient to join Jumu'ah, which implies that the congregation must be present until at least the first sajdah (completing the first rak'ah). The athar from Ibn 'Umar reinforces this. The cut-off sentence at the end likely completes the reasoning that without a full rak'ah, Jumu'ah is not established.

Key Terms
جماعت (jama'ah): Congregation; here, at least three men besides the imam required for Jumu'ah.
سجدہ (sajdah): Prostration; specifically the prostration of the first rak'ah that establishes Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum number of men required besides the imam for a valid Jumu'ah?
A) One man
B) Two men
C) Three men
D) Forty men

Key Takeaway
The minimum congregation for Jumu'ah in the Hanafi school is three men besides the imam, who must remain until the prostration of the first rak'ah.

The Condition of General Permission for Jumu'ah
States a condition of Jumu'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of general permission (al-izn al-'aam) for Jumu'ah and apply it to determine the validity of a Friday prayer gathering.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires public access; without general permission, the prayer is invalid.

In the Hanafi school, Jumu'ah has several conditions beyond the usual five daily prayers. This lesson focuses on one: general permission. The idea is that Jumu'ah must be open to the public, not restricted to a select group. Understanding this condition helps avoid invalid gatherings that contradict the spirit of the weekly congregation.

Guided Path
1
State the condition as given in the text
Read the passage: 'al-izn al-'aam' – general permission. This is listed as the sixth condition for Jumu'ah.
2
Explain the meaning of 'general permission'
It means that the general public is allowed to attend without restriction. The gathering must be open to all who wish to pray.
This does not mean that only a large crowd is required; rather, the invitation is public.
3
Relate to other conditions of Jumu'ah
General permission complements other conditions like a town or city and a valid congregation. It ensures Jumu'ah is not a private gathering.
The Hanafi school lists conditions such as the presence of a ruler or his deputy, but this condition relates to public access.
4
Apply the condition to a scenario
Imagine Jumu'ah is held in a private compound with limited entry. Apply the condition: if the public is not allowed, the Jumu'ah is invalid because general permission is absent.
This hypothetical scenario tests understanding.

Source Text

Chapter of Friday. Sound (785): General permission. Translation (785) [6]: General permission should be there. Explanation: For coming to Friday prayer, there should be general permission for the people. If there is general permission, then Friday will be valid. This is the sixth condition.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This is a ruling statement specifying the sixth condition for the validity of Jumu'ah. The condition is that the general public must have permission to attend the Friday prayer. The term 'general permission' (al-izn al-'aam) indicates that the gathering is not restricted or prohibited for the general populace. This condition ensures that Jumu'ah is a public congregation.

Key Terms
الاذن العام (al-izn al-'aam): General permission for the general public to attend Jumu'ah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Condition of Congregation for Jumu'ah: Three Men Besides Imam
States the congregation condition and proofs for Jumu'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah congregation (three men besides imam) and explain the timing requirement (remaining until first prostration) using the provided proofs.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires at least three men besides the imam, who must remain until the first prostration.

In this passage, we learn the essential condition for the Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) according to the Hanafi school. The ruling is not just about the number of participants but also about when they must be present. Understanding this condition helps us appreciate the school's reliance on specific hadith proofs and the rational basis for the timing. We will explore the proofs and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Determine what the passage says about the minimum congregation for Jumu'ah: three men besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. Note that women and children do not count.
2
Examine the timing condition
The three men must remain with the imam until he prostrates in the first rak'ah. If they leave after prostration, Jumu'ah continues; if before, it becomes invalid and Zuhr is prayed.
This timing is derived from the definition of 'catching a rak'ah' in the proofs.
3
Analyze the proofs
Read each proof: (1) hadith of Umm Abdillah al-Dawsiyyah on minimum number, (2) hadith of Abu Hurairah on catching a rak'ah, (3) athar of Ibn Umar, (4) rational reasoning that a rak'ah requires prostration.
Note that all proofs are zanni in transmission (ahad) but sufficient for establishing a wajib condition.
4
Understand the invalidators
If the congregation diminishes below three before the prostration, or if they flee, Jumu'ah is invalid. Even if the imam continues, he must pray Zuhr.
This shows the condition is strict: the congregation must be physically present at the critical moment.
5
Compare with other schools
Contrast the Hanafi position (3 + imam) with the Shafi'i position (40 men). Recognize that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of proofs.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that Jumu'ah is more widely accessible in small communities in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۶)[۷] اور جماعت ہو اور وہ تین مرد ہوں امام کے علاوہ ، اگر چہ غلام ہوں ، یا مسافر ہو، یا بیمار ہوں، اور شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ امام کے ساتھ سجدے تک باقی رہیں۔ پس اگر وہ سجدہ کرنے کے بعد جائیں تو امام اکیلا جمعہ پورا کرے، اور اگر امام کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے بھاگ جائیں تو جمعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح : جمعیت سے مشتق ہے اس لئے کم از کم تین مرد ہوں تو جمعہ قائم ہوگا، چاہے ایسے مرد ہوں جن پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے، مثلا غلام ہوں یا مسافر ہوں یا بیمار ہوں تب بھی جمعہ قائم ہو جائے گا لیکن اگر عورت ہو، یا بچہ ہو تو اس سے جمعہ قائم نہیں ہوگا ، اور یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ جمعہ قائم ہونے تک باقی رہیں، اور جمعہ پہلی رکعت کے سجدہ کرنے سے قائم ہوگا، اس لئے پہلی رکعت کے سجدے تک باقی رہیں تو جمعہ پڑھا جائے گا ، اور اگر اس سے پہلے بھاگ جائیں ، یا تین میں سے ایک کم ہو جائے تو جمعہ کے بجائے ظہر پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن ام عبد الله الدوسية قالت سمعت رسول الله لا يقول الجمعة واجبة على اهل كل قرية وان لم يكونوا الا ثلثة ورابعهم امامهم . (دار قطنی ، باب الجمعۃ علی اہل قریہ ج ثانی ص ۷ نمبر ۱۵۷۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہو کہ امام کے علاوہ تین آدمی ہوں تب جمعہ ہو گا۔ (۲) پہلی رکعت کے سجدہ تک باقی رہیں اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال : أن النبى الله الله قال : اذا ادرك أحدكم الركعتين من يوم الجمعة فقد أدرك الجمعة و اذا ادرك ركعة فليركع اليها أخرى ، و ان لم يدرك ركعة فليصل أربع ركعات (دار قطنی ، باب فیمن یدرک من الجمعة رکعة أولم یدرکھا، ج ثانی، ص ۹ نمبر ۱۵۸۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک رکعت پائے تو جمعہ پڑھے اور اس سے کم پائے تو چار رکعت ظہر پڑھے ۔ (۳) اثر میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ قال عبد الله بن عمر : من ادرك ركعة من الجمعة فليصل اليها أخرى و من لم يدرك الركوع فليصل أربعا - مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من قال اذا ادرک رکعتة من الجمعة صلی الیها آخری، ج اول ص ۴۶۱، نمبر ۵۳۳۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک رکعت یعنی رکوع تک ملے تو جمعہ کی نماز پڑھے، اور اس سے کم ملے تو ظہر کی نماز پڑھے۔ (۴) سجدہ سے پہلے ایک رکعت پوری نہیں ہوتی اور جب تک ایک رکعت نہ ہو تو جمعہ انعقاد نہیں ہوتا اسلئے ایک رکعت یعنی سجدہ تک تین آدمی رہنا ضروری ہے۔ جمعة وان نفروا قبل سجوده بطلت
Translation (786) [7]: And there should be a congregation, and they are three men besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. And the condition is that they remain with the imam until he prostrates. If they leave after his prostration, he completes it alone. If they flee before his prostration, the Jumu'ah becomes invalid. Explanation: It is derived from congregation, so at least three men are needed for Jumu'ah to be established, even if these men are not obligated to attend Jumu'ah, like slaves, travelers, or sick. However, if a woman or child is present, Jumu'ah will not be established. It is also a condition that they remain until Jumu'ah is established. Jumu'ah is established by the prostration of the first rak'ah. So if they remain until the prostration of the first rak'ah, Jumu'ah is prayed. If they flee before that, or one of the three diminishes, then he prays Zuhr instead. Proof: (1) In this hadith: From Umm Abdillah al-Dawsiyyah: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of every town, even if there are only three, and the fourth is their imam.' (Dar Qutni, Bab al-Jumu'ah 'ala Ahl al-Qaryah, vol.2, p.7, no.1578) This hadith shows that with three men besides the imam, Jumu'ah is valid. (2) For remaining until the prostration of the first rak'ah, there is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah: The Prophet said: 'If one of you catches two rak'ahs of Friday, he has caught Jumu'ah. If he catches one rak'ah, he should add another. If he does not catch a rak'ah, he should pray four rak'ahs.' (Dar Qutni, Bab fi man yudrik min al-Jumu'ah rak'atan aw lam yudrikha, vol.2, p.9, no.1586) This hadith indicates that if one catches a rak'ah, he prays Jumu'ah; if less, he prays four Zuhr. (3) This is proven by an athar: Abdullah ibn Umar said: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Jumu'ah, let him add another. Whoever does not catch the bowing, let him pray four.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab man qala idha adraka rak'atan min al-Jumu'ah salla ilayha ukhra, vol.1, p.461, no.5332) This athar shows that if one catches one rak'ah, i.e., until the bowing, he prays Jumu'ah; if less, he prays Zuhr. (4) Before prostration, a rak'ah is not complete, and as long as one rak'ah is not performed, Jumu'ah is not established. Therefore, it is necessary that three men remain until the prostration of the first rak'ah. If they flee before his prostration, it is invalid.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proofs regarding the condition of congregation for Jumu'ah. The ruling states that Jumu'ah requires at least three men besides the imam, regardless of whether they are slaves, travelers, or sick. The key condition is that these three must remain with the imam until he performs the prostration of the first rak'ah. If they leave after the prostration, the imam can complete Jumu'ah alone; if they leave before, Jumu'ah becomes invalid and must be prayed as Zuhr. The passage provides four proofs: (1) A hadith from Umm Abdillah al-Dawsiyyah stating that Jumu'ah is obligatory on a town's people even if only three, with the fourth being the imam. (2) A hadith from Abu Hurairah defining catching Jumu'ah by catching at least one rak'ah. (3) An athar from Ibn Umar with similar meaning. (4) A rational explanation that a rak'ah is not complete without prostration, so the congregation must be present until that point. The commentary emphasizes that women and children do not count for this condition, and that the three men need not be obligated to attend Jumu'ah themselves.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregation – here refers to the group of men (at least three) beside the imam for Jumu'ah
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer
سجدة (sajdah): Prostration – the point after which Jumu'ah is considered established if congregation remains

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is valid with three men besides the imam who remain until the first prostration; otherwise, Zuhr must be prayed.

Condition for Valid Jumu'ah: Three Men Required
Ruling on Jumu'ah validity with woman or child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Jumu'ah requires three adult men and identify when a woman or child invalidates the congregation.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah needs three adult men; a woman or child does not count.

This lesson clarifies a key condition for Jumu'ah: the congregation must include at least three adult men. If only two men are present along with a woman or child, the Friday prayer is not valid and must be prayed as Zuhr. This ruling is based on the requirement derived from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Validity Condition
First, recognize that the act under discussion is Jumu'ah (Friday congregational prayer). The ruling concerns its validity (sihhah).
2
Note the Requirement of Three Men
The text states that three men must be present. This is a condition for Jumu'ah to be valid. If only two men attend along with a woman or child, the condition is not met.
The three men include the imam? According to this text, 'three men' likely means total adult males in the congregation (including imam).
3
Understand Why Women and Children Do Not Count
Women and minors (children who have not reached puberty) are not considered fulfilling this condition. Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them, and they do not satisfy the requirement for the congregation.
In Hanafi fiqh, a child (sabi) does not count for Jumu'ah congregation.
4
Consequence: Must Pray Zuhr
When Jumu'ah is invalid, the obligation of the Friday prayer is not fulfilled. The attendees must pray the Zuhr prayer instead (either individually or in congregation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

But if with two men there is a woman or a child, then Jumu'ah is not valid, because according to the hadith, there are not three men, and Jumu'ah is not established by a woman or a child.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This is a ruling statement clarifying that Jumu'ah is not valid if the congregation consists of two men and either a woman or a child. The condition of three men is strict; women and children do not fulfill the requirement. The explanation references the earlier hadith that requires three men besides the imam.

Permissibility of Slave and Sick Leading Jumu'ah
States permissibility for slave/sick to lead Jumu'ah with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a slave or sick person may lead Jumu'ah and explain the Hanafi reasoning that upon attendance it becomes a personal obligation (fard ada').

Core Idea
Even those exempted from Jumu'ah can lead it once they attend — attendance transforms it into a personal duty.

This passage answers a practical question: if Jumu'ah is not originally obligatory on a slave or sick person, can they still lead the prayer? The Hanafi school says yes, but the reasoning is nuanced. It hinges on the concept of 'fard ada'' — once they attend, the obligation becomes actual, and anyone for whom the obligation is actual can lead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states clearly that a slave and a sick person are permitted to lead Jumu'ah. Note that the ruling is permissibility (ja'iz), not obligation.
2
Understand the initial exemption
Jumu'ah is not obligatory on a slave or sick person originally due to hardship (haraj). But the key point is that they are still men and capable of performing the prayer.
3
Analyze the effect of attendance
When they attend Jumu'ah voluntarily, it becomes fard ada' (obligatory performance) on them. This means the obligation to perform Jumu'ah in that specific time becomes binding on them personally.
This is distinct from fard qada' (make-up).
4
Apply the principle of leadership
The general rule is that anyone for whom Jumu'ah is valid (including those with fard ada') may lead it. Since the slave and sick person now have fard ada', they qualify to lead.
The same reasoning applies to a traveler.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۸۸) اور غلام اور بیمار کو جمعہ کی امامت کرنا جائز ہے۔ تشریح : غلام اور بیمار پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے لیکن یہ مرد ہیں اس لئے یہ جمعہ قائم کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتے ہیں ، اس لئے یہ دونوں جمعہ کی نماز کی امامت کرنا چاہیں تو کر سکتے ۔ وجه : مسافر، مریض، اور غلام کی امامت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان لوگوں پر جمعہ واجب اسلئے نہیں ہے کہ انکو آنے میں حرج ہوگا، لیکن جب آہی گئے تو جمعہ فرض اداء ہو جائے گا ، اور جب فرض اداء ہو جائے گا تو امامت بھی کر سکتا ہے۔
Translation (788): And it is permissible for a slave and a sick person to lead Jumu'ah. Explanation: Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon a slave or sick person, but they are men, so if they wish to establish Jumu'ah, they can. Therefore, both of them can lead Jumu'ah if they wish. Proof: The evidence for the leadership of a traveler, sick person, and slave is that Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon them because there would be hardship in attending. But when they do attend, Jumu'ah becomes an obligatory performance (fard ada'), and when it becomes a fard ada', they can lead.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage rules that a slave or a sick person may lead Jumu'ah, even though Jumu'ah is not originally obligatory upon them due to their status. The reasoning (wajh) is that once they attend, the obligation of Jumu'ah becomes due upon them personally (fard ada'), and anyone for whom Jumu'ah is valid to pray can lead it. The same applies to a traveler. The proof is based on the absence of hardship (haraj) once they are present.

Key Terms
العبد (al-'abd): Slave – a person in servitude who is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah
المريض (al-marid): Sick person – one who is ill and exempted from Jumu'ah obligation
فرض اداء (fard ada'): Obligatory performance – the duty that becomes actual upon attendance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a slave lead Jumu'ah according to the text?
A) Because Jumu'ah is obligatory on him
B) Because he is a man and once he attends, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory for him
C) Because he has permission from his master
D) Because he is free from sin

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a slave or sick person may lead Jumu'ah if they attend because attendance transforms Jumu'ah into a personal duty (fard ada').

Defining the City (Misr) for Jumu'ah – Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of a city for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a city (misr) for Jumu'ah and distinguish it from the view of Sahibayn, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
For Jumu'ah, a city is defined by legal institutions, not population size.

The validity of Jumu'ah depends on it being held in a 'misr' (city). But what exactly constitutes a city? The Hanafi school has an internal difference. This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's definition, supported by traditions, and contrasts it with the view of his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn). Understanding this dispute helps you see how conditions and definitions can affect the obligation of Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The issue is the definition of a city (misr) for the validity of Jumu'ah. Without meeting the definition, Jumu'ah cannot be held.
2
State Abu Hanifa's definition
According to Abu Hanifa (in the zahir al-riwayah), a city must have a mufti, an amir, and a qadi who enforce Islamic laws and hadd penalties, and its structures must be permanent like those of Mina (not tents).
The passage also mentions that Mina had about ten stone houses at that time, indicating permanence.
3
Examine the proofs
Abu Hanifa cites two athar: (1) The saying of 'Ali that there is no Jumu'ah except in a comprehensive city (misr jami'), and he counted Basra, Kufa, Madinah, and Bahrain as such. (2) The statement of 'Ata defining a comprehensive town as having an amir, qisas (penal enforcement), and adjoining houses.
These proof texts are from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Compare with Sahibayn's definition
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) define a city by the capacity of its mosque: if all worshippers gather and fill the mosque, it is a city. Their proof is not fully quoted in this passage.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both views are valid but one is preferred.
5
Determine the practical consequence and relied-upon view
The thamarah al-khilaf: A town with permanent buildings but no qadi or mufti may qualify as a city according to Sahibayn (if the mosque is large enough) but not according to Abu Hanifa. The passage indicates that Abu Hanifa's view is in the apparent riwayah, making it the mufta bihi (operative position).
This affects where Muslims must perform Jumu'ah; in such towns, Hanafis following the relied-upon view should pray Zuhr instead.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage defines the condition of a 'city' (misr) for Jumu'ah to be valid. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of misr for Jumu'ah. The text is cut off but the dispute is clear.

The Minimum Number for Jumu'ah: Women and Children Do Not Count
Ruling on the invalidity of Jumu'ah with insufficient men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for a valid Jumu'ah congregation and explain why a woman or child does not fulfill that condition.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires three adult men; a woman or child does not count toward this minimum.

This passage establishes a key condition for the validity of the Friday congregational prayer. While many know that Jumu'ah requires a gathering, the Hanafi school specifies that only adult men are counted towards the minimum. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under consideration is the Jumu'ah (Friday) prayer. The ruling given is that it is invalid (batil) when the congregation consists of two men and one woman or one male child.
2
Locate the condition for validity
The implicit condition is that Jumu'ah requires at least three adult men. The text states explicitly that with two men and a woman/child it is not valid, establishing the three-man minimum.
3
Understand who qualifies as 'men'
Women and prepubescent children (sabi) do not fulfill the requirement. Their presence does not make up for a missing adult male. The hadith basis for this ruling is that Jumu'ah is established only by adult males.
The hadith is known in Hanafi sources: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon every three men who are residents.'
4
Contrast with other schools
Unlike the Hanafi requirement of three men, the Shafi'i school requires forty men. This shows the range of scholarly interpretation on the same evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تصح بامرأة او صبى مع رجلين ترجمه : (۷۸۷) اور جمعہ صحیح نہیں ہے جب دومرد کے ساتھ عورت ہو یا بچہ ہو۔ تشریح : تینوں مرد ہونا چاہئے لیکن اگر دو مرد کے ساتھ ایک عورت ہو یا ایک بچہ ہو تو جمعہ مسیح نہیں ہے، کیونکہ حدیث کے مطابق تین مرد نہیں ہوئے ، اور عورت یا بچہ سے جمعہ قائم نہیں ہوتا۔
And it is not valid with a woman or a male child along with two men. Translation: (787) And Jumu'ah is not valid when there is a woman or a child with two men. Explanation: There must be three men. But if there are two men with a woman or a child, then Jumu'ah is not valid, because according to hadith there are not three men, and Jumu'ah cannot be established by a woman or a child.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the validity of Jumu'ah. The author states that Jumu'ah is not valid if the congregation consists of two men and one woman or one male child. The explanation clarifies that at least three men are required. A woman or a child (who has not reached puberty) does not count towards this minimum. The proof is based on the hadith that Jumu'ah requires three men. This ruling emphasizes that only adult men are considered for the validity of the Jumu'ah prayer.

Key Terms
جمعة (jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer
صبی (sabi): A male child who has not reached puberty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Three men; women and children do not count
C) Forty men
D) One imam and any number of people

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is invalid if fewer than three adult men are present; women and children do not count towards this minimum.

Permissibility of Slave and Sick Person Leading Jumu'ah
Ruling on slave and sick person leading Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a slave or sick person may lead Jumu'ah and explain the istihsan-based proof.

Core Idea
A slave or sick person may lead Jumu'ah upon attendance, as Jumu'ah then becomes obligatory for them.

This passage examines a nuanced ruling: individuals who are not originally obligated to attend Jumu'ah—such as a slave or a sick person—may nevertheless lead the prayer if they do attend. The key lies in the principle that attendance transforms the obligation, and istihsan (juristic preference) overrides the general rule that only those obligated may lead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (leading Jumu'ah) and the hukm level (permissible, not obligatory).
The act is leading Jumu'ah prayer, and the ruling is jā'iz (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is istihsan, based on the principle that Jumu'ah becomes obligatory upon those who attend, even if they were excused initially.
No specific Quran or hadith is quoted; the reasoning is rational (dalīl 'aqlī).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil supports the ruling: since attending makes Jumu'ah fard for the slave or sick person, they are then qualified to lead as any other obligated male.
The link is that obligation (wujūb) upon attendance establishes the capacity to lead.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school requires the imam to be free and not a slave, even if he attends. This passage implicitly contrasts that view.
The Hanafi position is more flexible, relying on istihsan.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (muftā bihī) in the school, and the reasoning is considered sound despite the Shafi'i objection.
No explicit tarjih is given in the passage, but it is part of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاز للعبد والمريض ان يؤم فيها ترجمه : (۷۸۸) اور غلام اور بیمار کو جمعہ کی امامت کرنا جائز ہے۔ تشریح : غلام اور بیمار پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے لیکن یہ مرد ہیں اس لئے یہ جمعہ قائم کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتے ہیں ، اس لئے یہ دونوں جمعہ کی نماز کی امامت کرنا چاہیں تو کر سکتے ۔ وجه : مسافر، مریض، اور غلام کی امامت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان لوگوں پر جمعہ واجب اسلئے نہیں ہے کہ انکو آنے میں حرج ہوگا، لیکن جب آہی گئے تو جمعہ فرض اداء ہو جائے گا ، اور جب فرض اداء ہو جائے گا تو امامت بھی کر سکتا ہے۔
And it is permissible for a slave and a sick person to lead in it. Translation: (788) And it is permissible for a slave and a sick person to lead the Jumu'ah prayer. Explanation: Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon a slave and a sick person, but they are men, so if they wish, they can establish Jumu'ah. Therefore, both of them can lead the Jumu'ah prayer if they so desire. Reasoning: The proof for the permissibility of a traveler, a sick person, and a slave leading Jumu'ah is that Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon them because coming to it would cause difficulty, but if they do come, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory upon them, and if it becomes obligatory, they can lead.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of certain individuals leading Jumu'ah prayer who are not themselves obligated to attend it. The ruling is that a slave and a sick person may lead Jumu'ah, even though Jumu'ah is not originally wajib upon them due to their circumstances (slavery or illness). However, if they attend the prayer, it becomes obligatory for them, and they are qualified to lead because they are men. The reasoning is based on istihsan: since they are men and Jumu'ah becomes obligatory upon them upon attendance, they can lead. This shows that the permissibility of leading is not contingent upon being obligated initially.

Key Terms
عبد ('abd): A male slave
امامت (imamah): Leading the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because they are excused
C) Yes, but only if they are healthy
D) No, because they cannot attend

Key Takeaway
A slave or sick person may lead Jumu'ah upon attendance, as attendance makes Jumu'ah obligatory for them and qualifies them to lead.

Definition of a City for Jumu'ah: Imam vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on definition of a city for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the definitions of a city for Jumu'ah between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to determine where Jumu'ah is valid.

Core Idea
A city for Jumu'ah: Abu Hanifa requires authorities and permanent buildings; Sahibayn require only a mosque that holds all residents.

Jumu'ah prayer is only valid in a 'city' (misr), but what defines a city? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa's definition in the zahir al-riwayah versus the more lenient definition of his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for determining where Jumu'ah can be established in practice.

Guided Path
1
State Imam Abu Hanifa's definition
From the passage, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) defines a city as having a mufti, an amir, and a qadi who execute judgments and establish hudud, and whose buildings are permanent like those of Mina.
This view relies on a hadith of Ali (RA) and a statement of Ata'.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's definition
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) define a city based on the capacity of its mosque: when all residents gather, the mosque must be able to hold them. They do not require separate authorities.
Their proof is the statement of Umar ibn Dinar.
3
Examine the proofs cited
List the dalils: Imam Abu Hanifa cites a hadith from Ali (RA) that Jumu'ah is only in a comprehensive city, and Ata' describing a comprehensive village. The Sahibayn cite Umar ibn Dinar that if the mosque accommodates all, Jumu'ah is valid.
Both are naqli (textual) proofs from sahaba and tabi'un.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage concludes that today Hanafis follow the Sahibayn definition. This means Jumu'ah can be performed in a village if the mosque holds all residents, even without a mufti, amir, and qadi.
The fatwa authority is the later practice (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

(مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القرى الصغارج ثالث ص اے نمبر ۵۱۹۳ ) ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بڑی بستی اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں امیر ہو ، قصاص اور حدود نافذ کئے جاتے ہوں اور گھر قریب قریب ہوں، خیمہ زنوں کی طرح دور دور گھر نہ ہوں۔ (۳) لیکن صاحبین کے یہاں شہر کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ شہر کی مسجد سب نمازی جمع ہو جائیں تو مسجد بھر جائے اس کو شہر کہتے ہیں ، اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ سمعت عمر بن دينار يقول اذا كان المسجد يجمع فيه الصلوة فلتصل فيه الجمعة( مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب القرى الصغار، ج ثالث ، ص ،اے نمبر ۵۱۹۸) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر تمام آدمی جمع ہو کر ایک مسجد میں نماز پڑھتے ہوں تو اس میں جمعہ جائز ہے۔ آج کل حنفیہ کے یہاں اسی تعریف کو مانتے ہیں اور اسی کی بنیاد پر دیہات میں جمعہ کی نماز پڑھتے ہیں۔
And a city is every place that has a mufti, an amir, and a qadi who executes judgments and establishes hudud, and its buildings reach the level of Mina in the apparent narration. Translation: (789) A city is every place where there is a mufti, an amir, and a qadi who implements rulings and establishes hudud, and its urban development is like that of Mina, according to the apparent narration. Explanation: They are defining the city: where there is a mufti, a qadi, and an amir, and they implement rulings and establish hudud, and the city's buildings are like those of Mina - that is a city where Jumu'ah can be established. In that time, Mina had ten houses. Meaning, they are not like tent-dwellers but rather permanent residents with mud and stone houses. So Jumu'ah is permissible there. Proof: (1) The saying of the companion (Ali): 'There is no Jumu'ah and no Takbir al-Tashriq except in a comprehensive city.' He counted the cities as Basra, Kufa, Medina, and Bahrain. (2) For the condition of amir and qadi, there is the saying of the tabi'i (Ata'): 'I asked Ata': What is the comprehensive village? He said: A place with a congregation, an amir, retaliation, and houses that are clustered together, not scattered, one attached to another like the structure of Jeddah.' (3) But according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the definition of a city is that when all the worshippers gather in the mosque of that city, the mosque is filled. For this, there is the saying of the tabi'i (Ibn Dinar): 'I heard Umar ibn Dinar say: If the mosque accommodates all the people for prayer, then perform Jumu'ah in it.' From this, it is understood that if all people gather in one mosque, then Jumu'ah is valid there. Today, the Hanafis follow this definition and on its basis they perform Jumu'ah in villages.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi definition of a city for the purpose of establishing Jumu'ah. The primary view (from Imam Abu Hanifa in zahir al-riwayah) requires the presence of a mufti, amir, and qadi, and that the settlement is permanent like Mina. It also cites the view of Sahibayn that the definition is based on the capacity of the mosque to hold all residents. The passage then notes that contemporary Hanafis follow the Sahibayn's definition, which is more lenient, allowing Jumu'ah in villages if the mosque can accommodate all. This is an important intra-Hanafi dispute with practical consequences.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or large town where Jumu'ah is valid
صاحبين (sahibayn): Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi definition of a city for Jumu'ah?
A) A city must have a mufti, amir, and qadi.
B) A city must have permanent buildings like Mina.
C) A city's mosque must be able to hold all residents.
D) A city must be a provincial capital.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position defines a city for Jumu'ah by the capacity of its mosque to hold all residents, not by the presence of authorities or permanent buildings.

Combining Roles of Qadi/Amir and Mufti for Jumu'ah
Ruling on sufficiency of qadi or amir being mufti for city definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining the roles of qadi/amir and mufti for the validity of Jumu'ah in a city.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the conditions for a city in Jumu'ah are satisfied if the qadi or amir is himself a mufti.

The requirement for a valid Jumu'ah includes that it be held in a city, which is defined by the presence of certain officials. This passage resolves a practical question: must a mufti be a separate person from the qadi or amir? The Hanafi school allows combination, simplifying the condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for a city
Recognize that for Jumu'ah to be valid, the prayer must be held in a city, which is defined by the presence of a qadi (judge) or amir (ruler) and a mufti (jurisconsult).
These are conditions (shurut), not pillars.
2
Understand the potential requirement of distinct persons
Some might assume each role must be held by a different individual. The passage addresses whether the mufti must be separate.
3
Apply the ruling of combination
If the qadi or amir is also qualified as a mufti, then the condition of having a mufti is fulfilled, and no separate person is needed.
The Arabic word 'او' (or) indicates sufficiency of either.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا كان القاضي او الامير مفتيا اغني عن التعداد ترجمه : (۷۹۰) اور جب خود قاضی یا امیر مفتی ہو تو دوسرے مفتی کی ضرورت نہیں۔ تشریح : قاضی یا امیر مفتی نہ ہو تو شہر ہونے کے لئے ایک مفتی کی بھی ضرورت ہے، لیکن اگر خود مفتی بھی ہو تو ایک قاضی ہونا، یا ایک امیر ہونا شہر ہونے کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اب الگ سے مفتی کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔

Explanation: If the qadi or amir is not a mufti, then for a place to be a city, a mufti is also required. But if he himself is a mufti, then having just one qadi or one amir is sufficient for the city definition; there is no need for a separate mufti.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This short passage clarifies a nuance in the definition of a city as it pertains to Jumu'ah. The requirement for a city includes a mufti, amir, and qadi. However, if the qadi or the amir himself is qualified as a mufti, then the positions can be combined, and the condition of having a mufti is satisfied without needing a separate individual. This is a practical application showing that the conditions are about functions, not necessarily distinct persons.

Key Terms
مفتی (mufti): A scholar qualified to issue fatwas
تعداد (ta'dad): Counting or needing a separate person

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The amir must also be a mufti

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the functions of qadi/amir and mufti can be combined; the condition for a city is satisfied if the qadi or amir is a mufti.

Validity of Jumu'ah in Mina During Hajj
Ruling with two proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Jumu'ah in Mina during Hajj and explain the two proofs that establish its validity.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is valid in Mina because it is a city (or fina' of Makkah) during Hajj.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: holding Jumu'ah in Mina during the Hajj season. While Mina is normally a valley, during Hajj it becomes a bustling city with shops and authorities. The Hanafi school provides two independent proofs for the validity of Jumu'ah there, grounded in urban character and the Quranic indication that Mina is part of Makkah's precincts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is holding Jumu'ah in Mina during the Hajj season. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) and valid (sahih).
The passage specifies this is for the caliph or amir of Hijaz, but the principle applies generally.
2
Analyze the first proof: urban character
The passage argues that Mina has permanent buildings (makanat bani hue) and during Hajj it becomes like a full city with shops and officials. Since Jumu'ah is valid in a city, it is valid in Mina.
This is a qiyas: Mina during Hajj is analogous to a settled city.
3
Analyze the second proof: fina' of Makkah
The Quranic verse (5:95) commands that the hady 'reach the Ka'bah,' but it is slaughtered in Mina. This indicates that Mina is within the fina' (precincts) of Makkah. Jumu'ah is valid in the fina' of a city, so it is valid in Mina.
The dalil is the Quran, and the wajh al-dalalah is that the verse treats Mina as effectively part of Makkah.
4
Note the historical context and current status
The passage adds a note that nowadays Mina has become a full part of Makkah, so there is no dispute. This confirms the ruling's continued applicability.
The ikhtilaf was only theoretical; in practice, the Hanafi position is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And Jumu'ah in Mina during the season is permissible for the caliph or the amir of Hijaz. Translation: (791) And it is valid for the caliph or the amir of Hijaz to establish Jumu'ah in Mina during the Hajj season. Reasoning: There are two reasons for the permissibility of Jumu'ah in Mina: [1] Mina has permanent houses, not like a desert, and during Hajj it becomes like a full city with shops, and qadis and amirs gather. Since Jumu'ah is valid in a city, it is valid in Mina. [2] Mina is within the precinct (fina') of Makkah, as indicated by the verse 'and the hady reach the Ka'bah' (5:95) whereas the hady is actually slaughtered in Mina. This shows that Mina is in the fina' of Makkah, and Jumu'ah is valid in the fina' of a city. Note: Nowadays, Mina has so many buildings that it has become a full city and has been included within the boundaries of Makkah, so Jumu'ah there is valid without dispute.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of holding Jumu'ah in Mina specifically during Hajj. The author provides two reasons. First, Mina itself has permanent buildings, and during Hajj it has all the features of a city. Second, Mina is considered part of the greater Makkah area (fina'), supported by the Quranic verse that treats the hady as reaching the Ka'bah even though it is slaughtered in Mina. The note adds that in present times, Mina has become a part of Makkah, so there is no disagreement.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The immediate vicinity or precinct of a city, including its suburbs and surrounding areas where services are integrated.
موسم (mawsim): The Hajj season, a specific time when Mina is populated.

D) Mina has no buildings

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates Jumu'ah in Mina during Hajj due to its urban character and its inclusion in the fina' of Makkah.

The Validity of a Minimal Jumu'ah Khutbah: A Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on minimal khutbah content in Jumu'ah with proof from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a minimal khutbah (tasbih or tahmid) and identify the Quranic proof (wajh al-dalalah) that supports it, including the reason for karahah and the Shafi'i counterposition.

Core Idea
A Jumu'ah khutbah is valid with even a single dhikr, though it is makruh to abandon the sunnah.

This lesson examines the minimum requirement for the Jumu'ah khutbah according to the Hanafi school. You will learn that the Quranic command to 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (dhikr) is general, so any form of dhikr, even saying 'Subhan Allah' once, fulfills the obligation. However, doing so is considered makruh because it contradicts the established sunnah of a more elaborate sermon. The lesson also highlights the difference with the Shafi'i school, which requires specific content.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the Jumu'ah khutbah. The ruling is that even if the imam restricts the khutbah to a single utterance like 'Subhan Allah' or 'Alhamdulillah', the khutbah is valid (sahih) but it is makruh (disliked).
Note that the khutbah is wajib, but its content requirement is minimal.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 62:9: 'O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on Friday, hurry to the remembrance of Allah (dhikr Allah) and leave off trade.' The word 'dhikr' is the proof.
The verse commands hastening to 'dhikr Allah', which is interpreted as the khutbah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi school argues that 'dhikr' is a general (amm) term that includes any form of remembrance, not a specific form. Since the verse does not specify a particular wording, any dhikr suffices to fulfill the command.
This is based on the usul principle that al-amm yufidu al-wujub and remains on its generality unless there is evidence to restrict it.
4
Note the karahah and its reason
The ruling of karahah (dislike) is attached because the Prophet ﷺ and the early Muslims would deliver longer khutbahs containing praise, exhortation, and dua. Reducing it to a single dhikr neglects the sunnah, hence it is makruh tanzih.
Karahah does not affect validity; it indicates the preferred practice is otherwise.
5
Compare with Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school disagrees: they hold that the khutbah must contain specific elements such as praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and exhorting the congregation. They interpret 'dhikr' in the verse as referring to the khutbah with those specific components. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul methodologies.
The practical difference (thamarah) is that a minimal khutbah would be invalid in the Shafi'i school, while valid (but makruh) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح الاقتصار في الخطبة على نحو تسبيحة او تحميدة مع الكراهة ترجمه : (۷۹۲) اور خطبہ میں اکتفا کرنا صحیح ہے صرف سبحان اللہ یا الحمدللہ پر کراہیت کے ساتھ۔ تشریح : یوں تو خطبہ میں اللہ کا ذکر اور نصیحت ہونی چاہئے اور دو خطبے ہونے چاہئے لیکن صرف سبحان اللہ کہا، یا صرف صرف الحمد للہ، کہا تب بھی خطبہ ادا ہو جائے گا اور جمعہ پڑھنا جائز ہوگا، البتہ ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیث کے خلاف کیا۔ وجه : (۱) اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں خطبہ کو ذکر فرمایا ہے، جسکا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ صرف ذکر سے خطبہ اداء ہو جائے گا۔ آیت یہ ہے ياايها الذين آمنوا اذا نودي للصلوة من يوم الجمعة فاسعوا الى ذكر الله وذروا البيع (آیت9،سورة الجمعة
And it is valid to restrict the khutbah to something like saying 'Subhan Allah' or 'Alhamdulillah', albeit with karahah. Translation: (792) And it is correct to suffice with only saying 'Subhan Allah' or 'Alhamdulillah' in the khutbah, though it is makruh. Explanation: Ideally, the khutbah should contain the remembrance of Allah and exhortation, and there should be two khutbahs. However, if one only says 'Subhan Allah' or 'Alhamdulillah', the khutbah is still fulfilled and Jumu'ah is valid, but doing so is makruh because it goes against the sunnah. Reasoning: The Quran calls the khutbah 'dhikr' (remembrance), so any remembrance suffices. The verse is 'O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on Friday, hurry to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade' (Surah al-Jumu'ah, verse 9).
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum requirement for the Jumu'ah khutbah. The author states that even if the khutbah consists of just saying 'Subhan Allah' or 'Alhamdulillah', the khutbah is valid and Jumu'ah is valid, but it is makruh (disliked) because it deviates from the sunnah of having a lengthy khutbah with admonition. The proof is the Quranic word 'dhikr', which linguistically includes any form of remembrance. This shows that the requirement is the act of dhikr, not a specific length or content. The karahah indicates that while the ruling is valid, it is against the preferred practice.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before Jumu'ah prayer
تسبيحة (tasbihah): Saying 'Subhan Allah' (Glory be to Allah)
تحميدة (tahmidah): Saying 'Alhamdulillah' (Praise be to Allah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is valid and recommended

Key Takeaway
A single tasbih or tahmid in the Jumu'ah khutbah fulfills the wajib, but it is makruh because it abandons the sunnah.

No Need for Separate Mufti if Ruler is Mufti
Ruling on sufficiency of a mufti-ruler for Jumu'ah condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah regarding the presence of a mufti, and explain when a single ruler-mufti suffices.

Core Idea
If the ruler is a mufti, no separate mufti is needed for Jumu'ah.

The Hanafi school sets specific conditions for a settlement to hold Jumu'ah prayer. One of these conditions is the presence of a mufti—a qualified jurist who can issue fatwas. But what if the ruler (qadi or amir) himself is a mufti? This lesson clarifies that the ruler-mufti fulfills both roles, eliminating the need for a separate mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the condition for a settlement to be considered a city for Jumu'ah. The ruling is that if the qadi or amir is a mufti, no separate mufti is needed.
2
Locate the dalil
The matn (text) states this ruling in the context of Zahir al-Riwayah, indicating it is from the authoritative Hanafi corpus.
The phrase 'fi zahir al-riwayah' signals this is the relied-upon transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal implication (wajh al-dalalah) is that the presence of a mufti is a required condition, but a qadi or amir who is a mufti fulfills that condition by virtue of his role.
The ruling combines two requirements into one person.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not require a mufti at all; any settlement with 40 permanent residents suffices. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The difference stems from the definition of a 'city' for Jumu'ah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is as stated in the matn: a ruler-mufti suffices. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجمعة الـحـدود وبـلـغـت ابـنـيـتـه مـنـي في ظاهر الرواية . (۷۹۰) واذا كان القاضي او الامير مفتيا اغني عن التعداد . (۷۹۱) وجازت الجمعة بمنى فى الموسم للخليفة او امير الحجاز. (۷۹۲) وصح الاقتصار في الخطبة على نحو تسبيحة او تحميدة مع الكراهة. تابعی ہے۔ سمعت عمر بن دينار يقول اذا كان المسجد يجمع فيه الصلوة فلتصل فيه الجمعة( مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب القرى الصغار، ج ثالث ، ص ،اے نمبر ۵۱۹۸) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر تمام آدمی جمع ہو کر ایک مسجد میں نماز پڑھتے ہوں تو اس میں جمعہ جائز ہے۔ آج کل حنفیہ کے یہاں اسی تعریف کو مانتے ہیں اور اسی کی بنیاد پر دیہات میں جمعہ کی نماز پڑھتے ہیں۔ ترجمه : (۷۹۰) اور جب خود قاضی یا امیر مفتی ہو تو دوسرے مفتی کی ضرورت نہیں۔ تشریح : قاضی یا امیر مفتی نہ ہو تو شہر ہونے کے لئے ایک مفتی کی بھی ضرورت ہے، لیکن اگر خود مفتی بھی ہو تو ایک قاضی ہونا، یا ایک امیر ہونا شہر ہونے کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اب الگ سے مفتی کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of Friday. The limits and it reached that it is built from me in Zahir al-Riwayah. (790) And when the judge or the amir is a mufti, it suffices without (the need for) another. (791) And the Friday prayer is permissible in Mina during the season for the caliph or the amir of Hijaz. (792) And it is valid to limit the sermon to something like a tasbih or a tahmid, although with dislike. A follower: I heard 'Umar ibn Dinar say: If the mosque is one where the prayer is gathered, then pray the Friday prayer in it (Mannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qura al-Sighar, vol. 3, p. ay, no. 5198). From this it is known that if all people gather in one mosque and pray, then Friday is permissible in it. Today among the Hanafis, this definition is accepted and on its basis they pray Friday in villages. Translation: (790) And when the qadi or amir himself is a mufti, then there is no need for another mufti. Explanation: If the qadi or amir is not a mufti, then for (a place to be considered) a city, one mufti is also necessary. But if he himself is a mufti, then having one qadi or one amir is sufficient for being a city. Now there is no need for a separate mufti.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation about the condition for a city to hold Jumu'ah prayer according to the Hanafi school. The original matn (numbers 790-792) lists three rulings. The commentary focuses on (790): If the ruler (qadi or amir) is himself a mufti (a jurist capable of issuing fatwas), then this suffices to meet the requirement of having a mufti for the city, and no separate mufti is needed. The explanation clarifies that for a place to be considered a city for Jumu'ah, it requires either a qadi, an amir, or a mufti. If the ruler is a mufti, that single person fulfills both roles. The preceding Urdu lines (from 'tabi' hai' to 'parhte hain') are an additional proof from a hadith transmitted by 'Umar ibn Dinar stating that a mosque where people gather for prayer suffices for Jumu'ah, and the Hanafis apply this to villages. This is not directly part of the ruling (790) but is included in the chapter's introduction.

Key Terms
قاضي (qadi): A judge appointed by the ruler to decide disputes.
أمير (amir): A governor or ruler with executive authority.
مفتي (mufti): A jurist qualified to issue fatwas.
